O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, dear sons, I have completed this book for you which contains the principles and practice of the medical science, and have ended it with explanations and clarifications.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the practical application of medical knowledge is lacking in our region and has been completely abandoned by all, the science has perished and disappeared, leaving only the small written descriptions in books from ancient times that have been handled by the hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And it is due to this lack of practical application that errors and falsehoods have arisen, knowledge and understanding have been clouded, and the scientific field has been neglected.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I wish to gather together the organization of this treatise following the order of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will gather together the forms of the fire-making tools for cautery, and the other instruments of the work with the addition of explanation and preparation as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled craftsmen of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has been abandoned.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who practices it to master the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that they may know precisely the members and their forms, and their connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones, nerves, veins, and arteries, and the number thereof, and their movement and repose, and where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And so Hippocrates says that a name without the deed is much, and with the deed is little; and the same goes for the art of handicraft.[Note: "art of hand" is a possible interpretation of "l'art de main"]
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the previously mentioned things should be cautious not to fall into error and not to kill men; as I have seen many times with those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who lanced an abscess of scrofula in a woman's neck and cut the arteries in her neck, causing so much blood to flow out that the woman died in his arms.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another doctor who treated a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large. He brought with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew that if he were operated on, he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see one other physician who took in charge a duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the break there was a wound; and the ignorant physician tightly binds the break over the wound with splints, and did not leave any bandage at the wound, and he left it like this for a while; and he commanded him not to loosen it; and it remained so until the leg became entirely swollen and the foot came to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and unbind the leg; and when I had undone it, he was well and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But still the corruption (gangrene) had already set in the member (leg), and I could not heal it; and the corruption continued to spread throughout the member until the member was entirely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see one other physician who lanced a hardened abscess and then inflamed it through the malice of his handling.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron if it cannot entirely remove what is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two branches: namely, surgery where there is danger in many situations; and I will point out in each place in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore, it is necessary for you to be careful so that foolish fools cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	So take up your weapons in cotton (?), and undertake your patients lightly and resolutely, and use the best approach so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are praised; and leave behind fearsome diseases with serious health consequences; and put aside your weapons from what makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other world of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen says in one of his teachings: «Do not treat serious illness if you do not want to be called a foolish doctor.»
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter deals with fire cauteries and medical cauteries, and is organized from head to toe; it covers the shapes of instruments, cautery irons, and everything necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, cupping glasses, wounds, the extraction of arrows, and similar things, and it includes descriptions of the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is arranged according to the joints from head to feet, and the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, so that we remember the work, it is appropriate that I speak of the quality and harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of help and harm is a lengthy and subtle science and secret knowledge; and about this, many wise people have spoken and agreed; but their words satisfy me little because I dread their length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the cautery helps universally in every complexion where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, the hot complexion without matter and the dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a hot and dry temperament, some have divided and said that cautery is of great help; and the others said the contrary: that cautery is of no use for a disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For fire's nature is hot, and should not be used to cure a disease caused by heat and dryness; and he who says the contrary says that cautery brings great help to a hot and dry disease in the human body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body to be cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in no way should one meddle with it unless it is someone who has tested it, and who knows through long experience the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of men's complexions, and their dispositions and the causes of their illnesses, and their outcomes and the species of time; we are not afraid of other complexions, even in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors gathered and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that a fire cautery gathers together heat and is of greater benefit than a burning medical cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple and does not come to any member except the one that needs it, and does not harm any other member if it is applied carefully.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Hot medicaments move from one member to another while spreading apart, and they bring illnesses with difficult healing to the afflicted part and possibly kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fevers, due to their intensity and the goodness of their substance, do not cause any harm if there is no excess or superfluity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experiment and the length of service and study that I have devoted to the art, which is close to the truth of matters. Therefore, I excuse myself for the length of my words, as I do not wish to take away from you the secrecy contained within fire, and its quality of work, how it dispels diseases in bodies, just as the philosopher says in his demonstration. Now, receive this in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, that they agreed on when cauteries should be performed and chose priests.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harm arising is placed beneath through the aid of cauterization; and even if the cautery is necessary due to urgent and rapid pain that cannot wait for the time it takes for greater evil to come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think, dear child, as foolish men do; because the illness that is healed by cautery will not return; and they say so; but it is not as they think, because cauterization is not a medicine that changes complexion, and dries up the humors which are the cause of pain, rather it is a quick medicine due to its power and effectiveness.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the illness comes at times according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the disease and its virtue; and impurities are gathered in him due to the acquisition of food and similar things, unless cauterization is administered where there is little excess and moisture, such as cautery for toothache and similar things, and that pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the "rear guard" of medicine, but this is true; however, they do not believe that cautery has any value after medication, but their understanding is false, and cautery is the "rear guard" of medicine because when we administer methods of cures for any illness and they are not effective, then we administer cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery with an instrument of gold is more gentle than iron, and they did not say this without reason but because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance; and they said that the place of cauterization does not cause mortification, but that is not true, for I have tried it and found it to be true in some men; and cautery with gold is more gentle than iron, as they rightly said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot because of the color of the gold and it quickly cools down; and if it is heated too much, it becomes brittle in the fire; and so there are many difficulties with this.[**Prompt**: Translate the following text into English.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use iron cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have arranged this chapter on dislocations from head to feet, so that the vein may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for moistening and cooling the brain, and it is made for a disease called "soda," as well as for many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for an abundance of dreams, pain in the teeth, and sore throat, and also for all illnesses that come from coolness, such as paralysis and stiffness and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The shape of this cautery is such that the patient must be purged with a cleansing medicine that cleanses the head three or four nights, depending on the strength and age and custom of the patient's body; and then warm the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make the patient sit cross-legged between your hands, and place their hands on a weight; then put the base of your palm on the base of their nose between their two eyes; and place your middle fingers where the tears come out. Warm the "olivare" cautery, which is shaped as follows:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it (the mark) on the spot where it is dislocated, and make a sign with ink by pulling down and stretching out your hand repeatedly; then lift your hand immediately, and look at the spot to see if you see a small swelling; and if you do not see it, then repeat the cauterization until you see the swelling as I have told you; after take a small amount of fat, and put it in a soft cloth and place it on the spot, and leave it for three days; after put a wet compress soaked in butter on it; and leave it on until the burn has healed; after cure the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges itself; and therefore, movement helps.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that one should leave the cauterization in place long enough that part of the bone is burnt, and then remove what has been burnt from the bone, and then cure it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others said that one should leave the cauterization in place for so long and press down so hard that it sinks into the bone as wide as a distaff that women put in their flax, so that the humors can come out; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one should cure and suture it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem good to me in every way, except in certain men where there is fear; and it seems to me that I should abandon the other one; for the head is weakened by continuous natural solutions, as we witness in other members; and even when the patient's head is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is more healthy and effective for me, and of this one I use work for a speedy recovery.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain comes all over the head and lasts long, the patient should use roots and pills which are called "cochie", and purgatives for the head and eyes and poultices; and if one applies the cautery that we have previously mentioned and it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's head is of strong constitution and not too cold; then cauterize it a little below the cautery that we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After perform cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as stated before, and perform a cautery at the spot called "vasselz"; and this is a location where one can apply cupping glasses; and arrange your hand so that you do not see up to the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of that later; and the cauteries of the horns should be more refined than those used for the middle of the head, and this is the method.
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When there is sudden pain in a part of the head, and the illness extends up to the eye, and the head has been purged with cleansing medicines, and the other cures that I mentioned in the division of diseases have been attempted, and yet none are effective: then one performs cautery in two ways, namely using medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery of medicine ague is as follows: take a piece of aloe wood, remove the bark and soak it in a little wine for two days, then apply it to the temple where the pain resides in such a way that you can place the piece of aloe wood under the skin; when it is in place, bind and secure it well and leave it for twelve hours; then undo it and remove the piece of aloe, leaving the wound open for two or three days; then apply a compress soaked in butter until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the care of wound healing until it is healed; and if you wish, use any burning medicines that I have written in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cautery is of this kind. Heat the cautery to the following shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the end is shaped like a bell with one curved hollow portion and a small projection in the middle; place it on the painful area and hold your hand steady while moving the cautery lightly back and forth until half of its thickness has been burnt, then lift your hand so that the artery (which is located further out) does not get burned, allowing for an abundant flow of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterward, place a piece of cotton soaked in oil on it and leave it for three days; then apply moistened cotton with butter, and continue to care for the wound until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the "cultellare" cautery, do so at the very tip, being careful not to touch the artery in this new (not ancient) migraine.
de emigraine	of a headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat a headache as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not help at all, and you see that the cautery before spoken of by medicine and fire is not sufficient, then you should heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it turns white; and place it above the painful area in a straight line half a finger long, and remove your hand once, and hold firmly so as not to cover the artery or reach the bone; and be aware of the movement of the jaw when chewing, and the nerve should not move and spasms should not come upon the patient, and be aware of blood loss from the artery when it is cut, or fear greatly even for one who does not know and is not a learned and experienced person; and leave the work half-finished; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it fits in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries do not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize it on the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals; and if necessary, use the cautery we mentioned in the chapter on arrow extraction, with a cautery having two blades; and this cautery is better than the previous one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of ear pain due to cold draughts.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear from cold, and medical solutions and other cures have been tried, as we have said in the division, and the pain does not lessen, then heat this poker-like cautery, called "poins", of which this is the shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterward, cauterize all around the affected ear, or around both if the pain persists in both, and move back a bit above the root of the ear after you have marked the spot to be cauterized. Then make ten cautery marks around each ear; afterward, care for the area until it heals completely.
de la torture de la bouche	The following text appears to be incomplete. However, based on the provided phrase "de la torture de la bouche," I will provide a possible translation:
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	The torture (pain or affliction) that should be treated with cautery is only those that move from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make any cautery for similar ones that come from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this type of torture that moves with fluid from purging of the head and gargling, and it is ineffective, then you should cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the base of the ear, another a little behind the temple, and the third on the joint of the two lips; and place the cautery on the exposed healthy part, and make the cautery near the top of the ear a little below the ear's horn, and another in the temple as long as a thumb; and leave the cautery in place until half of the heart is burned; and this is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the appearance of the scalpel that we have mentioned before, but it is a bit more subtle and requires that the knife be a little larger; after curing the wound as I said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, but it does not improve and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two corners of the head, one at the middle of the head, and one in the place called "vasselz" as we mentioned before, and the last cautery at the mouth of the stomach; and cure it as we said before.
de litargie	The term "litargie" is a variant spelling of "lethargy," which refers to a state of physical or mental lethargy or sluggishness, often caused by illness or lack of sleep. It can also refer to a condition characterized by prolonged unconsciousness or coma.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this ailment, give the patient large grains and purifying pills for the brain; then thoroughly heat the patient's head and apply to the back of the head the plaster of sinape as written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the method of cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is cured in this way, it is good; and if not, perform three cauteries along the head down to the neck, leaving a space of two fingers between each cautery; and treat it as you would any other injury, and if you wish to add to it and the patient is tolerant, perform one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two others on the two horns (temples), and continue treatment until he is cured; and let the cautery used be called "olivare", as I have previously mentioned.
de la froidor dou chief	of the chill/coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head must be cleaned of grains and other things previously mentioned; then heat the patient's head, then perform cautery on the head and on each temple, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient tolerant, and the illness is strong, if necessary, perform four cauteries on the spine of the back; and leave it alone until the most severe part of the heat has subsided, then remove your hand; then treat it until it is healed; and use the "olivare" cautery that was previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to cleanse the brain first with purgatives and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and able to take medication.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, make them gargle and chew purgatives frequently to cleanse the brain with good foods; then let the king's touch be applied in the middle of the head, and perform one cautery on the scalp and one cautery on each horn (temple); and if the patient is strong and able to tolerate it, perform cauteries as I have said for those with paralysis and weakening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be made of olive wood in the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, perform one subtle cautery in this way:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, superfluities or corrupt moisture cause thick phlegm, then use such cautery as we have said for someone who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, the superfluities tend towards melancholy and the body of the patient is moist, then give them to drink something that purifies the brain, according to what has been stated in the division (i.e. the earlier part of the text).
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, wash the patient's head; then make a well-made linen compress, like a circle, and place it on the head; and have the patient lie crosswise, and be held firmly from all sides; then apply the linen, and use old sheep's butter; and heat it with moderate fire, so that the skin can bear it; then empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool down; and do this to the patient once a week, along with other good treatment, until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	Or, if you wish to cauterize (by making multiple punctures) over the entire area of the cautery. This method of cauterization moistens the brain excessively; and then place a cotton soaked in butter and chicken fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	of the evacuation of tears/eye discharge
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When there is first an evacuation of tears/eye discharge according to the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink something that purifies the head, guards against all moistures, and makes them sweat or take several baths while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterwards, instruct the patient to tilt their head back, and perform cautery in the middle of the forehead, and make two cauterizations on the two temples if the evacuation of tears/eye discharge is in both eyes together, or in one if it is in one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are beneath the skull for the entire length of the cautery; and beware of excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop the bleeding as best you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in making incisions how to stop the bleeding; and sometimes cautery or a hot iron is done beneath the two bones at the back.[Reference(s):
dou cors des larmes	"the source/origin of tears" or "the heart of tears" in modern English. It is unclear what exactly the author means by this phrase without more context.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes have become old and customary and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are apparent on the outside of the head; and it is seen that it comes from cold fluids, then he should apply the caution that I said in the beginning of the chapter, descending towards the eyes: one cautery to the forehead, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries in the corners below the two bones; and if more is needed, then cauterize abundantly above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the fluid from within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you administer the medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the patient three rooster combs to drink; then raise the head of the sick person, and apply a moderate cautery with an olive-oil soaked sponge; and make two cauteries with the "clavilis" cautery on the eyebrows, a little below the hairline; and be careful not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the papyrus of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then use this cautery which is called "olivary," of which the form is as follows:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish to do so, make two cauteries on the two swellings as long as the swellings are; and do not remove your hand until a third part of the papyrus is burned, in the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, and cauteries are made according to two methods: namely by fire or by heating medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they (hairs) grow and are even, then place the patient in your care; afterward, on a piece of paper place an outline that is similar to the leaf of a fern, and let the beginning of the sign be next to the hairs; then put cotton soaked in egg white and powdered lichen of parsley on the eye, then heat the cautery of the shape that is shown here:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing along the outline that you have marked many times, so that the skin is burned in that spot; and the sign of the success of the operation is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs standing up at the edge of the eye; then lift your hand and leave it like that for three days, then put cotton soaked in butter on until the burn is healed; after that, treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after that the hairs return and the paper becomes softened, then repeat the cautery on the same spot as before; and if the hairs are missing, then cauterize until the paper rises to its natural level, and is even, and do not prick the eye with the hairs.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The fiery cautery of medicine is what you should instruct the patient to do: let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment in the shape of a fern leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one third, and grind them together well; and do it quickly so that it does not cool down, then spread it on the form that you have made similar to the fern leaf, and put it on the paper of the eyes; and if the illness is in only one eye, then work on one side, and if it is on both sides as well; and place cotton soaked in egg yolk under the eye; and let the patient's head be in your care and place your hand over the medicine, and press a little and move it every time the patient feels the biting of the medicine, for he will feel it like the biting of fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from the wound.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the biting (pain) has passed, lift the wound's crust and check if you see the skin underneath lifted as if it was lifted by constriction of fire or incision; and if it is so, then it is good. If not, then apply more medicine on the wound until your work is even and your eyes are healed; then put a wet cotton swab with butter on the burnt area until the burn has healed; after that, cure the place of the ointment which is called "dyafenis" and other, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if it is necessary for you to be very careful in your work so that the medicine does not fall into the eyes. And if the skin becomes soft and hairs prick into the eye, then reapply the medicine on the affected area where the skin has softened properly; after that cure it until it is healed; and this is the method of the mirthe leaf.[Note: The word "mirtre" in old French means a type of plant/herb. It's not clear which specific herb it refers to, but contextually it seems to be referring to some kind of medical dressing or herbal application used for healing.]
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this should be your constraints (precautions); and let not the direct path be held as the same for one whose study is of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the section on diseases, and your treatments do not help at all, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on them in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in your lap; and have the assistant hold the patient's head between your hands so that it does not move or shift; then place a cotton swab soaked in egg white or pennyroyal juice on the eye; then heat the cautery which is parted: and attach it to the head like the shape of a dove's feather, with the tip touching the skin; if you wish, make it pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, also like a tent; but in any case, this which is attached is more useful for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Afterwards press on the fistula if it is open, and extract the rottenness and dry matter from it; and if it is closed, then open it and extract the pus from it; afterwards place hot wheat flour on the cautery, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part above the eye, so that your hand does not move foolishly; and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery down to the bone, it would be good. If not, then perform cautery again, and another time if you need to, and leave it for three days; afterwards place a cotton swab soaked in butter on it, and treat the wound with a drying ointment until it is healed; and if 40 days pass and it is not healed, then apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and treat it according to what comes in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a type of cautery for a fistula that some of the ancients mentioned. Understand "fistula," and open the place; after, put into the opening a thin piece of iron, the shape of which is as follows:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make it the size of a hazelnut; and hold your hand firmly on the iron, and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted lead does not enter his eye; and it is necessary to place cotton soaked in egg white or oil on the patient's eye: the lead will heal the fistula, and the healthy flesh will marvelously heal.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good. If not, then one must administer a perforation to the nose and draw the fistula to the nose's flesh according to what is appropriate in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	Here is my new line to translate: "des crevaices en levres"
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks occur on lips which are called “crevices,” and the same is true for children’s lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks, as we have mentioned in divisions, and the treatment does not work, then heat a small scalpel-like fire cautery of this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And quickly place it in those cracks until it reaches the root; then apply a salve to the area until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	on an abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the eye, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has rotted and turned and become a fistula; and you treat it as we have mentioned in divisions, but it does not improve: then you must use a cautery appropriate to the size of the fistula; then put it over the opening or hole of the fistula, and keep your hand until the iron becomes hot and reaches the bottom of it and behind it; and do this once or twice, after treating as we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured this way, that is good; and if not, then you must uncover the area and remove the rotten bone, according to what you find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	from movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines but it is of no avail, then place the patient's head in your lap; after that, heat the cautery so that its shape will be as follows: place a stick on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery inside, holding your hand in such a way that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and repeat the cautery as you wish; after that, have the patient fill their mouth with salty water and gargle for an hour.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the moving tooth is strengthened, and the softened gum is constricted, and the moisture is corrupted and dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from coldness, whether real or imagined, and medical treatment is not effective, then it is necessary to use the cautery in two ways: with butter and fire.[IST] Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery of butter is as follows: take cow's butter, and the tip in an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a lance, and moisten it in boiled butter, and place it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it there until it has cooled down; and do this often until the virtue of it reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and place a hot iron on it until the heat reaches the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery is as follows: take an iron or bronze rod, and make it thick enough so that the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, which will form as follows, and place it on the tooth, holding your hand until the cautery has cooled down; do this often, for the pain will be eased on the same day or the next. And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cautery, and then rinse it out; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery of whatever eyelid you want, and according to what you have power over; and this is the form of the rod:
des scrophules	of scrofula (a disease affecting the lymphatic glands in the neck)
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulous swellings are of phlegm and cold moistures, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the fire-iron until it is red-hot, and have two openings for the fumes to escape on the side away from the swelling; and place the hot iron on the abscess once or twice as needed, until you reach the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the iron accordingly, and leave it in place for three days; and apply a wet compress soaked in butter to ease the burn; after that, treat the area with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the moistures have overcome the channels of the peritoneum, and likewise when it is due to a cold complexion, then the patient should first be evacuated with soluble medicines; after that, perform cautery at the base of the throat, but make sure not to come too close to the throat, and only burn slightly. Then perform another cautery at the joint between the neck and the spine, using an iron shaped like a "clavile" as we have described before; and treat the area as we have said before until it is healed.

Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all the symptoms and the disease of the peritoneum are due to cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or wasting, and the illness is chronic, then perform two cauteries on the stomach in visible places; and another cautery between the breasts in the area near the nipples; and use an iron shaped like a "clavile" as we have described before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a .xxx., ou enqui entor.
