Afterward heal the area as previously mentioned, and let the cautery have three notches according to this shape.
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And therefore, the cauteries are lighter, because you make three of them at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	about the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, have the patient recline on their back and side; then lift the heart that is within the chest with the tips of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery which has two nerves, such is its form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the heart until it pierces to the ribs, and the figure of the cautery would come together as four cauteries; and for this reason, the cautery is made with a three-nerved cautery, so that the figures of cauterization are six cauteries; and the nerves are according to the fineness of a tent and such is the form of the three-nerved cautery:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes, it is adjusted on this one nerve, for which there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards, place the powdered cautery on it, mixed with oil; then let the patient rest and do not move the limb for a long time until it is fully healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant. Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	And if it is dislocated upwards, little consequence occurs, then apply the cautery to the thick part of the clavicle, or many cauteries by pricking. For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the pleurisy cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make cauteries for pleurisy from aristolochia roots, and in this manner: take a long aristolochia root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and let it be as thick and as long as your thumb; and moisten it in oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauteries a little below in the area that is beneath the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, inclining a little behind; and one cautery in the middle of the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two at the sides of the breast outside the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but instead act openly as if you are smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	And certain ancients said that some people use a fire cautery similar to a razor, heating it and placing it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and then the pain goes away, as we have said in the abscess of the liver. But in this work, there is fear that the patient dies or a fistula develops which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse (or perhaps "marrow" - the Old French word "mice" can mean either)
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the "mice" (or marrow) in those we have mentioned in the divisions of treatments, and it does not help at all, then there are three kinds of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	One of these methods is to make three or four cauteries in a row, following the length of the "mice" (or marrow), according to the shape of the liver that we mentioned earlier; and do not press your hand on all the cautery, and let the patient be lying on their back.[Comments: Here, it seems like the text is describing a surgical procedure using cauterization, possibly to treat an abscess or tumor in the liver. The surgeon is instructed to make several cautery marks along the length of the affected area, following its shape, and not to press too hard on the instrument. It's interesting to note that the patient is positioned on their back, which may have been a common position for abdominal surgeries in medieval medicine.]
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	And another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the kidney which is next to the "mice" (or marrow), where the patient's costal ribs come towards the left, and let the lifting of the kidney be according to the kidney, according to the length of the body, and let the cauteries be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After that, put the two inflamed nerves in until the kidney is pierced from the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and in this way there will be four. And if you wish, cauterize the entire cautery with three nerves. Afterwards cure when it has rotted for a long time, and this is worth more than the other cures mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	The fire cautery is not beneficial for the dropsical patient, except for the method called "asclites". When you cure them according to the methods that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit at all, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, two behind the back on the spine, and one next to the ribcage; and let the cauteries be close to the thickness of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery on to suppurate for a long time, and do not stop the patient's care after the cautery; and if healing is hastened, both intentions will be achieved with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the stomach is the clavicle, as shown before; and the one for the back should be olive-shaped, as it is described earlier.[NOTE: The text seems to refer to specific shapes for cauteries that have been previously mentioned. I assume "clavile" refers to a claw-like shape, and "olivaire" likely means an olive or round shape. However, without more context or illustrations, it's hard to say for certain.]
de l’enfleure des piez	of swelling in the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner. Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	When the feet are swollen in someone who is dropsical, and are full of watery serosity, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning it. And do not enter too deep, otherwise you will cut through the watery serosity, and let the cautery be in this shape:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Afterwards, make two cauteries on each leg at the tip of the scalpel; and let the cauteries be long, one beneath the knee in front and the other in the middle of the leg in back; and leave the cauteries open for a long time without curing, so that the water drains out; after taking care of the other treatments that we have mentioned.

Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the stomach comes from coldness and moisture, to such an extent that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines become weakened and cannot be cured by any means; and you see the patient suffering greatly but still having strong vitality, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before about the stomach cautery, at the circular cautery; and four subtle cauteries around the belly, with one subtle clavile cautery for each one, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each side, and two small cauteries next to the large one on the stomach, for the cure is beneficial when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Here is a line-by-line translation of the medieval medical text about the treatment of hemorrhoids:
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are in the rectum, one or more, and are old and consist of large cold and moist corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not improve, perform cauteries: three on the spine of the back, the one which is entirely outside below the prominent sacrum and sacrum in a triangular shape, and one beneath the buttocks. two fingers' widths.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that their stomach is cooled down, and the food does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then perform a large cautery on the stomach, as it is said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen at the entire length of the cauterizing iron; and leave the cautery in place for a long time. Afterwards cure the area until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut thelul (a term for fleshiness), heat up the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it completely burning on the cut thelul; and leave your hand in that position until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein, from which the blood flows. Do this once or twice, and if there are many theluls, cauterize each one as we have said; after that cure them with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on alchemy (possibly meaning a chemical substance), it will be of greater help.
de plaie mal curee	of a wound poorly treated
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, then comes a disease that can only be cured by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes to someone and it is festering, casting off rotten and corrupt matter, you should test it with a thin probe and make sure that you know the depth of the entire probe. Afterwards, heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the length that the probe has entered, and continue heating the cautery until the rotten and corrupt flesh is burned away, once, or twice, or three times, depending on how much is needed. And be careful not to burn the nerves which are inside, and the large veins. If the fistula goes towards the body of the bladder and intestines, then be cautious of these areas, and do not perform this procedure outside of a fleshy area, and keep in mind that it is not safe; after caring for the area until it is healed, if the area becomes elevated and matter has been drained for a long time, then know that the area is completely healed. But if the matter is not drained, then know that the area is not fully healed, and the bone will become corrupted at its foundation. And so it is with one of those which we will discuss in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain in the cold comes to the kidneys, and there is swelling from an abundance of wind, and they have no desire for a woman, then you should perform cautery on the kidneys, one on each side, using the clavicle cautery that we mentioned before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and this will provide greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak due to cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then perform cautery on the outer side above the bladder, where the hair of the groin starts, with one on the right and one on the left, each cauterization should be as long as the width of a coin; and perform one cautery on the back, or two if necessary; and let the cauteries be shaped as described before.

Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit. de la hainche	In this context, "de la hainche" likely refers to a condition known as dropsy or edema in modern medicine. It is characterized by the accumulation of fluid in the body cavities or tissues. In Old French, "hainche" can refer to swelling or inflammation, and it was often treated with cauterization in medieval medical texts. Here's a possible translation:
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When humorous vapors descend to the hip's case, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and one of the signs is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the location of the separation is visible, then you should cauterize the patient on the hip's case with a cautery similar to a circle, and mark before the separation around the case as it turns, so that the case is within the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not present, make three cauteries of large olive size, and let the cauteries be as deep as all hearts; and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the hip.
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip's case, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient has been treated with what we have said in the division and the treatment does not work, and the illness is old: then you should purge the patient of heavy humors with stinking pills or other good similar pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	Afterward, perform cauterization; and the types of cauterization are according to two methods: that is, burning medicines, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is of many kinds, one of which is as follows: you cauterize on the boil's knob three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make a good depth and size, and let there be between each cautery a space the width of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes a single cautery is done in the middle on the top of the boil, so that there are four in this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize it with the circular cautery that we have previously mentioned for the dislocation of the boil; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire boil, and all the flesh of the area is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the method used for sciatica, when the pain resides in the hip and does not reach down to the thigh or leg. And if it reaches the thigh and the leg, then two cauteries are made where the patient indicates the pain, and one above the ankle four fingers wide, slightly to the left; and let the cautery be knife-shaped, and let the fleshy areas be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near them, then cauterize it in three or four points with the cautery called "points" where the patient feels the pain.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, perform more cauterization; and if the patient feels that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then perform a knife-shaped or circular cautery, and take great care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery on for too long such that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause further harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen several who had cautery applied to the ankle of the foot, and they let it heal for so long that the leg swelled up completely, and so did the foot, and the whole foot became pierced and corrupted. Afterwards, they died from a stomach ailment.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two places together, perform cautery on both, in this manner. // And the wise men said in the cautery of inflammation, of which this is the method, make a such a iron and let it be as thick as a small bean stalk of date palm, or slightly less, and let there be crosspieces at equal distances, and let them be spaced as much apart as the width of a bean of pocktree; and let the crosspieces be turned in two parts, and let them be like knots, and there should be one well-made iron handle; and this is its shape.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it is completely red and starts to drip, then place it on the swollen boil of the patient, and turn it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery rod and leave it for three days; then apply a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) said that we use little of this cautery because of fear of its effect, and if one were to see those who use it; and nevertheless, it is one of the good cauteries which can be endured by those on whom it is used, and where it is applied.
de la dolor dou dos	of the back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling, or from percussion, or from excessive evacuation, or from spread out cold matter, none of these instances is suitable for cauterization, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after the patient has been purged with foul-smelling pills or other similar things, three lines be signed on the back, in the place where the pain resides, using ink; and in each line there should be five cauterizations or more, according to the potency and quantity that the patient can tolerate; and let the cauterization be done using the type of cauterization called "poins"; and if you wish, do three or four cauterizations using the clavile moien method, in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a stiff neck when they get up, and fear; and you will find on the back, on the last spine of the spine, an appearance which comes before the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, cauterize it with the cautery of this sort, in this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery reaches every part of the spine evenly. And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the cautery pointing two or three lines away, and let the points be close to one another. Afterwards, cure the area until it is healed, as we have said, and be careful not to apply cautery to a gouty area in a nerve bundle.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is due to humors that are spread throughout every member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which is properly called "gout" by laymen, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured by medicines, it can be cured by cauteries in the following way: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped in this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary to apply the cautery to the sole of the foot, let it be a whole cautery that is called "point". And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, which happens frequently, let three or four cauteries be made on each knee on every side, with the whole cautery olive-shaped; and if you need more, do so, but do not hold your hand away for too long that the thickness of the flesh is not burnt.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend down to the knee and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist two lines deep; and if there remains no pain in the knuckles, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the wrists or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care to the patient and give them medicine. For if you provide good care and purge phlegm, they will heal with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the opening of the abscess.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the abscess comes to a head and the bowels descend to the haunches and this is recent, then when you see it needs to be cured, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that evacuate the belly, so that feces descends from their stomach; after make them sit on their back between your hands, and command them to hold their breath until the abscess has subsided, and then massage it with your fingers, and apply a bandage below the abscess over the bone of the wrist, and in such a way that it forms half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with which this form is made:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and releases pus. Then massage the bowels back into place; and the caregiver should keep their hand over it so that they do not return; and work well on the thighs of the patient, and put a cushion and a servant under their thighs, and another on the chest who holds their hands; then place the cautery on the mark with your whole hand, and hold it firmly and strongly until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, try again until you do; and be careful that the abscess does not burst when you apply the cautery, that you do not burn them, and that through this the patient does not die or suffer any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless. And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be fine, according to the measure of eggs, and also large for large people, according to their measure; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the heat is removed; after curing other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie down for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left on for a long time, so that the boils do not come out when he takes exercise in chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, prepare a well-made belt for him, and let him wear it for another forty days; and have good rest, that he works little and guards against excessive consumption of drink and food, and loud talking; and when he follows this teaching, he will be completely healed. And I will speak later about the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	"of abdominal surgery" is what you meant to say, right? The Old French phrase "la routure dou ventre" translates to "the rupture/tear of the belly/stomach".
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other stomachs and are known, and you see that they do not grow any larger, perform one cautery with the same type of cautery, according to its size, and burn one third of the belly; after that, cure it as we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-pointed cautery in this shape: [I'm attaching an image to illustrate the shape of the cautery, but I'm unable to do so here.]

But the first cauterization is lighter and subtler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in some member (limb)
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to some member (limb), either from falling or being struck, and this pain lasts for a long time, and medical treatment is of no use, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the "pointed" cautery, and let the cautery be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, and strength, and its location, considering the twisting and pain. If it heals from the first cauterization, that's good; if not, begin again with another cautery on top of it, for it is often the case that it must change to the member that is near it, so you must perform the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of leprosy (Hansen's disease)
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Lepers are sometimes helped by cautery with great benefit, as well as diseases that come from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy. When you see them to be cauterized, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and it does not worsen nor remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the patient's body, then perform five cauteries on the head: one on the crown of the head, and another towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two horns (temples), and one behind on the nape; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the gross humors can escape; and cauterize the area according to what it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the illness is spread everywhere and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize it with the cauteries that we have mentioned in the head, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the haunch and another next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the hips, and two on the tendons of the arms, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are at the back pressing down, so as not to burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that when you make more cauteries, you do more help and benefit the patient; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because their body is already completely corrupted. And you should make the cauteries large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the ways of ironwork. Afterwards cure the wound with a mixture of flour of chickpeas with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
de enfleure	It seems that the last word of your previous message, "de enfleure", was meant to be added to my translation of the medieval medical text. Here's an updated version with the additional phrase:
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to any limb and is treated by medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then cautery is done on the limb according to its size; and let the cautery be a little into the thickness of the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it is healed. And sometimes cautery is done on the hand, foot, and back, at the opening of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; but no one should meddle with it if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the openings of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	The term "de albaras" does not appear in the provided Old French medical text. It is possible that this is a transcription error or it may be a term from a different source. Without more context, it is not possible to provide a translation or interpretation of "de albaras".
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has become persistent and the means of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the quantity of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed and its color changed; then cure it with bran of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and each one part of swallows' blood and sparrows' blood; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and expose it to air until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The phrase "li cure de chancre par cautere" can be translated as "the treatment of chancre by cautery". Chancre was a term used in medieval medicine to refer to various types of ulcers or sores, including those associated with syphilis. Cautery was one method of treating these sores, and involved using a hot iron or other heated instrument to burn the affected area. This was believed to promote healing by destroying infected tissue and sealing off blood vessels. The specific instructions for performing such a treatment would depend on the particular medical text and context in which it appears.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a chancre begins and you want to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the circumference of the chancre. And yet, wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen several times; and a more appropriate thing is that it be cauterized around, using the "circular" cautery, as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	If someone has a disease called “adubelati” which does not heal, either due to the excess it causes, or due to the patient's old age and weakened condition (when they are very old and have little blood), or due to time; and you want to hasten its healing: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries in punctures. Afterward, leave it that way. Because it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you want to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery like this:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of the ailment called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced through to the heart, and let the cauteries be such that the patient feels them from outside in a manner that lightens the course of the gangrene. Afterward heal it until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the healing by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	There is another kind of illness called "corrodens," which is nothing but an eating away of the limbs, just as fire consumes dry wood. If you see this disease in a place where it can tolerate cautery along with fire, then heat the iron cauteries very gently, both large and small, according to what is required for the location where the illness is; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all of the corruption, and let nothing remain of it. Then leave it alone for three days, and put soft bread soaked in oil on the heated cauterized areas until the burns from the fire are healed, along with all of the corruption. Afterward heal with ointments that generate flesh. And if you see after three days that healthy flesh is not born, this is good; but if not, then repeat the cautery on the parts that remain corrupted. And sometimes this eating away has been cured by medicinal treatment instead of fire cautery; however, cautery with fire is of greater help. I have already mentioned the cure for the medical treatment in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the splinters that come to (or go into) the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often happens that at the feet arises a sickness called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large abscess that wounds the foot. And the cauteries for this sickness are of two kinds. That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery. The fire cautery is that you heat a small knife as big as a roof tile's pen, and make it from good iron, of a size that can reach the nail from all sides, and have fine edges; then place it very hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the base of the nail; and leave it like this for three days until it begins to rot; then make a plaster with crushed mallow leaves with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the place with ointment spreading out the flesh until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are turned away from the body, both in hands and feet, then you should apply hot water cautery; and it is done in this manner: take a rod of iron or copper, or a roof tile's pen, and place it on the nail and the althelul, that is to say porrelz verrues; and place the rod on it so that it boils all around, then put some hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the edges of the rod come to the base of the nail, and can find a deep path through the hot water to the root; and let the patient endure the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will be uprooted along with all its roots. Do so on each one, until you reach all that are on the body, then cure them with ointments that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment for shaking/trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone shakes from cold nerves or quartan fever or other causes, then you should apply four or five cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery on the hip, and one on the stomach at the location of the olive cautery; this will stop the shaking, and hasten the healing of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes appear on the body, due to a lack of care, bad-smelling pustules which come from large corrupted matter. At first, when they appear, one should make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery made from a myrtle stick, with its tip taken by fire, or from a long aristolochia root, or from a round cautery. And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning, in this manner, and they cannot grow any further, but the superfluities from which they come are broken and they heal; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut[The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	It often happens that there is a large loss of blood from the artery which has been cut in a wound or incision of an abscess or in the cauterization of a limb, and similar things; and it is very difficult to stop the bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to someone, hasten to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press it very hard so that the blood is calmed beneath your finger, and no more comes out; then put
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you remove your finger from above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, quickly take another one of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be stopped easily, especially if the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by tightly binding with a bandage, or by medicines placed on it which have the power to stop blood; and let it be bound and held firmly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer the stopping of the bleeding by tightly binding with bandages or by placing hot things on it, or other similar things, if it does not help then it is of no use.[Note: This sentence is a continuation of the previous translation and provides a cautionary statement about the methods mentioned in the previous sentence.]
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if it happens to someone who does not have medical equipment or medicine present, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and pull hard until it stays above the wound and vein; and he should not move it, but wet it frequently with very cold water until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and make preparations for what he needs in terms of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgeries.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or heated medicine, and we have described their causes, instruments, and forms; and I put this chapter about the head down to the feet, and I will go in this chapter the same way so that one can more easily find what they are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so as I begin this one, it is important, dear son, that you understand that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter on cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to undertake folly. For many kinds of people come to cures: those who are so afflicted by their illness that they easily die due to the severity they find in their disease, and the gravity of its malice; and one should fear these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And among them are those who give you their trust and say: "wait, I am healed." The illness is scornful. It is not at all appropriate to agree with those who come to you with this attitude, but rather put more effort into your honor than your greed, and do not foolishly open up for those about whom you are uncertain and can potentially harm your reputation; and use prognostication and indication in the care of your patients so that their health may be restored; and this will help you to achieve good renown, glory, and praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may Our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to inhale the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Here is the translation:
dou chief plein d’aigue	"the head full of water" or "the swollen head"
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	"Know that this disease often occurs in children during childbirth, and when the birth is difficult and the mother grips the child's head too hard; and sometimes it happens for no apparent reason."
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	"And I have never seen this disease except in children, and among those that I have seen, their deaths came quickly; and for this reason it seems better to me to leave such work to more skilled practitioners."
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	"And I saw a child whose head was full of water and became larger every day until it could no longer support its own weight; and the fluid increased so much that he died, and this fluid collects under the bone at the temple, between the brain and the skull; and the procedure is such when the fluid is between the brain and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make an incision in the head, a slit wide enough for the fluid to flow out; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the fluid can escape; and here is the shape of the spatula:"
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more advanced and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the form of a cross, following this pattern:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs you see are that the corners of the mouth are open on both sides, and pus comes out when you press it from the inside with your hand, and this does not respond (to treatment); then you must make three incisions in the middle of the chin, following this pattern:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. After the incision, remove all the pus. Then bind the incisions with cloth and powder, and apply wine and oil. Also continue to keep the chin bound up, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is healed and healthy again.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is to observe where the swelling of the abscess is most prominent, and where the pus has gathered; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then at the place where the abscess is open, and the filling of water, and the opening according to what you have the power; and take care not to cut the artery; and if blood flows, so that the patient dies from the outpouring of blood and evacuation of moisture.

Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old-age migraine comes, and acute catarrh, due to moisture in the tears and heat in the temples and swelling of the crazy ancient head and similar things, and it is treated by various medical cures but none bring improvement, then let us extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of their extraction is that the patient shaves the hairs from their temples and pays attention to the artery that appears in the temple, for it appears clearly through its beating, and is not deeply hidden except in some men who are very cold; and if it is hidden, let the patient strain their neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth and apply hot water to it until the artery is clearly visible; then take the spatula of the form described:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout. For if it is not cut, the blood will not come out completely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw blood from the six holes until three have been made; and if the arteries are large, you must tie them in two places with a strong double thread of silk so that rotting does not occur before the wound is healed and proper bleeding occurs; then cut away any excess tissue between the two ties at once; and if you wish, cauterize the wound with a knife-edged cautery to the bone until the holes are closed; this is the more effective method, if the patient does not have a fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery serves to end moisture: therefore it is of greater help for moisture-related conditions.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, that one fills the wound with old cotton and places well-made bandages on top; and when they are loosened, they should be cared for with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with bandages, until it is healed; and if blood flows from the slit of the artery as much as you work, then hurry to cover it with a hot cautery, or fill the wound with vitriol and hold it with your hand until the blood stops; and if you don't have this present, then place your finger on the wound until the blood clots, and pour cold water over the wound until it ceases, and hold it as is necessary; and that which is easier and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the slit with this two-part cutting cautery, but let the cuts be thick to keep their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be a finger's breadth of space between the two knives, and then when you have marked the two places, place the red-hot iron on them until it reaches the bone, and cut the slit in two places; and they should be far apart because this cutting cautery is not welded together in its entirety; and that is the form of the cautery.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes flow from the veins that are above the forehead, and curing with medicine does not help, and you see the face of the patient turn red, and feel a pulsating sensation on the forehead as if in trembling; and the eyelids are held closed and moist such that the eyelashes have fallen out, and the eyelids are heated and irritated from the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And the ancient people called it "cure contused", and this is what you should do for the patient who has this illness: have them grow out the hairs on their forehead, then make three even incisions on the forehead according to its length; and one of the incisions should be in the middle of the forehead, going down to the nose, and the other two should be at the temples above the eyelids, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are located near the temples; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and each wound should be the length of three fingers held together.

Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.
