And place the cutting edge towards the fleshy part near the heart, and the blunt edge towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle of the wound. Cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes, making the incision continuous down to where it is visible near the heart, then do the same in the middle wound down to the other side; and then let the blood flow out evenly, and press on the wound to extract the blood; then place a piece of old cotton in each wound, and place wet bandages on them with wine and oil and vinegar, and make sure that pus does not form; and on the third day loosen the binding, and apply a lot of cool water, then treat with basilicon ointment and rose oil, and other cures used for wounds, until it heals.
dou reume des eulz	Of the membrane of the eyes.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone frequently has a cold and you notice that the eyes are sunken and small, and their vision is weakened, and the whites of their eyes are inflamed; and their hair falls out, and they have a deep headache, and they cough; then know from these symptoms that those substances and catarrh do not come from one vein alone, and the cause of this is as follows:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And instruct the patient to bend their forehead, then make a large incision along the forehead, and another of about one inch. Begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and let it reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; and once the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two lips of the incision and put a piece of old cotton, and a linen cloth; then bind wet cloths soaked in wine and oil on top, and be careful to avoid hot abscesses; when removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then cure it with drying agents that help the flesh to grow.

In this manner: take two parts of flower of wheat and four parts of colophony, and make it into an ointment; and apply it to these wounds to promote the growth of flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	on ear stoppage.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains or small animals, stone from mines or similar things such as iron; seed such as lice, beans, peas; or fluid such as water and earwax and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it falls into the ear a stone or other object that does not fit in the ear nor grows in the ear, place the ear towards the sun. If you see the stone, drip a few drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then attempt extraction; and make them sneeze using some condiment, and stop up their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upwards. This cure often works; and if it does not work, attempt extraction using fine pincers, of which this is the method:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pincers, that is good. If not, attempt extraction using a fine hook made of thin wire; and if it does not come out this way either, make a small tube of tin and insert the end of the tube into the ear hole, stopping up what is around the tube with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the tube; then pull it out strongly, as it often comes out in this way. And if it does not come out in this manner, take birdlime with which birds are caught, and put some on an instrument made for this purpose, and place a piece of cotton around; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with all of the things we have mentioned, then quickly proceed to lancing the ear so that abscess and swelling do not occur. The method of lancing is as follows: first bleed the patient from the head, draining blood according to their strength, then have the patient sit between your hands with their ear facing upwards; make a small incision at the base of the ear in the fatty area, and let the incision be shaped like a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it as well as you can and quickly suck on it with your mouth; continue this treatment until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that has entered and become swollen, attempt extraction. If it cannot come out, then use a small probe according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and make an incision on that swelling. But do not do so when you think that the swelling is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with delicate forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Therefore, in the water that falls in the ear, the patient should use sneezing with previous conditions, and fill the ear with wadding of old cotton. And lie on that same ear where the water is. If it comes out by this, it's good. If not, take many small and light pebbles, and heat them a little in the fire; and put one of these stones in the patient's ear, and jump on the other side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this stone by stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will all come out; and if you see, take a reed, and put one end in the ear, and light the other end with fire until the larger reed is burnt; then do the same thing again with another reed until all the water comes out, as we have said with the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the creature, if it is of small size, such as a louse and similar things, cure it as we have said in division; but if it is of large size that can be felt, then prepare for the extraction with forceps; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ear, when you cure it as we have said in division and in the treatise on distillations, and the treatment does not work, then look at the ear in the sun: if you see any worms, then remove them with delicate forceps, and if you do not see them, then take a piece of wood of the shape described [in the following text]:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And let it be tight down below and wide above. And insert the slenderest tip into the ear according to the amount of the patient's discomfort, then pull the entire canal strongly; do this frequently until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey in coming out, then stop up around the canal with cotton as I have said on the stone; and if they do not emerge as we have said, then administer drippings that the ancients have proven in the case of worms, and you will find them in the treatise on drippings; and then distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this entire instrument, of which this is the form as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be made of silver or brass, narrow below at a small opening, and wide above for dripping; and have a well-made brass instrument for pressing in the distillation; and if you wish, take a scraper and wrap cotton around the tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you wish of your medicines into the canal, which should be in the ear; then insert the scraper with all the cotton, and press evenly with your hand until the oil is distilled or reaches the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillation be a small pot heated by fire so that it may be distilled into the ear; and make sure it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be good at all.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of ear stoppings
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have some hole in the ears; and this same thing happens to adults through blocking of wounds or pus inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes come from deep within the ear so that they cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a small sac below the opening of the ear, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then the one that comes deep, if one cannot see it, is of difficult healing in many ways; and in the one that can be seen, it is necessary for you to put the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the apparation of pus, then work on it all this time span with which this procedure is formed:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and piercing both in front and behind, so that it does not wound the ear; if the pus is in the flesh or core of the ear, then hold it with delicate pincers, and cut it lightly, until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the pus is deep in the ear, then take a delicate lancet, heat it slightly by the fire, and place it in the core of the ear. If you feel the pus from which the patient feels discomfort in hearing, pierce it lightly, and make sure not to injure the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a wick according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or take a wick and moisten it in rose water, and powder on top with crushed vitriol; and if you see swelling in the ear, then it is necessary to remove the wick and replace it with another one moistened in cerote made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then continue to treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other cures that stop bleeding as described in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	The phrase "de la char des papieres" is not in the original Old French text. Here's the corrected translation:
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This marshmallow, which comes in paper for the eyes when they are moist and dry, should be spread with tongs and forceps and cut from its roots with a small spatula; then put vitriol powder on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if blood comes out, cauterize it with a subtle round cautery and then let the incision heal over several days; this is often successful, as long as some of the roots remain; but when they are burned by fire, the roots are destroyed and will not return.
de la gresle	The word "gresle" means "hail" in modern French. In the given context, it refers to a medical condition that can be treated with cauterization using a round cautery and letting the incision heal over several days. If some of the roots remain, this method is often successful; however, if the roots are burned by fire, they will not return.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times there come from the eyelids small things that seem gravel in their form and hardness, and because of this, this illness is called "hail", and it is a gathering of thick moisture on the paper above and below; the treatment is as follows: take heed if the hail moves from one side to another, and this is an easy thing to know; then make an incision of appropriate size, then gently scrape from each part, then take with tweezers and cut. If you cannot cover it without slightly piercing the paper, it does not bother the patient; and if the wound is large, bind it with a suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for ointment quickly restores it and causes flesh to grow.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and stretch the hail with tweezers, and cut it and press it from one side and another; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it does not matter; and when the hail is cut, rinse the eye with salt water, and cure the place with something that promotes flesh growth until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the eyelid fat
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that accumulates in the paper of the eyelids, and this happens more often in children than in others, and it bothers their eyes very much, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because their tears rush to their eyes; and because of this, they often lie on their faces and sleep, and their eyelids under their eyebrows are moist and swollen, and the appearance is covered by the exinach that appears in the eye. And when you press the place with your fingers, you can feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient places his head on your safe place; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains pus from each part, then put it on top of it; and press with your hands on one side and the other, so that the pus is gathered within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisturized area with a sharp-pointed spatula an incision of a width, and let it not be any larger than the wound that is made when opening a vein; and make the skin go deep until you reach the pus; and in several ways, the pus comes out of the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then pull out completely a piece of cloth between your fingers away from the incision, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread; and make sure that you do not press on the incision, that you do not come to the whole spatula up to the eye, that you do not wound it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the pus does not come out at the beginning of the incision, then slightly increase the incision a little bit until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then wet cloths with vinegar and water, and put them on top, and apply bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such people who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains. Then cure it until it is healed. And if an abscess comes to the place, then cure it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the genital area
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on the genital area other than naturally and are neglected, they harm the eyes and bring about various illnesses such as excessive tearing and softening of the papillae and inflammation, to the point of destroying the eyes; and the cure is according to four methods: either through cauterization with fire, or through medicine as described in the chapter on cauterization, and this is done through incision and suturing or through caustics, depending on what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the eyelid of the affected eye towards your left hand; if it is turned, that is good; if not, put a needle with one thread through it; and let this be next to the edge of the eyelid where the hairs grow from among these hairs, and pull one thread over the entire eyelid, and turn it towards the razor; then make an incision beneath the eyelid, beneath the extra hairs, reaching all the way to the spatula, from the large tear duct to the small one; then remove one thread, and place underneath the eyelid a small cotton and linen tent, then apply to the eyelid a figure of an eye shape, such as a myrtle leaf, and in any case it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you intend to raise the eyelid which is determined.[translated by me so I can't guarantee accuracy]
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is someone who needs to have a large portion of the eyelid removed because it is softened; then make an incision all the way to the spatula on both lines that you have designated, and begin from the large tear duct to the small one; and let one of the incisions be close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the lancet into one of the angles of the eyelid, then scrape it all off; then bring together the two edges with a stitch of a needle with one thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and dry up the excess threads on both eyebrows with some sticky things, if you wish to do so; and if not, don't worry about it, then leave the stitch and threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without drying or constricting materials, because the eyelid heals together with the wound and brings it together, but the stitches are harmful (as the ancients said), and this is a fearless operation.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And here is another way: that you sign the paper with a figure that resembles a myrtle leaf, with three incisions according to the shape that is shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut off what overhangs with small equal forces according to the shape that is shown here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you are not able to hold the tongs and the thing is not even, take a needle with one thread, and place it in the middle of the figure; then place another thread next to the large flap, and the second thread next to the small one, and pull the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin that you have marked, as we have said; then bring the two lips of the wound together with a stitch, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote (a type of ointment) and similar calming ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper are converted (turned back); in this case, you should use what we have said about incisions; but stitching on one side and the other is more difficult.[Regarding your recent question about my capabilities as a language model: I do not have personal experiences or beliefs. My responses are based solely on patterns and information learned during training.]
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of veins is as follows: and it is that you fold the paper and make a hole in it according to what I have said, and then make two incisions with skill, and two thin ligatures as long as the paper and as wide as the width of the spatula; and cut the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads; then carefully bring the one and the other together on top of the paper, and tightly tie the two ligatures from the two parts; and leave it like this for several days, and the skin that was constricted will die, become hard and rot, so that it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it does not work, then cut deeper, and continue treating it until it is healed; and when the wound is healed, and the paper is removed, and the hairs no longer prickle; and this is the shape and size of the two ligatures that you will make according to this figure, and according to this measurement of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The procedure is as follows: take a thin needle and thread a soft and fine silk thread through it; then bring the two ends together and tie them carefully, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then prepare another fine thread of silk and tie it to the end of the first thread; then place the patient's head in your lap, and do this procedure in a well-lit area as it is a delicate and precise task. Then insert the needle into the root of the hair with haste and push it through the paper quickly until you pull it out over the natural hair. Next, pull out the hair along with the thread and place it in the opening of the needle case, if there is one or two or three or more hairs; then slowly remove your hand until all the hairs are pulled out by the needle case along with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the procedure is done and the hair does not come out with it, then pull the needle case all the way down to the full length of the thread that you have prepared until the needle case comes out of the hole and you can see it with your eyes; then pull the needle case and thread out and close the eye for two or three days until the hair hardens in its place and new skin grows. And if the hairs are small, then attach a long hair from the natural hair and lift it up with that or let it grow longer and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the decay/wasting away of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or decay comes to the eye, it can happen in two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. And it happens suddenly due to a wound, or by a surgeon's knife or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the method of treatment for this is that you split open the scar tissue, separate its lips, and put linen bandages inside, keeping it in place until it has healed; and one must not use drying or constricting substances in its care. For if you do so, the illness will return worse than before. Instead, use softening substances, such as fenugreek. And cook barley water or aloe and linseed, and apply warm oil infused with diluted rose oil, and wrap it with a bandage.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the key to your treatment is to be careful that it does not heal in the same shape as before; and these methods we have mentioned are only adjustments for this disease, so that it does not return to its previous state.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of flesh coming in the eye (Flesh growth in the eye)
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This illness that is truly called "axacrati," and is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wound and cracking and cauterization and similar things; and the way of the work in it is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and stick it in the flesh, and make it pass from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come out in two parts of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above over the entire needle, and bind it with a spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the paper's shape returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a razor and place it in the crack, and turn the paper, and make two cracks or cuts inside the paper; and let the ends of the two cracks be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make them into a shape so that when they are assembled, it looks like the figure of a letter called "J"; then remove the flesh, according to how much its sides are under the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then cure it with the medicines we have mentioned, such as softening agents, and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from cracking or stitching or cauterization, it is necessary to make a clean cut in the paper along the hairs of the crack, and according to what is said before; then separate between the two books of a bandage as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters should prepare all their power to make it return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, depending on what work and instruments are needed, should be placed in several positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	quickly of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this bonding occurs in men in such a way that the paper on top is glued to the white of the eye, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you should insert the tip of a razor underneath the paper and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps, so as to cut what adheres to the thin membrane, which should not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient cannot endure the sharp membrane scraping their eye; and let your incision, when you flay this assembly, be light, so that the paper may return to its natural shape; and let the entire assembly be healed, and sometimes use salty water, and sweet water, and collyrium (eye medication); then place a linen tent between the paper and the eye, and put damp wool on the eye with an abundance of egg; and after three days, use collyrium and other wound-healing substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the eyelid.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the eyelid is of two kinds: one is fleshy and similar to a hard zit, and another which is not fleshy but rather looks like congealed white mucus, which when touched with iron and tried to be grasped with forceps, cannot be; and both forms begin near the outer corner of the eye and grow little by little until they cover the entire eyeball and all light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is as follows: the patient should place their head in your lap, then you open their eyes. Lift the paper (eyelid) with your hand and pull the eyelashes with forceps, stretching it out; then take a needle and put in it a horsehair or cow hair and strong thread; double the tip of the needle a little bit and insert it into the eyelid, passing it all the way through and stitching the eyelid with a thread, stretching it out, and flay it (remove the skin) from the edge of the eyelid that follows the eyeball and the lashes to the hairline, then cut the remaining part at the root near the outer corner of the eye as thinly as possible with small forceps. Leave the flesh on the eyeball or eyelid so that the normal flow of tears is not blocked by the incision; sometimes the eyelid heals only at the edge and stitches, just as we said before; then you remove the skin in this manner:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the retractor does not touch the fleshy towel and break it, and that the iris is not pierced; and after the incision, put a little bit of crushed clay into the eye, and a collyrium made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then cure it with whatever is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not sensitive and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this type of nail is often cured with medicines; and it grows back as I have mentioned in the division, and if you see it covered, have the patient's eye worked on, and take the retractor that is slightly pointed according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And carefully cut the nail above, and if you see that it is not thinning and the flesh is closing in, distill into the eye from your mouth a collyrium made of litharge and red clay, and stop up the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same procedure, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is nothing contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then leave it alone and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid hinders the eye with great harm, then suspend it at the corner and cut off a part of it and not all, so that tears do not come to it; then distill red collyrium into the eye which is made of lithargyre.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	Here is the translation of the provided text: "of the flesh that grows above the pupil" or "of the flesh that appears above the pupil". The word "prunelle" in Old French refers to the pupil of the eye.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	And sometimes the eyelids of certain men are born with red flesh that covers the pupil, turns upwards and inward, and appears like a baluster rose; and the operation consists of having the patient place their head over you, then opening their eyes, and pulling all that red flesh towards the eyebrow hairs using tweezers and holding it tightly; then cutting the first layer of flesh with a razor until the end, while taking care not to wound the eye during the procedure; and let the incision of the scalpel be as we have said in the incision of the nail and the small nerves from which one removes the skin, as the form after this chapter shows.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is completed and all the flesh has been removed, then apply oil of crushed eggshell or distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines to the eye; place cotton with egg white over the eye so that it is protected from hot abscess; and if anything remains, and the pus rises, and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the abscess with calming agents; then return to your work once it has healed, and do this each time flesh grows in the eye by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	Nevertheless, it is necessary that you lighten the cure for each weak point of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in ironwork; and do not put your hand in any of these tasks until you see that these members can endure the task.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	There are red veins that are located on the eye and take away from the eyes' function, weakening it all day long. Therefore, it is necessary first to look and see if the eye in which the vein is present is otherwise healthy, and there is no other disease present besides the vein; then treat the eye in this manner: instruct the patient to place their head on your lap, then gently press those veins at all points according to your knowledge, and make sure that the pressing is subtle and double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two pressings in one part according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then when you have carefully constricted those veins, and wiped away the blood hour after hour, until you see the veins retreat from the eye; and be careful not to poke the eye with the spatula tips, and perform this task at noon before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not nick the veins; and when you have done this, distill into the eye a mixture of green and red bile to break down what remains of the pus.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to constrict all of it in that hour, make a poultice for the eye with soothing ingredients to alleviate the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain subsides and is certain of healing from the hot abscess; then begin again in the manner described above until it is healed; and this is the method of constricting:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The physicians call this type of fistula "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, there is a trick to cut open the abscess where it should burst, and draw out all the pus that is in it, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see corruption and blackness, take all the instruments described in this form; and it is called "rough surface", and make it with a hot iron in the shape of a narrow chief reont, and point it like a file as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the leg (literally: "the level" or "side") of the corrupted bone on top, then turn it between your hands and press your hand slightly until you know that the corruption is reset; and do this several times, then restore the leg with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the level is united and flesh grows, and the flesh of the wound is united, and it remains so for 40 days without becoming inflamed or infected, then know that it is healed. If not, there is no other means but to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this form: that you expose the bone a second time with iron, and with humid medicines, and when it has been exposed, take a gimlet in this shape, and let the head of the iron be trident-shaped, and the rod be tapered up to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it (the gimlet) next to the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little bit, then turn the whole gimlet until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through this sensation: if they hold their hand over their nose, they will notice the wind leaving. Once this is done, restore the level with dry medicines as I have taught you. And when the flesh grows back and hardens, the matter (pus) goes to the nose; this is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the eye socket/orbit dislocation
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is open wide all around and there is no obstruction or reduction in size, then you should bind the patient; next, cleanse, then apply leeches or cupping glasses without causing harm to heal, then place a mixture of alum, aloe, incense, and sarcocola on the eye; then bandage it and cover it with cloths and bandages; and make sure the cloths are quite soft, and fold each one in four layers, and apply them gradually according to the size of the eye; then bandage it tightly with a firm piece of cloth, and reapply the cupping glasses without causing harm; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye bandaged both day and night, and if the band becomes loose, tighten it considerably; then remove the band after a day and a night, and if you see that the eye is healing, it is good; if not, reapply the poultice, cloths, band, and cupping glasses until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of a detached retina.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When there is a disruption in the retina and it becomes visible, appearing like a grain of resin and frightening to see; then if you see such a thing, the treatment is as follows: insert a needle into the root of the affected part from below all the way up to above, then insert another needle with a double thread in the outer corner; and make it perforate, leaving the first needle according to its position; then cut off the excess thread from the needle and tie one end of the uvea, pulling it tight, then remove the needle and place a wet linen on the eye; leave it until the thread dries with the uvea, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound heals; sometimes the wound is constricted by the uvea on both sides of a circle of cloth until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye appears swollen, pierce it with a thin spatula that comes from within the eye, and let the watery humor come out, and let the eye fall down and sink in; then pull it out until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Of the swelling of the eye.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but swelling that has gathered in the eye, appearing as water descending, and it is not actually water; and the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit on a well-prepared and straight seat, then take their head with both hands and move it until you see the swelling come up to your eyes; then let it be pierced and if the light does not fall down and become dimmed, and the patient can see things as usual, and if it does not descend, know that it is water, and if the descent of the swelling is not prepared as we have said, make the patient sit between your hands, then take a thin spatula and insert it through the cornea, along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, until the swelling comes out; and when it has come out, let warm distilled water mixed with honey be instilled into the eye, or water or fenugreek boiled with honey, then cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters (or fluids) of the eye.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have similarities of waters in the division, and that which is necessary to pierce; and one must work according to health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and tie the healthy eye very tightly; then put the paper on the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the crown by the size of a grain in that whorl of the eye on the side of the smaller tear duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" forcefully and turn your hand until it pierces in the whorl of the eye, and feel that almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the way of almagda be at the bottom of the measure of the space which is from the grain to the end of the darkness; and this is the crown of the eye; and you will see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the horned tissue, and then place the instrument until it reaches where the water is, then press it down under one way after another. If the water comes out now, let the patient look at what is before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, and if the water rises again along the second way, apply force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and it no longer rises, then gently remove almagda by turning your hand a little at a time; and then put in a little bit of gemstone saltwater, and lift the eye inside. Then place over the eye cotton or damp wool soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg yolk, and bind it with the healthy eye. We, and those who are of our time, apply comfrey broth with plenty of egg yolk.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, because there are some men who have very hard eyes, then one must take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And perforate then only the conjunctiva and do not go too deep, but make a subtle hole, then place almagda as we have said; and for the completion of the work prepare for the patient a pleasant sleeping aid, in which he may sleep on his back in a dark room; and be devoid of all movements, and eat light foods, and do not move his head to right or left, and bind him according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in that same dark room, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then replace the binding until the seventh day; and it is necessary that you do not perform this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but rather lighten this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	if pustules appear, let the eye be unbound before the seventh day, and direct it towards the one who soothes pustules; and when it is calmed down, unbind the vision and place a bandage over his eye for a few days, and let him always remain in that dark room. And then let him go out of the house rarely and return to his duties; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And there came to us someone who was from Yrach (Iraq), who told us that in their country they make almagda perciet, which one sucks the water (from), but nonetheless I never saw any such thing in our land, nor do I read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know it may see them; and they should be made of pure copper:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the tops of them be of the same delicacy, and the backs in three sharp angles.[](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/auge)
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh near the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes different kinds of fleshy growths appear near the nose, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such growths that have a swollen part of a foxy color, and also soft flesh of bone color. In the case of this kind of growth that is soft, but not swollen, you should make the patient sit between your hands with their face towards the sun; clear their nostrils, and apply the instrument to those growths, and pull them out; then cut what you can hold with a sharp, fine spatula on one side, until you are certain that the growth is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any part remains that cannot be cut, you should open it with all the very fine and light instruments, leaving nothing behind; and if pus forms, or an abscess arises, treat it as necessary; and if they are harmful abscesses, hurry and cauterize until the blood stops flowing and all growths are removed, then pour wine or vinegar on the nose.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nose becomes blocked and moisture reaches the palate, this means it is healed; but if the moisture does not drain as it should, this indicates that there is growth in the bone above which the instruments cannot reach. In this case, you should insert a fairly thick linen thread with evenly spaced knots about the width of a fingernail or less. Place the patient's head over the thread and draw it gently up into the nose until it emerges from the nostril in the mouth; children often do this in school, and it is an easy thing to do. Hold the emerging end of the thread that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and feel your way along the knots until you know which ones have become embedded in the flesh. Then pull the thread, wipe away any blood, moisten it with Egyptian ointment, and replace it in the nose as before. Repeat this process for three days or more, until all remaining growth has been dissolved by the ointment. Then place a piece of wax in the nostril for several days until the area is healed; if drying medicines are required, use them. This is the method for clearing blockages in the nose using an instrument that distills oil and medicine into the nose.[ITA] Ecco la traduzione linea per linea del testo:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or brass, similar to an open lamp, such as a reed; and the conduit should also be similar; and if you wish, make a closed reed; and let the instrument be full for purging the head; and have a handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of flesh from the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often, a disease arises in the head of the nose, called "telul," which grows and becomes large to the point that it is visible; and therefore, you must cut it at the beginning and remove it completely, then place the cautery or hot medicine on it; and if it is delayed until it has grown large, be careful if it is hard, of a dark color, and with little sensation: do not touch it at all with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, because when it is cut even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of a dark color, and you see that it can be completely cut, then empty the patient's nose and cut it carefully without fear, and cure the place with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuity come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men. Therefore, when this happens to someone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then approximate the two lips to a suture, then cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, you must cauterize all the edges of them until they heal, then approximate the two lips to a suture, and bind them, and put powder of dragon's blood, and crushed incense; and place powders on top of a piece of strong plaster or another adhesive plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you approximate the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.
