To some men there come within the lips hard abscesses, similar to grains of pepper, sometimes smaller and sometimes larger; then you must turn the lips, and make an incision on each node, and take it with forceps and cut in each part; then apply the place after the incision of powdered vitriol until the blood is stopped; and then clean the wound with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a swelling of the flesh of the gums arises, which the ancients called "albulus"; then you should hold it with tongs and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood run out; then put vitriol powder or other drying and constricting powders on the wound; and if this flesh comes back after the incision, which often happens, then cut it again and cauterize it: for it will not come back after cauterization; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of "sordens" (a medical term used in medieval texts) - It is possible that this refers to a specific medical condition, but I am unable to find a precise definition or translation for it with the context provided. "Sordes" can be translated as "filth", "dirt", or "crusts" in a general medical context.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, accumulations occur on the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth become black, greenish, and gray, such that corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling; then you should have the patient sit between your hands, and their chin in your holy hand, and clean the visible teeth or the scabs until nothing remains; and similarly for the blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is there at the first cleaning, it is good; if not, then resume again on the second day and the third, until everything is cleaned; and know that teeth require various shapes of instruments for cleaning, depending on what the task requires, because the scrapers used to clean above the teeth have different forms than those used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary, when you cure the tooth of its pain, that you delay pulling it as much as you can, because one should not do this hastily; for it is a very risky substance up to the point where there is no excuse for damaging it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then, when the patient is ready to have it pulled, you must make sure that you identify the problematic tooth. Often, the pain deceives the patient, and they think the issue is in a healthy tooth, leading them to have a good tooth extracted; however, the pain does not subside because of this, as we have already seen done by some ignorant surgeons. Once you are certain of the problematic tooth, you must cauterize all around it with a strong spatula to protect the gum from all sides. Then, place the molar between your fingers or use fine-tipped pliers and gently pull at the root until it is loosened. Make sure to securely fasten the pliers, and have the patient sit between your knees so that they cannot move during the procedure.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth carefully without breaking it, if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and gently insert it on both sides to loosen it further, and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is cracked or decayed, you must fill it with cloth where the cracks are, then gently squeeze it with pliers so that it doesn't break. It's important to work very delicately around the gum to widen the socket and remove any remaining fragments of the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	I advise you to be careful not to break the tooth and leave a piece in the patient's mouth, as this could result in even greater pain than before due to the malice of the root. Also, be cautious not to act like ignorant surgeons who, out of haste and arrogance, sometimes break the jaw and do not address the issue at all; instead, they cause significant illness due to the remaining roots or broken jaw, as we have often seen. After extracting the tooth, rinse the area with wine, vinegar, or saltwater, especially if bleeding occurs, which is common. If that doesn't help, use vitriol and if it still persists, cauterize the wound.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments used to move teeth first should be long and have thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of thick stock so that they do not bend when pulling, and should be made of well-forged iron, and should have teeth to hold onto [the tooth].
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains when pulling, you should place cotton soaked in butter on the wound for one or two days until the area is numbed, then use tongs called "algefri", which look like a bird's beak; and inside they should be made like a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all those tongs, you must expose all the flesh around the root and place the instrument called "althali" there, that is, a scalpel, of which this is the shape:[translated] \_/ | | | | | | | | | | | | |
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the roots come out through this, it is good; if not, use all the instruments, of which forms are described hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one uses this instrument that has two hooks, of which the form is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other metallic instruments that are in front of the teeth, and of this instrument that looks like large pliers, of which the form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be strong so that they do not break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments that are not mentioned here. And the wise master skillfully finds his own instrument according to what his work and the illness indicate, for there are such diseases for which no instrument was taught by the ancients due to their diversity of use. And one does not break anything on the cart or other bones, but rather searches among the instruments that are needed, as I have said, and helps with gestures; of which the forms are as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and able to hold the bone so that it does not slip, but rather can hold and remove it; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines for this, and if there is rot in the bone and it is small, it heals with this entire instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, and similarly in young women, you should know if the tooth is not erupted after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and it cannot be straightened or filed: then file it; and if it is opposite to the tooth, take this instrument, which has the shape of a small beak, and made of sharp iron at the tip.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And frequently take the file and hold it between your fingers for several days because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file it with a file like this as shown in the figure.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is similar to the file used for making needles; and with this file, you should file the tooth frequently, several days, lightly so that it does not move until it becomes loose; then use a smooth plane at the end in order to even it out completely, and if the tooth is too sharp and injures the tongue, then you must file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not injure the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth loosen, either from a blow or falling, and the patient cannot bite down on what they eat without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines but to no avail; then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to realign the teeth, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the loose ones between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more than one, until you come to a healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering again up to the point where you started, and gently but firmly pull your hand until it does not move; and let your grip be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the loose teeth with pliers and align them, and place them between the healthy tooth and the loose one, so that it does not wound the tongue; and then leave it as tight as it can stay, and if it comes loose or the wire breaks, constrict it again with another wire; and let it remain and serve in this way all its time, and this is the method for aligning two healthy teeth and two loose ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place as soon as possible, as we have said; and let no one who is not wise and skilled meddle with it; and sometimes the form of a cow's bone tooth is made, and it is placed in the empty socket, and it is constricted as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tie of the tongue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes there is a ligament beneath the tongue, which is natural at birth or due to an accidental wound that has healed; and the procedure is as follows: open the patient's mouth and hold their head in your hand, then lift the tongue and cut the nervous ligament widely, so that the tongue is loosened from its attachment. If there is hardness or knots, which is due to a hasty wound healing, insert the unicorn (a surgical instrument) and widen the ligament; and be careful not to make the incision too deep, as the artery beneath could be damaged. Then apply a compress of rose water and vinegar or cold water, then place a linen bandage under the tongue. Have the patient wear it every night so that the wound does not heal. If bleeding occurs, apply vitriol powder; and if the bleeding persists, cauterize it with a ligature cautery which is good for this purpose; then continue treatment until it heals.[STHAPDA: This text describes a surgical procedure for releasing a tongue-tie (ankyloglossia). It advises to cut the lingual frenulum, the membrane connecting the underside of the tongue to the floor of the mouth. If there are hard knots or adhesions due to previous wound healing, it recommends using a surgical instrument such as an unicorn (a type of forceps) to widen the ligament and cut it with caution to avoid damaging the artery beneath. After the procedure, a linen bandage is placed under the tongue, which should be worn every night until healing occurs. The text also advises on how to manage bleeding if it occurs.]
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it of a bluish-black or hard color, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards blenchor, and there is moisture, throw the "oncine" (a type of surgical instrument) and make an incision with a thin spatula, and release it from one side and the other; and if the blood overwhelms your work, put vitriol powder on it until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you pull everything out; then lift it up with ease and support, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes there come within the throat growths that are called "godath," and they are properly called the "two almonds." And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is hard abscesses of little sensitivity and bluish color, do not touch it at all with iron. And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it at all with iron, for fear of bleeding; but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will be able to remove it, or it will break open by itself; and if it is of white color and the root is thin, have the instrument ready to cover (the wound), but first see whether the hard swelling has subsided and is calm. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his head should be in your lap, and the surgeon should open the mouth and take the instrument with both hands, and press the tongue down beneath the entire instrument, as follows; and it should be of silver or fine brass, like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And when you have pressed the tongue down beneath the entire instrument and you see the abscess, take the "oncine" (a type of surgical instrument) and insert it into the almond (growth), and pull it out as much as you can; and pull some of the pus with it, then cover the wound with the instrument, which is shaped like a pair of forceps. But be aware that the patient's teeth are clenched together, and one presses against the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of hard iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then take pliers, of which this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side, and blunt on the other side; and when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision rinse the patient's throat with warm water, and vinegar, and salt, and if there is bleeding, then rinse the patient's throat with water, or peels of pomegranates that are cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then heal it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses grow in the throat besides the two almonds, then cut them in the same way as the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and it had completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not exhale due to the passage that was stopped up, and she could not eat or drink, and she would have died if she had stayed like that for one day or two. And the abscess was so swollen that it had already pushed out two pieces through the two nostrils. I hurried then, and inserted a probe into one of them, then pulled it out and extracted a large amount of pus; then I did the same in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the probe into these abscesses, and cut off a part of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage of the woman's throat was unblocked, and she started to drink water and then wine, and I kept cutting this abscess for a long time; and the abscess increased again, and filled the space that I had emptied, so that it became very large; then I squeezed it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it did not increase anymore; and I left that place, and I do not know what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When pus descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below thick and round, it is called "eye". When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the chief abscess has calmed down, and it is fine, then you must make an incision; and the one that is rounded together and is not long; and it is blood-red or ash-colored or black, then you must avoid making an incision near it. Because there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to its swelling and length, you should have the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then insert the probe into the eye, and pull it down, and make an incision with one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. And you should not cut more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; because if you cut more, it harms the voice, and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed. And if the patient is afraid of cutting, then you must use a trick with cauterization without fear. And the manner of cautery is lukewarm. And this is that the patient places their head in your lap, and then presses their tongue with the instrument that we have said in the chapter of cautery, and apply live coals, so that it is not too thick nor too thin; and use the handle of this instrument, of which this is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let there be a hair on the head where the medicine is placed, such as the handles of a spoon, and place the instrument full of medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie down on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and cause harm; then keep your hand on all the medicine and press it on the eye, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it absorbed and the bites of the medicine have calmed down; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument full of cotton into the wound, until the cotton hardens on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall off after three or five days. And if you need to renew the cautery with the medicine, then renew it, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton stuffed with butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and let it be rinsed with cold water, and cured with gargling until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take pennyroyal and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and elder and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in one pot, and put them in a pot and boil; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot have an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And whether it be of silver or bronze, and one of the eyes be put in the patient's mouth until the steam reaches the eye through the canal, until the eye is made lifeless; then begin to frequently replace it, until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things can happen; and do not do it unless at the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and place an eggshell within the patient's head, so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the steam to harm the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with being healthy.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a bone or a fish spine, or some other object gets stuck in the throat; therefore, you must pull out what you can see, and press down on the patient's tongue with all the instrument, so that you may see the object move; and what you cannot see and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit, so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of napkin, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will swell up, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out through what we have said, take an instrument made of reed in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and hold the head high; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, that he does not choke, or push the bone in further; and it is better if the patient pushes the instrument in themselves, so that they know where the object is located; and move it up and down until the object comes out completely.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the throat's fat or flesh.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the veins are treated, as I have said in the division, with medical care; and when this does not help at all, then look at the sick person's throat in the sun, after pressing their tongue with the instrument that I have told you. And if you see the vein, then pull it with a tiny hook, or with fine tweezers that are suitable for this. And if this is not valuable, then take a live eel, and put it in the sick person's throat, then put a hot iron on the movement of the eel. And do this often. And if the patient becomes covered in water all day. Then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and throw it in without swallowing, and move it with their hand often; and as soon as the vein feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay. And the manner of fumigation is as follows: take a pot in which there are hot coals, and cover it with a perforated cloth, and the hole of the instrument should be in this hole; then put your fumigation in, and the patient should put the end of the eel in their mouth, and close their mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but reaches the vein; and the vein will fall now, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the vein, it is when it can be seen, similar to curved pliers so that they can enter into the throat; and it should look like a bird's beak, and have roughness like sandpaper, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and here is its form: [It is possible that this sentence refers to an illustration of the instrument that has not been provided.]
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many similarities of abscess are, according to what the following remembrance brings in this book, and they are different in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its own likeness, and those that hold moisture. And the second way is according to the locations where they are in the body. For the abscesses of the head are different than those of the bottom, and the abscesses of the fleshy part are different than those that come in joints, and each one should have its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is mature according to its completion; and there are such as must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it until it is entirely corrupted, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint have been corrupted, which causes contraction in that member. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the piercing until it is mature, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the bottom, so one should pierce it as soon as it is mature; and one must not pierce a grown abscess without completed digestion, except for those that are near the bottom, lest it corrupts in depth, and becomes elongated, and causes a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the abscess when it is mature according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the lessening of the fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the swelling and softening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the incision in the place where it is most dependent on the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the incision be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints, and near nerves and arteries, and in all places where there are no folds.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And in those that fold, according to the member. And when the abscess is in the fleshy part, it is better to leave the incision until it is strengthened after completed digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before this, the body of the pus will be elongated and full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will harden. And some abscesses must be pierced according to the width of the body, according to what is necessary for the member. And one must make small incisions in small abscesses, and large incisions in large ones, and many cuts according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses that require removing the core and covering it; when it has become as a piece of cloth, and is dead, one must do as with boils: and some abscesses are cut in three angles, and some are cut like the leaf of myrtle, such as abscesses of glands; and there are those that have a round cut, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who have no visible abscess, such as a mild subcutaneous one, should be fully lanced. And when the abscess is large, and has collected a great deal of pus, you should not remove all of it at once when you lance it, but instead remove some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, and remove some more; do this repeatedly, gradually increasing the amount removed each time, until all of the pus has drained out. The same procedure should be followed for those of weak constitution, women, young children, or frail old men. This is because the spirit may suddenly leap with the release of pus, which could potentially cause the death of the patient. Therefore, exercise great caution in this matter, and once you have lanced the abscess, clean the wound and check if the abscess wound is small. If it is a simple cut, then apply soft bandages made of linen or old cotton. But if it is a large abscess with many openings, then insert a tent into each one so that they press against each other. And if you have removed a piece of skin from the abscess and turned it back, then fill the hole with soft cotton or linen rags without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it and continue to treat the wound with ointment until it has healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs during your procedure, apply cold water and a compress to the area repeatedly. And if the bleeding persists, provide treatment and care, and use the powders that I have mentioned in this book. And if it is during the winter months, and the location of the abscess is very sensitive, then place tents and wet cloths soaked in warm wine and oil on top of it. And if it is during the summer, and the area is fleshy, then apply damp cloths soaked in water and oil or warm wine and oil for three days, as we have said; and then unbind the abscess, dry and clean it, and treat it until it has healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what should be universally understood in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one must proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here begins that chapter.[1](#myfootnote1)
des soros	I believe you are asking for a translation of the word "soros" from Old French. The translation of "soros" in this context is likely "abscesses."
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Where small abscesses of the head come, and they are of a kind that are in veins, as the hock of a chicken, and there are many similar ones. There are some that are fatty and such where there is moisture like pus; and there are others that are hard and stony to cut into, and there is no doubt if the artery does not oppose it. And the work of cutting consists of testing with every instrument called an "entromissoire", of which the form comes after, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, then one should make a slit above the long [vein/artery]. And when the moisture has been drained, then scrape off the skin that contains that moisture, leaving no skin behind, for it returns again when any is left; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who are on night watch will take care of it. And then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day, and on the third, until you are certain that nothing remains overnight; then cure the wound with a suitable ointment, until it is healed. And if the abscess contains a thick piece of fat, then cut it along its length; and insert your fingers, and scrape it all around, and direct all your effort towards removing the fatty tissue where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, then do as I have told you after. And similarly do for the abscess if it is stony, and cut and cure it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And cutting into a hard or moist abscess is easier, for they contain little blood. And some of these abscesses, whether on the head or where there is no moisture, and of these was one that I cut into on an old woman's head; and I found the abscess as hard and rough and white as a pebble, and could not break it; and if anyone had struck it, they would have made as much of a wound as if from a stone. In other abscesses coming to the head, except for those that come on children's heads and at the roots of ears, make the incision always in the lowest dependent place, so that pus can easily exit; and cure them as is appropriate.
des scrophules	"Des scrophules" is not a complete sentence in Old French, but it appears to be referring to scrofula, a form of tuberculosis that affects the lymph nodes in the neck. Here's an example of how you might translate a sentence containing "des scrophules":
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Scrofulous abscesses often appear in the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they appear in other parts of the body, and they are large and interconnected with each other. And each scrofula is specifically located within its own cavity, just like lumps and abscesses on the head, as we have said; and there are many varieties of these scrofulous abscesses. There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey health guidelines. In this case, if you see one that is well-disposed to touch and has the same color as the skin, and does not bulge out towards the nerves of the neck or the artery or the duct, and is not deep, then you should cut it from above, and scrape around each part, and pull apart the two lips of the incision with your fingers, if necessary, as we have said about abscesses on the head; and drain a little bit at a time, and be careful that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and make sure that the scalpel is neither too sharp nor cutting, so that you do not slip and cut something that you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut a vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound vitriol powder, or any powders that stop bleeding, and constrict the wound; and leave it for as long as the abscess has calmed down, and the wound has softened and begun to rot. And when the blood has stopped flowing, return to your work, until you have completed it; then see with your skill if there remain any small scrofulous patches, and cut and clean them. And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofulous patch, it is not appropriate to cut that scrofulous patch at its root, but rather bind it with a double strong thread, and let it fall off by itself without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the entire scrofulous patch, it is necessary to bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them up, so that there remains no excess because of the size of the scrofulous patch. It is necessary to focus on cutting the root of it and pulling it out, and sewing as we have said. For those scrofulous patches that have an excess, pierce where it appears necrotic; and pierce it as previously mentioned, depending (on its size), then apply dressings with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with a healing ointment, until it heals.
de squinance	The word "de squinance" appears to be a misspelling or variation of the French word "esc(h)inance", which is derived from the Latin "scrotum". It refers to the scrotum, the sac that contains the testicles in males.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the "tailleure de la gorge," but I have never seen anyone in our land who performed it, and this is according to their written words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinting, it is necessary that the slit of the throat called "epiglottis" be cleared; and this is not done with ease, because all the veins and the windpipe of the patient are closed, as is the case when they have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid suffocation which results from constriction.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to incise the epiglottis, it is necessary that we make a small cut horizontally, between three or four circles, or a small slit crosswise, between two of them and not in the cartilage.[](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cartilage)
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these locations are suitable for the incision of the epiglottis because there is no cartilage in them, and the vessels are long and far away from it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the throat to its full extent, then cut the windpipe until it reaches the windpipe; and release the vessels of blood, if you see any, and then cut the syphac, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe of the windpipe that jumps out through the ruptured hole, and by the defect of the voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed where there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the chest, and stitch it all the way up to the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) says that one should not do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the breathing has ceased.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, and thus are saved from death.[In modern medicine, this procedure would not be recommended as it can cause serious complications such as infection, bleeding, and damage to surrounding tissues. It is important to note that medieval medical practices may differ greatly from current medical standards and should not be attempted without proper training and knowledge.]
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And so the ancients ordered that the wound be left open until the evil of the disease has passed, and this takes three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they ordered to sew and treat the wound until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a damsel took a knife and plunged it into her throat, cutting some of the tendons in the windpipe.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called to treat her, and I found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had flowed out of it, and I realized that she had not cut an artery or vein but rather the windpipe was exposed through the wound.[INST) Je apris aucuns vaisseaux de sang et les li ligai; et puis li bailli a boire, si com je pus; et quant ele vit que je ne la voleoit morir, elle commencha a revenir en soi.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed the wound, and treated it until it was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and nothing happened to the damsel except that she became hoarse, and later returned to her normal state;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in the surgery of the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of jet, and it is common in women;[ST1]
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And it is according to two manners: natural and accidental; where the natural one has no skill.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And an accident is of two kinds, one of which is similar to fat from us, and the other kind is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery in us.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear, and one should not act with force except in the one that is small, and test and examine the entire instrument.[Translation notes]: "feir fuers que" could be translated as "act with force but only in" or "use force only in". The word "celei" refers to the kind of accident mentioned earlier, which is similar to fat from us. The word "intromissoire" likely refers to a medical instrument that is being inserted into the body.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it like our own fat, and if it does not bleed from any vein, then cut it as you would cut nails, and pull it out completely if there is any.[Translation notes]: The phrase "com .i. nout gras" means "like one of our fats". The word "cope" means "cut". The phrase "le trai a tout sa coife" means "pull it out completely". The word "sa coife" likely refers to the root or base of the growth that is being extracted.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And search thoroughly and treat it as appropriate until it heals perfectly.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways (forms) of us, of which I will tell all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now it is necessary for me to explain all the differences that exist between "nous" and "issue".[*Note: Based on context, I assume "nous" refers to a medical condition or disease, but could also mean "we." "Issue" could refer to either a medical issue or an outcome/consequence. The exact meaning may become clearer as more lines are translated.*]
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an "issue" is characterized by heat and fever that persist until the boiling (of pus) has passed and the decay is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the nose there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains one abscess, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a pimple and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they are of two types, either fatty or moist, and have much color as I have said in the classification.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of the nose, you should first test and inquire about all the instruments which are called "entromissoires," according to the form that comes in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiry for abscesses of the nose is to take the moistest place that you find in the abscess and turn your fingers back and forth until you are certain that the instrument has penetrated the core, according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the "entromissoire" and be careful that nothing falls out.[Instead of “ceu”, it might be more accurate to translate this as “from it.”]
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs and corrupts, whatever color it has, it swells up as I have said about other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the incision no moisture comes out, know that it is fat, then make a cross-shaped incision and use tweezers to gently peel back the skin from all sides and around the cyst so that you can pull it out whole with the pus.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot pull it out whole, then remove it in pieces so that nothing is left behind.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	Because if anything remains, the tumor will return many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if some of it remains and it causes you pain, apply corrosive powders to the wound and bind it up, then place a warm and soothing poultice on it to treat the abscess until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the wound is large, so cut the two lips of the wound, and clean out the flesh that festers.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if a pulsating vein is contrary to you or another, hasten and use the place of vitriol powder, and leave it there for two or three days until the wound rots, and let the boiling of the blood subside; then return to cover what remains to be covered of the new wound.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Behold the forms of intrusive instruments, which are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret," and one that is called "breb," and they are also of three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses or fistulas.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are similar to the needles used for sewing surplices, and they are made of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow in color are more valuable, and they are proven to be better at encircling the hollow parts of fistulas.[STH-13-95277 16:34:04.8] et sunt pur lonc et tenç; et s’en i a autres qui sunt courbez, si com les aguilles de chirurgie sont, por traire parmi l’os des espines, car ausi poez vous traire parmi le membre des fistules quant il est gros.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of ulcers are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are ulcers that have two craters of three kinds as well.[Note: I'm not certain about the translation of "oncines" and "corbeures". "Oncine" could refer to a specific type of wound or ulcer, while "corbeures" could mean "craters".]
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And there are ulcers that have three craters, and they are also of three kinds; and there are ulcers that have two craters, as well as ulcers with a single crater, and they are all necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these [ulcers] have cutting edges, and some of them do not cut at all except for one side, so that the nerve is not severed since the vein and the nerve are not cut.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these introductory [ulcers], the alumelles are arranged in bundles, so that the patient does not realize it during the incision of the abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and they are not used anywhere except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, ankles, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And sometimes, they make a small instrument like the scabs of abscesses in this shape, to stop bleeding:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And they place it sometimes on the wound that bleeds profusely from veins and arteries, and sometimes in this large shape:[img](![scabs of abscesses](https://i.imgur.com/1IWwvuZ.png))
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of men swell when they begin to become corrupt, so much that they resemble those of a woman:[img](![breast swelling in males](https://i.imgur.com/5jP072y.png))[source unknown][source for image](<https://www.pinterest.com/pin/548139666363565524/>)
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	"and they remain swollen and ugly, and whoever wants to cure them, must proceed according to the form of this line b to g."
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	"then remove the fat, and apply medicine to the wound, filling it with injected flesh, then bring the two edges of the wound together with stitches, and continue to care for it until it is healed."
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	"and if the breast sags downward and is soft due to its size, as it often happens in women, then make two cuts on top of it, similar to two slits."
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	"so that one extends to the other at the end of each, such that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this form, from line b to line g."
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	"then remove the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitches and powders, as well as everything necessary for the treatment, until it is healed."
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood loss, then you should fill the wound with cotton soaked in a corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it in place until it consumes the remaining flesh and fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses in the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.
