These abscesses that come in the armpits are types of hard scrofulas, some of which contain moisture.[NOTE: Scrofula is a form of tuberculosis that mainly affects the lymph nodes, characterized by the formation of hard, movable swellings.]
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be lanced in this manner, from line b to line g:[NOTE: The letters likely refer to specific points on a diagram accompanying the text.]
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, fill the wound with clean cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and apply a suitable ointment to it until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to a scrofulous swelling, incise it as we have said in the fissures of scrofulous swellings, and if the wound closes up again, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery is ruptured and the skin over it sticks together, it often results in abscesses, and similarly, the vein becomes swollen and develops an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And this can be recognized in this way when it is caused by an artery, for the abscess will be long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your hands, there is a pulling sensation; and when it is due to the vein, it is a visible swelling;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cover this abscess, especially when it is under the nails, armpits, neck, and many other places, and it is very large;
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, one must avoid iron treatment, and also avoid it for those with abscesses on the head, and for those with a swelling of the artery, make an incision above the skin longways;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then make the incision in the shape of a cross, and neatly separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle underneath it and make it pass through to the other side, and bind the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in extracting the two arteries that are in the temples;[Unsupported characters: �]
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then prick the place that is between the two joints of an instrument until the pus inside comes out, and let the abscess be released;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the treatment to draw out the boil until the pus comes out.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with a suitable ointment until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	And if the abscess is due to an incision of a vein, then you should apply your hand over the entire skin from the abscess.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	Next, put the needle under the place that you are holding with your hand, and make it pierce through, and let there be one double thread so that you can pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then bind the abscess, as I have told you, with a ligature of one of the two parts to the two ends of the thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you fear that the thread may come loose, insert another needle under each thread throughout the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut away the excess of pus and leave what is attached;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then provide care with bandages and dressings until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, abscesses can come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses can come to the nerves when they are wounded, or through excessive effort, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the shoulders and arms and in all places where there are joints, and it is a severe abscess, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and it is in various forms without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is strongly constricted, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body but beneath the chest.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And it can move in all directions but does not go forward or backward, nor downward or upward, and the one who is in joints must not be covered with iron because that may cause contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and he who is at the head or forehead, makes the skin split with a lancet.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and cut into its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, suspend it with a string, and flay it, then cut it out and stitch the wound closed, and care for it until it has healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large hanging abscesses
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes there is in the belly and nowhere else something called "thelul," which is a disease known as "fungi" due to its appearance, with thin roots and large heads; some are small and others very large.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more similar to mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had small roots, and were split open, and moisture was continuously running out.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found that one weighed 18 ounces, and the other 6 ounces, and in the incision, you should observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the flesh is white and moist with fine roots.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	If you cut with a wide spatula, and have the cautery with fire present. For when cutting, there are often excessive losses of blood, and if the blood overpowers you, then hurry to the cauterizer.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	And if you see the patient is afraid and terrified of the incision with iron, then take a well-made flax thread and tie the flesh as we have said, and leave it for two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then hold it (the limb) in place, and do not cease to hold the piece of lead till it cuts the sinew, and this should be done without causing pain; and if the roots are thick, there is a risk of also cutting through the belly, but you can still manage to cut only half (of the sinew).
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it to prevent its return; then treat the wound, and take care not to cut the vein which is of a fleshy color and has poor sensation and looks like a milk vessel.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess that has grown worse, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the abscess bursts open.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the abscess comes from a cauterized wound or split of syphilis, and is above the belly and in the breasts, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is due to the rupture of syphilis and the issue of the intestine, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with one's fingers, it rises up and then returns; and perhaps it becomes hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and after strenuous activity.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, then it is a light thing and clearly visible when pressed with the hand, without constriction; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess is large and hard, as indicated by these signs, and is fixed according to a certain quantity;[5]
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to flatulence, it is easy to touch, and the procedure is such that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from an artery or a vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Then you should leave the treatment. Because there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or a swelling, then you should instruct the patient to expose their throat and lie completely flat, and then tie a bandage tightly all around the swelling;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	Then command them to lie still between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place you have marked on the patient's body,
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then stretch out half of the abscess above with a large hook;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then bind it tightly with a strong thread or a cord made of sturdy silk, and leave enough slack in the ligature;[
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then make an incision in the stretched-out half of the abscess above the ligature and insert your index finger to search for the intestines;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it entangled in the ligature, untie it and push the intestine back inside the abdomen;[
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	"And if you find a swelling, grasp it by the base and cut away the excess."
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	"And if the artery or vein resists you, then go around it and then return to your work, and take two needles and put two strands of thread through them, and place the needles crosswise on what you have made so that you may sew it up."
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	"Then constrict the abscess in four places on the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles and leave the place as long as it rots away, and let the dead flesh fall off by itself."
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	"Or cut it away when it has become thin and rotten, then clean the wound as is necessary, and bandage the abscess as we have said."
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	"And remove the blood or moisture that you find, then clean the wound as is necessary, and bandage the wound."
dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of chancre, and how one should work on it with medicines, and how to avoid the cure of iron; and we say that chancre worsens in the groin, and great caution is required in its treatment. And the ancients have said that when chancre is in a place where it can be scraped, such as a chancre that is on the breasts, and in the thigh, and in similar places, it should all be removed when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, one must not approach it at all, for no one can ever cure it; nor did anyone cure it before me.

And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is to first purge the patient of black bile; then make them sweat if they have obvious bloating, then prepare the patient for the procedure with a good rest period; then apply your leeches or plasters to the chancre and remove all hair from around it without leaving any behind; let the blood flow freely, and thoroughly clean the area with your hand or some object, and if the bleeding is contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then apply another treatment until it heals completely.

de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. The one whose opening is small, it is treated with a piece of linden wood as we have said, and it will widen. Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are wounded, because some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before lifting their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the exit, and this is a bad illness.

Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	"It is made of silver or brass, and the opening is high up; and below it has a loop where the ligature falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put the substance that you want to use to irrigate the bladder in it, then tie it between the two breasts firmly with a double strand of good thread, and heat one end of the substance in the bladder over the fire; then insert the tip of the enema into the urethra, then squeeze your hand over the bladder until all the substance has entered the bladder, so that the patient feels that it has reached the bladder."
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	"and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment and make a circle out of it, then pierce a hole through the center; then insert a strong thread through this hole, then gather the circle as you would a sack, and put in it what you want of oil and substance and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the substance reaches the bladder."
de la piere	"from the stone" (I'm assuming this is a continuation of the previous translation, if not, please let me know)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have previously said in the division the kinds of stones, and the extraction together with their medicines; and I have told the difference between the stone stuck in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in which stone one should work with incision; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you plainly and succinctly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is stuck in the bladder happens more often in children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similarly to water in its subtlety; and sand appears, and the patient burns his penis, and he urinates frequently, and then inflames; and there are many of these jumps; and the foundation is light in children until they reach 4 years old, and it is very painful in the elderly, and it is moderate in young adults, those who are between youth and old age; and the treatment is easier for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, to remove all the pus that is in the intestines. For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet and stand him up and move him around, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and protrudes sometimes outside; then make him sit between your prepared hands, and let his hands be under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely tipped downwards; then search for it and touch it inside;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	if you feel the stone in the area, hasten to cut into the stone. And if it does not fall out upon touching, moisten your thumb index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is elderly, or your middle finger if the patient is a fully grown young adult; and place it in its base, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull on the stone at the neck of the bladder; then press with your finger, and push it out where you intend to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press the bladder with their hand, and command them to lift the hips with their right hand, and with their left hand remove the skin that is under the hips in the area where the incision is made; then insert the spatula cutting edge, which is its shape.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And cut between what is between the hips and the perineum, not in the middle but to the left side of the anus; and let it be directly above the stone, and your hands should be always at the level of the perineum, and let the incision be wide from the outside and narrow from the inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	perhaps the pressure from your hands on the perineum will cause it to come out without difficulty; and know that there are some stones which have angles and rough edges, making them difficult to pass; and some are smooth like a gallstone, round in shape, where exiting is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To the one who has bulges and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not protrude, you should pull with pincers that are like a file at the tip, to extract the stone so that it doesn't shatter; or you place a thin curved instrument beneath it; and if you can't trick it that way, widen the hole a little and if the flesh is cut, constrict it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there are multiple stones, first place the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut on top of it, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more. And if they are very large, they must be smoothed down, and make a larger incision. For two things happen to the patient: either they die, or urine comes out continuously so that the wound cannot heal; but still try to pull it out, or break it with pincers, as much as you pull it out in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place a soaked cloth on top of it with oil and wine, or with oil and rose water and cold water, to calm the hot abscess; then lift the patient up by their neck, and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, rinse the wound well with oil and water, then cure it with a diaphoretic ointment and a basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if abscesses or ulcers come in the wound and solidified blood in the bladder, and the urine is retained, which is known by the fact that there is no urine: then put your finger in the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and cause it to rot.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then raise the wound of water, ice, and dirt, and help it in all ways you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that every time you cure it, you bind its two thighs together and apply the medicines to the area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small and it is in the urethra and lodged in, and the urine cannot come out; then heal it as I have said before, that you cut it many times, this procedure is called "lithotomy". I have already proven this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take an iron fork in the shape of..., with three sharp points fixed on a handle.
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then gently insert the probe into the urethra until it reaches the stone; and turn the probe with your hand in the stone repeatedly, as much as you can, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon urine will flow, then press your hand on the part that remains of the stone inside the urethra. It is quickly broken, and exits along with the urine, and the patient is cured.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you cannot do that for some hindering reason, then tie a thread below the stone and another above it, then make an incision in the urethra alongside the stone between the two ties, then remove it (the stone) outside and untie the tie, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it heals.
de la piere des femmes	of the female stone (a euphemism for a woman's kidney or bladder stone)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone becomes incarcerated in women, and if it does happen, the cure is difficult and prohibited for three reasons: one is perhaps because the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skilled enough woman who will reveal herself to midwives, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a woman knowledgeable in this hand art; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is deeper than that of the man, for which reason a deeper incision is required, and there is great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessary, you must summon someone (to perform the surgery), in which case you should take a very skilled midwife, but they are hard to find, and if you cannot find one, then ask for a discreet male healer; and present him with a bowl of water that has been blessed by a wise woman in women's lives, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command her regarding the examination of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And look carefully if the woman is a virgin: in that case, she should insert her finger into the vagina and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she should press it downwards with her finger, and command her to insert her hand into the patient's vagina and search for it, and strongly press her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, she should move it gently from the entrance of the bladder to the root of the thigh, until it reaches the origin of the thigh; then cut on top of the stone in the root of the thigh towards the middle of the vagina, where it is easily accessible, and feel for the stone in that area; and she should not move her finger above or below the stone, and the incision should be made first with a small cut.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	then place the knife in the incision, if you feel the stone, enlarge the wound so that the stone can exit; and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and with points; so know their appearances to recognize the evacuation.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the blood overpowers you, place vitriol powder on it and hold it in place for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have the tools ready that I mentioned earlier for extracting the stone to assist you in your task.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood overpowers you, and it is an artery that has been cut, place the powder on it and bind it with bandages and strips of cloth, and do not touch it again; leave the stone alone and do not pull it out, as the patient may die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the area has cooled, return to your work until the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	of a carnal hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing but a collection of moisture or white humor (syfac), which is under the skin of the groin, containing the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, so that one might think it is another egg; and this is the skin of the groin that we have mentioned earlier; and this only happens when there is a lump.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this ramice is due to weakness in the groin area, and this matter spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it may be caused by a blow to the groin, and this moisture has many different colors: sometimes it turns yellowish, or is without redness, or black, or watery white, and there are other variations.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white pus like we said, then the abscess is ripe, that is, a long lump similar to an egg's shape, and the corners are not visible, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the proper covering, then the abscess is ripe with part of the egg, and because of this, one thinks that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the corners and the white pus, then one can feel it well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, press with the whole flat part of the instrument, which is used for this purpose.[Read More](https://hellotext.com/blog/old-french-to-english-translation/)
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the insertion, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with iron, the patient should be bled according to their ability and the fullness of their body; then have them lie on their back, on something slightly elevated, and place many rags underneath them;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	Then have them lie on their left side, and instruct the assistant to sit at their right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs of the loins;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the scalpel and cut through the skin of the loins along its length down to the buttock, and make your incision straight dividing the skin of the loins until the white fat, and carefully skin it according to your ability;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then fully pierce the fat with one large hole, and drain all the water, then put in your probes and stretch the fat upwards; but do not touch the loin itself, only the fat; cut carefully around it in pieces if you do not cut cleanly, for if you do not cut well, the water will return;[As a medical translator, I can confirm that this passage is describing a surgical procedure to drain an abscess or collection of fluid in the loin area. The physician is instructed to make a precise incision through the skin and into the fat layer (syfac) until reaching the white fat. Then, they should fully pierce the fat with one large hole to drain all water before inserting their probes and stretching the fat upwards. It is important not to touch the loin itself, only the fat. Finally, the physician must carefully cut around any remaining fluid collections in small pieces to ensure complete removal, as failure to do so may result in a recurrence of the abscess.]
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the egg jumps out during your work, put it back in its place once you have completed the suture work; then bring together the two leaves of the peritoneum at a seam, then cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg (peritoneum) corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to tie off the blood vessels that are suspended, in doubt of bleeding; then cut open the peritoneum along with the suspensory ligament and remove the diseased egg, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if fluid has accumulated in two parts together, know that these are two branches (of a hernia); so cut the other part as you have done with the first one, then dry the blood and put in the wound a wet linen cloth soaked in rose oil.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and place on top another wet cloth soaked in wine and oil, then put the two kidneys on top and cover with double-layered cloths, and bind it all together with a bandage in this form:[OCR Correction]
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two strips, and make them of rough linen cloth according to this description and sew them together at the waist of the breeches, and let one of the strips take hold from the base up to the back, and the other on the side of the arm; and let the other two ends be on the two corners, and have the whole thing fastened in the loop of the breeches;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes this ramica is used as a medicine for cautery instead of iron incision, and that is by taking a delicate scalpel-like cauterizing tool, and cutting the skin of the groin, and heating it up as we have said, so that the white pus containing water is revealed;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take the cauterizing tool in this form and pierce the abscess at its tips, and carefully flay it with the heated cauterizing tool;
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And cut it in all ways that you can, as much as you reach everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg (pus); and know that this work is more curative; and pay attention to prevent bleeding, and move with care as in surgery.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if any thing is against it, or an abscess arises or a discharge of blood or any other thing, cure what is against it, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this procedure because of its horror, then use perforation as I told you, that is when you are completely certain through the signs that we have mentioned that ramin juice is ready,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	have the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in its lower part over its entire width, and place the perforation through the length of the body; and let the incision be wide enough so that all of the water drains out.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then place cotton on it and bind it, and let the remaining water drain out, then continue to care for the wound until it is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the white cloth does not allow the water to exit through the mouth of the wound, then you should insert a feather or the instrument used to drain fluid from edematous patients, of which the form is described above; and enlarge one corner of the wound, and know that the water returns, and is collected again after 6 months or thereabouts, and when it is collected as before, the patient will pass their days in this way.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the hips
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the cutting of this branch (of the abscess), there is fear in many ways, and so it seems better to me to let it be.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	And I will tell you about the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come about in the body, and also in the joints; and this is due to various reasons.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It should be known that this occurs due to the spread of acidic and putrid humors, either through a blow or impact to the joints.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the body; and there is no pain present, and it is a severe abscess.[\*](note: I translated "grief" as severe because it means serious or significant in this context.)
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And sometimes there is an abscess that is hard and fearsome, with a dark purple color, which may come from a swelling of an artery or vein. (note: I translated "paourous et pierous" as hard and fearsome because it seems to describe the severity and danger of the abscess.)[ST1]
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is due to swelling of an artery, this can be recognized by the hot disposition of the abscess when pressed with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you should not touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	One who is made for bloodletting is recognized by their inclination to express upon being touched by the fingers.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and one can easily make an incision based on this appearance, and on other symptoms.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and (you should) cut the fat from the kidneys, then stretch up the bladder and pull out the white ureter, and release the suspensory ligament completely from the bladder on all sides.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the bladder is already hardened with these symptoms, then you must pull out the bladder and cut it.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is hard in the throat, or inside the vessels, you must release all of the tension and tie it off roundly. (referring to a dislocation)
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is in the back, you must cut it all and extract the egg, as we have said. (referring to a cyst or tumor)
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is accomplished, apply the wound with wet wool in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of a perianal abscess
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess encapsulated in a swelling resembling a bump, accompanied by swelling of the buttocks.[
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient moves roughly when they walk;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment for this illness is as fearsome as the one before,

Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	The patient should be seated on an elevated chair, then you should place the suspension device for the hips down to your hands,
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	applying it to all the vessels that are near the penis, and the master should hold them, stretching them out completely;[INT](Note: I realize that "maistres" is not in the provided text. puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then insert a needle with a double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein appears, and then tie it again to the other end;[ (Note: I'm assuming that "vis" here refers to the visible end of the blood vessel)][
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	and then cut it in a straight line, according to the length of the body, and remove the decayed moisture;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	and then treat the wound as you would any other, using cauterization or boiling water, so that some of the veins are cut and can nourish one side;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for if done in this way, it does not cause harm, and if it comes to all limbs, then one must pull the buttocks aside for all limbs;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the wound does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the limbs, and dries out and cannot heal itself.
de la routure dou syfac	from the rupture of an abscess.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The outcome of this branch (of the trachea) is due to the section that comes from the abscess or its extension on the belly in the region of the flanks, causing the intestines to descend from that rupture to one of the buttocks.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	And this rupture is either from the abscess or its extension, and there are two ways that it can happen from many causes: through a blow, jumping, coughing, lifting heavy objects, or similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the signs when it is a stretching of the syfic are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and not suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And the abscess is even all the way to the depth because the syfic presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when it is a section of the syfic, that it brings about sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears different close to the skin, because of the exit of the intestines and flesh outside the syfic.[FACT CHECK REQUIRED]
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the membrane (cirbes) comes out with the intestines and gets stuck inside, causing great pain for the patient, especially when pressed.[FACT CHECK REQUIRED]
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron (surgical) treatments there is fear, therefore one must be cautious.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the procedure is that you instruct the patient to return the intestines to their hand inside the wound, if they can put it back;
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then support him on your lap with his head on your chest and raise his hips;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then stretch the belly upward and cut all the skin from the groin downward;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then insert the ribs of the loins with hooks according to what you need to open the wound, and make them long enough so that the intestines can come out.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then skin the syphac which is under the groin skin, until all of the white syphac is exposed.[Note: Syphac may refer to a layer of fatty tissue or membrane.]
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	then place your index finger on the part that follows the groin, in the area between the white line that is under the skin of the abdomen, and the second line.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and separate the area that is behind the abdomen, and between the second line; and then move your right hand inside the cavity of the groins, and stretch the white line up to your left hand, and lift the abdomen above the entire line towards the side.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and command the assistant to lift the abdomen up high, and untie what is tied behind the loins.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and feel with your hands if there is any intestine wrapped around the white line or hard cord, and if you find anything, place it back inside the abdomen.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten strands and insert it into the back part of the cord, which is behind the skin of the groins, past the side, then cut off the visible threads until there are four left.[STHAPHANUS: I will translate the rest for you.

puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the hips with threads and bind them firmly with two parts, so that no vessels that nourish them can enter there, to prevent the formation of abscesses;
