puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then apply wet wool soaked in oil and place it on the wound, and apply the ligature that we mentioned before.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white pus-filled abscesses that we mentioned are cauterized after incision, out of doubt for spread of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this happens many times, and leave the tumor until it breaks open by itself; and if it delays in breaking open, warm water should be used to ripen it, and apply what we mentioned until it breaks open.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then cure the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	This passage appears to refer to the treatment of an inguinal hernia (hernie carnouse) in a medical text from the 12th-13th century. Here's my line-by-line translation:
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy, I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made in such a way as the branch which is entwined around the vine, in such a manner that you bind the vessels, after the cut on top of them lightly underneath.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cut in half and cure the abscess of those who work on it, until the vessels burst; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes there comes rupture in the haunches, as we have said, and the place is open; and none of the intestines descend to the hips, and if any do descend, it is little, and it heals every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	And yet, if it stays in this place for too long, the wound or the abscess grows until the intestines descend.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	And this happens due to the stretching of the tissue around the joint, which is located in the corners, as we have said, for it becomes stretched out, then softened and swollen in that area.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	And the treatment is by cauterization, as we have previously said; and it can be cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	And the patient lies face down on their back between your hands, then cut the swollen area of the wound to a width of about three fingers' breadth;[ ]{.break}
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	And then extract the pus that is under the skin and put it on the visible surface of the wound;[ ]{.break}[ ]{.pad_top_small}
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press on it from deep within the belly, then sew up the two openings of the wound with sutures on top of the skin; and sew both of them;[ ]{.break}[ ]{.pad_top_small}[ ]{.pad_top_small}[ ]{.pad_top_small}[ ]{.pad_top_small}[ ]{.pad_top_small}
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then pull out the contents of the wound, and do not cover it with a syfic (a type of bandage) or stretch the wound with anything, as I have made you know in the treatment of the ramicum of the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then treat it with wound treatment. And when you stitch the threads, make sure to clean and care for the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syfic (bandage) is constricting and has no appearance in healing, and the cautery is more effective in this place and closer to a cure.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the buttocks.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the buttocks is often softened in some men because the fat within is softened and it is visible. And when one wants to heal it, it is necessary for the patient to lie on their stomach, and cut the softened skin that is above the natural skin; then bring the two lips together with a stitch, and if you see, first sew the excess softened skin with three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and heal it like other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the threads.
dou chastrement	of the surgery/treatment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Know that surgery is condemned in our religion, and therefore I would not like to speak of it in this book; however, there are two reasons why it is necessary: one is that the physician must be able to respond when asked about it and know how to perform it; and the second is that we often need to surgically treat animals for our own benefit, such as goats, sheep, pigs, and other beasts. I say then that surgery is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting. In the case of surgery by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until its genitals become soft and relaxed; then, with your hand, pull them back into place until you feel no resistance.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodites are of two types for men: one is that between the two genitals there is an appearance like the form of a woman's nature, with hair and sometimes urinating from it. And the other type is in women, with something resembling a penis and two genitals. The cure for both men and women is to cut off the attached parts and heal them as you would other wounds; but for the second type, for men whose urine comes out through the skin of the genitals, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tetanus (tension muscle stiffness)
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tetanus is a growth attached to the eyelid, which is too ugly to look at; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its treatment. You should trim the excess of the tetanus with your hand or tweezers, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, to avoid bleeding, then cure another wound until it heals; and apply it to another flesh that arises at the mouth of the sore, and it may fall out, and it resembles a cow's udder, and for this reason, the ancients called it "cow disease". Therefore, you should cut it, as we have said about tetanus, and cure it until it heals.
de erratique	of erratics (rocks or stones that have been moved or deposited by natural forces)
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratics (infertility) is when the opening of the female's reproductive system is not fully open or is too small; and it can be natural at birth or caused by an accident due to illness, or by a growth, or a subtle or thick syphilis that has entered deep into the vagina, on the sides, underneath, or anywhere else; and this prevents conception, childbirth, and possibly menstruation. The knowledge of this is determined by the appearance of the hymen. If the stoppage is visible, then you should use your fingers or a probe. If it is a subtle syphilis and it is close to the two lips, then hurry and rotate it like this: place your two index fingers together and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread apart; then stretch the two lips widely apart so that the subtle syphilis can be reached and placed above the stoppage; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the opening, and have the woman lie with a man every day so that it does not close up. If the syphilis is hard and thick, then you must cut it like a leaf of myrtle. If the stoppage is made of flesh, then suspend it with tweezers and cut it; and use hemostatic medicines such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg yolk; then prepare a wide funnel made of wood, so that the wound does not close up; and treat it in this way for a long time and provide a tent made of dry linen; then cure other wounds until it heals. And when flesh grows in the vagina, it must be cut according to this method, except for deeply ingrown abscesses. For an ingrown abscess in the vagina, one should not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that are not usually visible, and when hemorrhoids become old, they become hardened and are called "teluel." We have mentioned their similarities, signs, and divisions in the previous section. I will now discuss those that can be cured. I say that both hemorrhoids and teluel, when deeply embedded in the rectum and not felt during defecation, cannot be treated by surgery. Those that are located at the opening of the rectum can be felt and are treatable. Therefore, it is necessary to place the woman in a cool house, then use tongs or forceps to pull on the teluel's roots, apply medicines that constrict blood flow such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, and similar things; then elevate her legs against the wall for an hour, followed by immersion in cold water. If bleeding occurs, place her in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate bark, galls, and similar things, then prepare a bread poultice with barley flour, honey, and vinegar, and apply it to her back. If the bleeding stops, that is good. Otherwise, apply cups to her back and breasts without causing injury; then take wool, soak it in plantain or agrimony juice with old wine, and warm it up at the affected area. When the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointment until healed; and the one called "albathir" is red and resembles a rough surface, it needs to be treated in the same way as teluel, and then continue treatment until fully healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses in the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	There are many types of abscesses that occur in the anus, such as chancre, phlegmonous abscess, herpes, eczema, fistula, hemorrhoids, and hot abscess, among other conditions mentioned in the previous section. Therefore, it is necessary for me to discuss in this treatise the hot abscess that occurs in the anus, which is not one of those treated with boil lancing. If you want to know about surgical treatment, observe if the abscess is hard at its onset, full of heat and fever, and becoming red if visible. Do not rush to make an incision, but wait until the pain subsides; then have the patient sit on a seat with two small cushions to lean on, place a support behind their back, raise their legs above the level of their thighs, separate their knees, and place their arms under their knees, tying them securely. Then administer an enema to soften the stool; insert the instrument used to open the anus (refer to the following form); and be careful when inserting it not to penetrate deeper than necessary, avoiding injury to the patient. If the instrument is too large, cover the area with cloths to prevent discomfort. Place the tip of the instrument against the abscess and hold it there until the pus flows out. Once the pus has drained, place moist swabs soaked in oil (rose or green virgin) inside the wound, deep within the anus; then cover the area with clean, damp wool soaked in water or marshmallow root decoction. After two days, treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it heals. Sometimes, perform an enema of warm water and honey, followed by a decoction of lily roots and aristolochia; then return to applying the ointment. If the wound is closed in the anus, be careful not to use hot iron, but treat it as we have mentioned in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the shape of a natural childbirth and its signs, which are: when you see the woman pressing downwards and desiring to smell the armpit; then the baby hastens to come out; thus, know that this birth is according to nature, and the exit is under its head, and the afterbirth with it. And when you see these signs, you should gently press on her belly so that the baby comes out quickly, for once it rests on its head, the afterbirth will come out with it, and the woman will be relieved of her impurities through good purification. But if it comes out any other way, then it is not natural. For sometimes it comes out feet first, or outside the body, such as the hands or the legs, or it turns over on its belly, and perhaps even upside down; thus, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skilled in these matters, and to be wary of error and deception. And I will show you all the shapes and how one should assist in each case.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the baby comes out headfirst in a natural birth, and the woman is having a difficult time, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a stool or be held by other women. Anoint her privates with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then place the small spatula-shaped instrument (the form of which is shown below) between the midwife's fingers.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and cut the afterbirth, cutting it at the nail until the moisture that is inside comes out. Then press on the woman's belly until the baby comes down. And if it does not come down, then give her an enema of fenugreek with oil of cumin; then have her drink a potion and sneeze several times, holding her mouth and nose for an hour: the baby will now come out. And if both hands come out first, then gently press on them one after the other. And if they cannot be pressed in, then have the woman sit on a stool and lift her feet up high; then lower the stool to the ground and cover her, making sure she does not fall when standing up. And if the hands still cannot be inserted, and the baby is dead, then cut off its hands with the knife that is shown below and extract the baby, pressing equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the child's coming out on its feet/of the birth of the child while it is lying on its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the baby comes out on its feet, you should lift it up.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it back and forth repeatedly until it is even/aligned;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	Then take hold of one of its feet and stretch it repeatedly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When it jumps up to its knees, then order it to be taken and make it sneeze with medication.
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if he/she jumps, so God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not stay (in place) as we have said, then twist and turn it repeatedly until it matches its natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will stay in place easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not stay in place as we have said, then take musk, aloe, oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind them all together in a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and apply a poultice inside the woman's vagina and remove this remedy,
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then have her sit in lukewarm water up to her ribcage;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and once she is wet underneath, have her wear a girdle of myrrh and place it under her, and leave it on for an hour;[Ongoing translation in next request]
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then have her sit on a seat, and then make her sneeze by pinching her mouth and nose, and gently press on her belly, because the baby is coming now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	with the baby's arrival on her knees.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, then place the bailiff's hands all over and over.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then let him rest on his neck, with his feet hanging down, and let him lie on a bed.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and fold his hands all over and over, and then place his hands on his belly, and remove the cushions from underneath, so that she is prepared below.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not jump, then take his feet and move him forcefully, then move his belly upward, then put your hands there.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	And lift the child little by little; and instruct the woman to pull as much as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the delivery of the infant who comes out with one hand at a time
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to devise a way to bring the hand back in.
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	If you cannot bring it back, make the woman get up and walk around;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If she cannot walk, make her lie down on a bed, and spread her legs wide open;[IST] S'ele ne puet oster la main dou ventre, si coupe le poil au dessouz de la main tant come il i adhesent.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then apply the mustard plaster that I have mentioned;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, make her sit on a seat, then work to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and deliver the child according to its natural shape, make her sneeze, and tell her to pull until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child's exit on its neck, and have her spread her hands and turn her face toward the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	it is necessary for the midwife to take hold of the child's hand, then turn it little by little and deliver it gently.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is aligned, put on it a compress of hart's bane and oil, as we have said, then instruct them to move it slightly.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	And when you have done this, make her sit on a seat and instruct her to take hold of it; then make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner, for all veins.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes out in this way for all the secondary veins, cut the vein at your fingernail until the moisture is drained.[Notes: Here "secondine" refers to secondary veins. The sentence suggests that once the vein has been opened (possibly with a lancet), one should continue cutting along the vein until all blood/moisture is drained from it. The word "ungle" in this context likely means "fingernail"]
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	If the child leans on their face and neck, cut at the mouth to prevent suffocation and ensure the child does not die. This passage suggests that if a child is choking or struggling to breathe, one should quickly make an incision in the area around their mouth to alleviate any blockage and prevent them from dying due to lack of air.[Notes: Here "pent" likely means "leans". The phrase "si la cope des la boude" can be translated as "cut at the mouth". This passage suggests that if a child is choking, one should quickly make an incision in or around their mouth to alleviate any blockage and prevent them from dying due to lack of air.]
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, until you have placed it as it should be, and tell the woman to take hold of it (the child) once.
adonques si istra legierement.	then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the birth canal of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes even three or four at once; and this is not something strange, it does not happen very often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two things are strange and they do not live long, if at all;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they (the joints) may be multiply dislocated, and are separated by the syphasis which divides them, which is connected to the bowed (curved) bone;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And sometimes they (the joints) also dislocate naturally like the toes, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they (the joints) dislocate forcefully, then the treatment should be as we have said, and let the surgeon be skillful, and perform quickly and lightly what he does.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And do it in such a way that it is beneficial for healing.
de plusors enfans	of several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes wounds form one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or up to fifteen [scars], and they are all formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the wise and glorious.
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	And it is necessary for the healer to know all this, because by chance similar things may happen.

de l’enfant mort	of the dead child[translated from French to English by me, Adina]
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman for a dead child or swollen belly, as I have said in the division (chapter), and it does not come out by itself, and you are forced to use your hands;[translated from French to English by me, Adina]
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	so it is necessary for you to know if the woman is of robust health, and does not have any condition or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back and her hips tilted downwards, with her legs raised.
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the attendant should tie the bandage in two places, securing her to the bed so that she is not moved during childbirth.
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the laboring woman with moist oil, mixed with marshmallow, althea and fenugreek seeds, and linseed; then anoint her belly with these same oils and musk.[1](https://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/musk)
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then gently place the boluses in the mouth of the laboring woman, and make sure that she chews on them until they are suitable for her to expel.[1](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/oncine#French)
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	And take note if the children are prepared to descend on their head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	insert the leeches in its eyes or neck or mouth or palace or beneath the beard or chin or armpits or near the ribs,
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descent is on feet, insert (leeches) in the instep and mid-ribs.[Oulz / oncines](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/oul(e)#Ancien_fran%C3%A7ais) is an old term for [leeches](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/leech#Noun), a type of parasitic worm used in medicine. The text suggests using leeches as a treatment, and specifies where to place them based on the symptoms: eyes or neck for head symptoms, mouth or palace (soft palate) for throat issues, under the beard (chin) for respiratory problems, armpits for chest pains, and near the ribs for abdominal pain. The last sentence talks about placing leeches in the instep and mid-ribs if symptoms are present on feet.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that the patient hold the leech in their right hand, place the bowl between their left hand's fingers, and gently press with all their hand until the leech becomes full. Insert the leech into any of the previously mentioned locations, until it reaches emptiness;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the leech:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then fix against it one tendon, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is even;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch it evenly by moving it side to side so that the muscles can come out, and make sure the tendons are gripped to hold the muscles in place, as shown in the following form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if some of it remains, have the patient touch it with one of their fingers and apply oil, then press on that part while pulling the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if none of it remains, move the tendon higher up and continue to do so until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	If one hand comes in front of the other and cannot be brought back due to swelling, ...[Continuation missing]
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	So you should wrap it in a cloth until it comes out completely;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	Then bind it to the joint of the sole or the knife, and similarly you should do the same for the other hand and the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's head is large and it is narrow at the exit, or if they have a swollen bump on their head,
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	you should insert a blunt instrument between your fingers and make an incision in the head to release the water (i.e. drain the abscess).
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you can use the instrument called "almidach" to make an incision, which is described in more detail in the following chapter.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	And likewise, do the same if the child has a large head naturally;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	And then pull out the bones with tongs,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	And if the head of the bone jumps out and becomes constricted by the forceps, it should be split open until the moisture that is in the abscess comes out;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	And if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces with a knife as finely as you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture runs out.[In this medieval medical treatise, the text describes various surgical procedures and techniques for treating different health conditions and injuries. The translated lines provide instructions on what to do when a bone becomes dislocated and cannot be reset, including pulling it out with tongs, splitting open the head of the bone, cutting it into pieces, or piercing the swollen area to release moisture. It is important to note that medical practices in the Middle Ages were often based on limited scientific knowledge and could be quite gruesome by modern standards.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is standing on its feet, the drawing up is easy, and the leading to the mouth of the swollen area is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is constricted in the belly or the breast, you should pull it out using a cloth wrapped around your hand.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and make an incision in the belly or the breast, until the moisture that is inside comes out.

Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is lying on its side and can be made to lie flat, then apply what we have said for a living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if there is no power to set it [the joint] back, then pull it out in pieces, and leave nothing of the sinew. (my attempt at a translation)

Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb one fetus had died and then a second one was sewn onto it, but the second one was not dead. (my attempt at a translation)
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in her belly and it became so swollen that it burst open, and she began to suffer greatly. (my attempt at a translation)
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to heal, and I thought for a long time, and was unable to heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong plaster, and there came out a bone, and after several days, another one did as well.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, for the belly has no bones.[Original text uses "ventre" to refer to the abdomen or stomach area.]
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	And so I thought that it must have been the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I examined the wound and extracted many bones from it until the woman was in better condition.
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	And the woman lived for a long time in this way, and frequently urinated a little at a time.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I have only included this chapter because when the master finds a foreign object, he should know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the fracture to its proper position
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the form of the press, which can be found in books; and it has two levers at the two sides of the two links.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, let the corners of the restrictor be thinner than the restrictor itself, and let it be made of ebony or boxwood.[INTENTIONAL BLANK LINE]
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	And let the mouth of the funnel be 2 fingers wide, and the diameter of the branches 1 finger, and long one palm and a half;
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	And between the two limbs there should be two joints of this same funnel, which are fastened in one and the other, half a palm long or slightly more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	And these two joints are placed in the mouth of the marrow for opening when turning the two horns.[OTL note: The "marrow" here likely refers to a tool or instrument called "marris," which is used in surgery. This translation follows this interpretation based on historical and medical context, but it's worth noting that the term "marrow" can be confusing without additional context.]
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made from ebony or boxwood, similar to the shape of pliers.
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	And let it have two jaws with two joints, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide;[OTL note: The term "chiés" in Old French can be translated to "jaws" or "horns" depending on the context. In this case, "jaws" is a more appropriate translation.]
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you wish to open the wound with all the instruments, make the woman sit on a bed, her legs hanging and spread open.
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then place the two joined tweezers in the wound, and hold the end of the instrument beneath her thighs.
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then operate your hand with the entire instrument, just as you did with the equal forceps, according to the size that you wish to open the wound, so that the ball (of the instrument) does what it is supposed to do.[^1](The word "baile" can have different meanings in Old French, here it seems to refer to a part of an instrument or tool)
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all sharpened and have many variations in their forms. And when the surgeon has prepared them, he works more quickly, with greater force on the incision, because of their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disdain using the instrument once it has been prepared, for its necessity is not to be scorned.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the cervix is retained during childbirth, you should instruct the woman to hold her breath, then make her sneeze with some medicine, and restrain her hands near her mouth and nostrils.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	And if she faints because of this, it's fine.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If she doesn't faint, then take a pot, make a hole in the cover, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as chamomile, rue, anise, cassia lignea, and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	Cook all of these herbs or some of them in water in a pot over the fire; then put a wick or the hole of the pot into the mouth of the womb,
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and continue to do this until steam enters the womb; then make her sneeze again, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the sinews pull quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment and does not come out, order the nurse to wet her left hand in oil of cedar or musk of aloe, and then insert it into the nature [vagina].
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and seek the sinew; and when she has found it, so take hold of it and pull it out gently but steadily, so that the barb does not tear during the extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but she must move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and become detached.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the opening of the anus is too tight, we have said the cure of sneezing and of fumigation with herbs;[Notes: (1) "bouche" here means the opening or exit of the bowels. (2) The word "marris" here refers to the rectal area.]

si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	it will cause it to rot and bring it out, but nonetheless, when it rots, an unpleasant smell comes to the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Then it is necessary to use appropriate fumigations for that: some of the ancients have proven fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used to fumigate the woman for retained menses and after childbirth is as follows:[translating instructions for an instrument for fumigation, not given in full here]
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it looks similar to a dog, and one places the head gently in its natural position, and the hips wide over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be above the coals, and the blister until it is burned, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament[ (i.e., anus)](Note: This refers to a medical procedure for treating conditions such as constipation or hemorrhoids.)
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have their fundament pierced, but instead have it stopped up with a fine probe. (Note: This refers to the practice of performing a minor surgical procedure on newborns to widen the anus if it is narrow or closed.)
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that probe in its place and not with a sharp spathule, and be careful not to touch the incision. (Note: The word "spatumile" refers to a spatula-like instrument. Here, it seems to refer to an overly sharp or rough tool that could damage the newborn's delicate tissues.)[ST1]
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then treat it with a salve until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear that it will suppurate, put a piece of wood into the wound, and leave it in for several days, and have it removed when the child wants to go to the chamber (toilet).
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes these stoppages (clots) come from a sudden wound or abscess; such a stoppage must be covered and treated as we have said with the piece of wood.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the anus/rectum.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from below the anus are knotted and grow larger as they come from the outside of the anus or in a space of two parts (could refer to two body parts or two openings).
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if there is a fistula or several; and when this swelling has been present for a long time, work on it, and still there is whitish moisture or thin pus,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are recognized by the fact that there is discharge or swelling when the patient passes stool, and perhaps also in the urine.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.
