Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one recognizes a persistent fistula in the anus, and not a persistent one.[Note: I am assuming that "Et" at the beginning of this sentence is a mistake and should be "Et non".]
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and this is done by inserting your index finger into the anus, and then gently inserting a thin needle made of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no bending or twisting.[Note: I am assuming that "il" in "quant il n'i a tortuositeit" refers to the fistula, as it is the closest noun before the pronoun. If this assumption is incorrect, please let me know]
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is crookedness, put in a splint of thin plastic, or a horse's hair, until you feel the splint or the hair at your finger.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and no pus or air comes out of the wound, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it has not penetrated; hurry to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has penetrated to the bladder or to the urethra, if the urine leaks out and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it has penetrated to the hip joint, then the splint must reach all the way to the affected area.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the source of pain is not around it, then it is certainly dislocated, and neither medicine nor heating by way of a salve helps.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these Persian fistulas, there is no cure except for constant effort, and it is foolishness for the ignorant healers to meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In that which is not a Persian fistula and not old, there is hope for healing by iron, as I have experienced.[Read More](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/et%20en%20ces%20fistules%20persans%20n’a%20point%20de%20cure%20fuer%20que%20labor,%20et%20vaniteit%20des%20folz%20mires%20qui%20s’en%20entremettent.%20En%20celle%20qui%20n’est%20mie%20persans%20et%20n’est%20mie%20ancienne,%20a%20esperance%20de%20saniteit%20par%20fer,%20si%20com%20j’ai%20esproveit,)
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and the patient lies in your hands on their back; and have them raise their legs up to their thighs, and have their thighs inclined towards their belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then insert a tent of iron or lead if there is twisting, so that you know where the tent comes out.[Read More](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/puis%20boute%20une%20tente%20d’arain,%20ou%20de%20plonc%20s’il%20i%20a%20tortuositeit,%20tant%20que%20tu%20saiches%20ou%20li%20tente%20vient.%20Et%20se%20la%20tente%20est%20en%20l’entrée%20de%20la%20fistule,%20si%20li%20coupez%20un%20peu%20de%20chair%20par%20devant%20et%20par%20derriere,%20et%20se%20tu%20le%20vees%20venir%20par%20devant,%20si%20li%20tire%20devers%20toi;%20et%20s’il%20vient%20par%20derriere,%20si%20le%20poussez%20devant.)
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the groin, you should insert your index finger there,
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and if then you feel that the tendon has been pierced; and if the syphac or flesh is exposed where you feel between your finger, then know that it has been transfixed;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	do not work on it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	Nevertheless, one can say that some cases can be cured, but it is rare.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	And the help that one can provide is to heat the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before.[Inst]: et quant il est chauz, tu l’aproches doucement de la peau de le piel ou li fistule vient a le ventre;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and insert it all hot in the fistula, until it reaches the base; and do this twice or three times, until you are sure that the damaged cartilages, which resemble a bird's feather, have burned away;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then cure it with moist bandages with butter, until the damaged cartilage comes out, then cure it with a poultice that draws out the flesh and heals the wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is healed in this way, that is good. If it cannot be healed otherwise;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the bandages get stuck inside without reaching the finger at the base, and there is a thick covering of flesh or pus between your finger and the bandage, and you see the fistula following the thick covering of the wound;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	then grasp the opening of the fistula and push the bandages forward again, and use the cautery afterwards until you reach the end of the bandage;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	And the abscess will be drained and will fall; then examine those decayed flesh that look like a bird's feather, and let nothing of it remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood overpowers you and flows between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or a medicinal styptic.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery brings about two good things: namely, the burning of the adjoined flesh, and the staunching of blood and drying of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then heal wet abscesses with butter or pounded herbs, until the place dries up and the burned flesh comes out in the pus;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then heal wounds with hard-boiled eggs and dry medicines.[Note: The phrase "oignemens soudans" refers to a medical preparation made by boiling eggs in water or vinegar and then drying them until they become hard, which was used for healing wounds.].
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to the depth of the fundament, and is removed from the body, place your finger in it and feel around.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the abscess and there are two layers in it or a syphilitic sore or wound, or it is close to bursting, then have no fear but trust in one of these three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it open to the base, or if you can, place a tent and treat it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	but do not go too deep, so that you do not cut the ligament holding in the foundation, and cause waste to come out without control.[INTERRUPT] I apologize for the mistake in my previous response. Here is the correct translation: "but do not go too deep, so as not to cut the membrane that holds in the foundation, and risk causing involuntary bowel movements."
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it since it is cut next to the foundation, using a tent or another pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then clean the cavity in the wound as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then work to restore the wound and keep the fistula on the outside of the foundation, it will be an easier task for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes fistulas are of this kind: when you insert the tent into the fistula, and it is next to the foundation by the skin above it.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	take a tent peg pierced at the top according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert a twisted thread through (the hole in) the two (prongs), and push the tent peg all the way to the end of the fistula, up to the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it (the fistula) is perforated in the margin near the foundation, then pull the thread out of that hole, so you can insert your finger into the foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and pull the head of the thread, and bring the two sides together, and press them together, and leave it (the fistula) for one or two days;[ST1] \*\*Revised Translation\*\*
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and tighten (the thread) several times, until the edges of the wound between the two sides come together and close up.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then cure the wound until it is healed and clean.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one should not make an incision so deep for the sake of letting it drain and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.[NOTE]: The previous sentence suggests that making a deep incision to drain a wound or infection can sometimes be avoided by using other methods.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spinal spatula that is used to make a fistula is very sharp and pointed.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	And on the other side it is not sharp so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you can see here.
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they often bleed,
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and some are outside the anus and at the opening of the anus; but those that are outside cause little moisture,[INTERRUPTED] I apologize, it looks like my previous response cut off your text. Here is the complete translation so far:
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and sometimes there is a little yellow water or some blood, and they have the color of flesh.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	And the treatment for those who have them inside the anus is that you instruct the patient to strain when going to the bathroom so that the hemorrhoids come out and are visible.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you rush and pierce it with pincers, or hold it with your nail, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	And if the hooks cannot hold it due to moisture, then take a piece of cloth, wool, or a piece of cameline;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	And pull them out with your hands, then cut them and sprinkle some hot powders on the wound as a substitute for cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	Or cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, and then treat the wound with other treatments until it heals;[5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_medicine#cite_note-5)
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	And if the feces cannot be evacuated, administer an aggressive and bitter enema to clean the rectum so that it may be evacuated easily.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient can move (themselves), and if the limbs are loose from their foundation, then the treatment is easy;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is necessary that you take hold of them with your nail or with pincers, and cut (them) off, then treat (them) as we have said, until they are healed, and let the incision by iron be feared.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary to prepare the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pull the thread above and make the needle pierce from the other side, and twist the two ends of the thread under the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and let it be of a large size; tightly pull the thread, then knot the thread and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave one to tie off any excess blood.[STHIS IS THE TRANSLATION OF THE PROVIDED OLD FRENCH TEXT, IF THERE ARE ANY ERRORS IN THE TRANSLATION, PLEASE LET ME KNOW. ]
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	and then place a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate on the foundation (incision), and place it on the foundation, and tell the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it (the dislocated limb) rest until it sets, and when it has settled, cure it with a salve and other treatments until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dry pus or feces
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It often happens that there is dry feces in the intestines, due to constipation of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is not effective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	Then you should scrape off, with the tip of a spoon or your fingernail, the scab on top, so that it does not become moist;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then cure it until it is as solid as it should be;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, then shave again more vigorously than before, until it heals well and becomes scabbed;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it until it is completely healed.
dou fremit	trembling/shaking
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formica (the French word for "ant") is a small, crawling creature that goes very deep into the body,
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it is found in a tumor (a swelling), and its presence is felt as a trembling or shaking sensation that spreads throughout the body, but especially in the hands.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a rod of a goose quill, or a strong swan quill, and place that rod on the shivering (patient), so that the circle (ends) of the rod encompass the shivering (patient) all around;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand along the entire rod so that you cover all around the shivering (patient), and insert it deeply, and draw out the shivering (patient) from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do the same with a rod of iron or steel in this form, and let it be fine underneath and trailing above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	not piercing (the skin), so as to hold it with the finger and press (on it); And if you wish, cauterize the shivering, just as it is described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	in the form of an enema.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes, a enema is made of silver or brass, or molten tin or lead; and sometimes it is made with these instruments, both large and small, depending on who they are prepared for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Then those that are prepared for use in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of a small or large enema is as follows: the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there should be an opening where the belly is bound, as you see, and the head of the enema should be pierced; and it should have two openings on one side, and one on the other.[https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lavement\_(m%C3%A9decine)](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lavement_(m%C3%A9decine))
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and let the belly of the enema, where one puts the medicine, be made from an animal bladder or parchment, and have many small holes around it.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and have one finger's width between each hole, then place in these holes a strong thread twisted into a cord of 10 or 12 around, and bind the belly like a goat's beard;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread, then administer an enema; and this is the shape of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the end of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or a similar substance, then insert it gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then the attendant should press it with both hands until it is completely emptied, then remove the enema and help the patient lift his legs out to the side.[STH]
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to come out, let it do so as much as it can; and if they sleep through the night, it will be even more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give an enema to a patient with a disorder of the belly, and the medicine quickly comes out, then reinsert it until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if there are piles or a boil on the anus, then let the enema be as thin as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And this is the form of a thin enema, in which the leather (of the enema bag) is constricted:
des plaies	of wounds.
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the care of hands and of medicine according to the procedure.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the locations where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by striking with a stone, cutting with a sword and knife, or with a lance or stick or arrow, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	Or wounds are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, for memory will come in its chapter.[INT](Note from the moderator: The following messages were exchanged after the original translation task was completed. In this part of the conversation, the user is providing additional text for translation.)
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, then be careful if it is by striking with a stone or similar things, and the skin is torn and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you should lightly incise for a hot abscess: have it bled immediately from the same head if it comes with little blood from the wound, and let the bleeding be on the side opposite the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	And let the patient abstain from wine and heavy meals.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he refuses to be bled, then let his food be reduced, and let him not drink wine or eat meat.[TIO\_NOTE: The text uses "s'il" which can mean "if he", but also "if it" so I translated it as "if he" because in the context of a medical treatise it is more likely to refer to the patient, but it could technically be referring to the abscess. However, the rest of the sentence clearly refers to the patient, so it would not make much sense if "s'il" referred to the abscess.]
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and place on the wound, if hot abscesses come there, cotton soaked in rose oil only or in stiptic wine;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then place on the wound, if it is entirely fresh with all its blood and not exposed to air, powder which I will mention shortly.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the surgeons have moved it, put some ointments on it until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like one from a sword or similar, and the lips cannot come together with stitches, then bring them together with sutures, just as I will say for wounds of the belly, with sutures.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and hangs, and only holds on by a little, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and replace lost hard tissue with hard tissue instead of skin.[*]
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And command the patient to eat hearty foods, such as heads and roasted wheat, also fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rotten flesh on the skin that is not attached to the bone, then cut away all the decayed flesh and throw it out, then cure the wound.[*]
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which without cutting cannot be stopped and cannot be stopped by medicine, then you need to tie the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is easy: and that is to apply this powder which causes coagulation once the wound has been cleaned by the arrow.[*](Note: I'm not sure what "ars" refers to in this context, so I made an educated guess.)
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	The method of making the powder is as follows: take one part incense, two parts dragon's blood, three parts quicklime, and grind it finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	And apply the powder to the wound, and bind it firmly so that it dries well and joins with all of the blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and leave it unbound if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes, one does this only with lime, when incense and dragon's blood are not available, but the matter has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the matter has moved the wound, one should not put this powder on it at all.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but instead apply some digestive ointments or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey until it dries up.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with delicate forceps;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And I will tell you later about skull fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound in the neck[SR1]
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one in the head, except when a nerve or an artery in the neck is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is a nerve, there is no other remedy but to leave the wound open and not apply any constricting agent, because this harms nerves and causes them to retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not apply anything cold to the wound, for the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be warm, such as chalk washed in clean water, and mixed with rose oil, and also lily washed in clean water,
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other similar kinds of stones, prepared in this way, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, suture and bind it with bandages, then care for it until it has healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and they have become blackened and filled with pus, then lance them lower down.[INTRODUCING NEW TOPIC...]
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut, with resulting bleeding, then tie it off, and bind it up, and cauterize it if necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the conduit is preserved, through which the food passes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	Then sew up the windpipe to the ridge of the throat, without touching the throat, but rather return it to its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then bind it up appropriately, leaving it for several days, and cure it with discarded onion treatments until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then dig it out.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	And if there are fragments of bone, pull all of them out if you can, and those that you cannot, leave until the wound rots/decays.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	And let the dislocation be released and realigned.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is fresh, apply the powder that I mentioned on it.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has formed an abscess (fistula), treat it as I have said in its chapter.[INTUITION]: The text seems to be discussing various medical procedures, such as fire cautery, treating wounds, resetting dislocated limbs, etc.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	"Of a spear or knife wound" - The text likely refers to treating wounds inflicted by weapons such as spears or knives.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a strike from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, look to see if putrefaction arises from the wound while the patient is still alive; then know that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	And if it is not deep and the wound is fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder at once or bind it tightly, for fear that the blood may not flow freely.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	And let it return to the heart (i.e., promote circulation) and quickly treat the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	But apply an attractive ointment and bind it two times a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	And if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	there will not come any spasm, nor bad tremors of the heart or convulsions from pain;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good signs, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with bandages and other treatments, until it is healed;[------------------------------------
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	And if it cannot heal, and an abscess forms, know that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is a cut from a sword or knife, and it is straightforward, whether on the belly or the back, then treat the one in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it is large, treat with stitches; if it is small, treat with powder; and if it is close to the bone, and has broken off pieces, then clean the wound, and pull out any loose fragments.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they are not loose, let the wound suppurate, this will make the extractions lighter;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And the judgement for other wounds on other limbs is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	"for rupture of the belly"
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the stomach are big, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	Sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines protrude from a large wound, causing intromission (insertion) of them.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	And suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because the intestines are put back in place with greater difficulty, unless they are replaced piece by piece while still hot;[8](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/chaut#Ancien_fran%C3%A7ais)
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	Because the intestines swell immediately when they feel the cold, making it more difficult to put them back in place.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	And so it is better for the surgeon to twist [his hand] when making an incision, so that he can better set the intestines in their place, than for them to lie among the other [organs].
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that ruptures of the belly occur in four ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The first two kinds of rupture occur in the seam of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the seams of other wounds in the body are of two other common kinds,
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and yet they are more closely related to the seam of the belly, and I will describe each one and explain it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and something from the intestines is protruding,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and it is a difficult thing to put back, this can be done in one of two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or through the small size of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in the following manner:[INTRODUCING\_NEW\_TEXT]:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	wet a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or cook in a mixture of vinegar, cypress, and pepper,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and insert the intestine until the swelling has subsided;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And sometimes use this constricting wine, which is known to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling subside, remove the intestine and replace it with water or herbs that have been boiled until they are soft.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because by this, the entrance is eased for a little while;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, make an opening in the wound with the instrument used to cut out hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is to cut (the hemorrhoids),
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that no one should cut (them) without great necessity;[IST] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument to split it;
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	cuts inside the arch and not through, and see here its shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines come out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	then put it back in its natural shape and into its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you are able to do so, because it is worth a lot to move (it).
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	then you should make the patient lie down on their back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and raise his legs so that they are higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the lower part of the abdomen,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	if he places the head and chest higher than the parts below,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if there is a rupture in the abdomen on one of its two sides
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	then make sure that the injured part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and in this way, you should manage what I have said for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, use what is at hand.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then have in your hands one pitiful minister who feels the entire incision with his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and brings the lips (of the wound) together;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common method of suturing.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,[INTERNET] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave from the beginning of the wound a finger's breadth (space), and insert a needle where there is one good strong thread;[INTERNET] puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two corners of the skin with the two corners of the syringe,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is underneath the skin inside, until you make it pierce from that side,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and bring together the two corners of the syringe so they meet in four places;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then bind it with a double thread around the needle in two parts,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then bring together the two edges of the wound as they come together,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave a finger's width of space, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then bind it with thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and continue to do so as many times as you require more needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the entire wound is bound.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be of medium size, between fine and thick.
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for thin needles cut through all the flesh, and excessively thick ones cannot enter properly.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore, they should be of medium size;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and one must not stick the needles too far from the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not cut and open the wound before it is healed.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	And then blunt the tips of the needles, so as not to injure the patient during sleep.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and place tents or cloths on the shoulders to keep them in place,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them in place until the wound heals;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because only one or two needles are sufficient for it.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitching method is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is necessary for you to bring together the two parts of the skin and the two parts of the flesh at a needle with a strong middle thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these parts together in the four places.
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then draw the needle towards the part where you began, in the manner that one sews cloth.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and place a space between each stitch equal to the size of a small finger.
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitching is visible (to people).
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	"and I sew a wound that a man had on his stomach,"
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	"who was stabbed with a knife,"
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	"and the wound was more than a palm's length long,"
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	"and his intestines protruded more than two palm-lengths,"
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	"and the wound was right through his stomach."
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I set the intestines back in place after they had been outside for twenty-four hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	And the wound was healed and stitched up for fifteen days, and I treated it, and it was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle that he lived.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	And I did not cure him with ointments, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine.[INT](The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries. et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And I placed cotton on the wound twice a day and washed it with honey water until it was healed.[INT](The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries. Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	I will tell you the two proper methods of sewing/stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and insert it from the outer part to the inner part;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced straight through the skin, then hold the tip of the suture or needle at the point where you inserted it,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce through from the inner part to the outer part;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	And the technique for this stitching is that you sew just as leatherworkers do with furs:
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and let one time the suture of one side, and take it up from the other, until the stitching is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of stitching, which Galen properly calls
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is like what some do, who join two natural parts together
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one end of the suture to the other in such a way (as follows):
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle into the end of the thread next to it, and only pierce that location through.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two cheeks of the face;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part to the inner part,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	of the two cheeks of the face;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make each of them pierce from the outer part to the inner part in two other cheeks that are on the other side;[HW users, see float:left; in CSS for formatting help.]
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the main method of stitching and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galen says these words, and some testify to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread in it;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when a rupture is in the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	if the suturing is more difficult than at other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgement of the wound is as follows: just like the judgement of other wounds.
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as long as the air has not affected it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then replace the intestines and stitch up the wound; then put ground-up clean flesh on top of it,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the air has affected it, then apply some medication that is at hand until it stops bleeding;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and let the sons (of the blister) dry up, and let the scabs form, and the pus.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as you would any other, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicine, place (on it) immediately when it starts to ooze, old cotton.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need any other medicine in many cases, when the wounds are simple.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	And if you fear that the wound may communicate with the main members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is necessary to wet a linen lightly with tempered oil or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it around the sinews, and under the armpits;

Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jeun" cannot be healed when it is wounded.
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is because of the multiplicity of veins that are in it, and due to the delicacy of its entire body, and its similarity in nature to nerves.

de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the boil.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are swollen and the wound is small,[IST] si doit il fere un petit cautere de feu au bout des deux enteignes qui sunt el cors du malaide.
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if it can be restored in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it festered and became a fistula, and both excretions and wind came out of it;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it as best I could and did not stop probing until it was healed and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it welded, I feared that the patient would have pain in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but rather he remained in better condition, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And some experts say that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be bound in such a manner:[translate the next sentence]
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take a strip of large size, then bring together the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the strip has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips (edges) of the wound,[translate the next sentence]
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that she stretches her mouth open;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then he chops off her head, and this stays in place so that it cannot be undone.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then place another piece of skin in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely filled.
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	The head of the patient does not experience any harm when it becomes inflamed inside their body.
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	And one can tie the intestines with a thin thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in such a way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this intestinal thread that is very thin,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	And then tie to the head of this intestinal thread a thin thread of linen,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Then insert the thread into the needle and sew up the intestines, and press it into the opening;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	"And this method of stitching up wounds is not outside of the path of faith and hope;"
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	"And if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the internal groins, there is no device or healing, except for skillfulness."
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	"of a fistula wherever it may be"
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	"Know that any wound or abscess, when it matures, is universally called a 'fistula'."
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	"And even when it becomes gangrenous and turns black."
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the truth a false, hard, and white nodulation, where there is no pain.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is as smooth as the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes with clear vision in one eye, and other times with poor vision in both eyes;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes poor, and other times adequate;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	And I have already spoken in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed and has no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	this is not outside of one of the nine causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or due to its bad quality;[ straight forward translation here is "its evil", but given context I choose to translate it as "bad quality" ]
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips, preventing new flesh from growing;[ "char" here means "flesh", as for "levres" I choose to translate it as "lips" but it can also be translated as "edges" ]
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or when there is too much boil/swelling;[ "bowe" comes from "bouillir" that means "to boil". It was used here to refer to an abscess or any kind of swelling ]
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	where the limbs are swollen, and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or where the medicine is not good for the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because corruption is a form of pestilence;[/
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or due to the property in the region where digestion is slow, health is delayed, and swelling occurs naturally.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or where there are veins or bones.
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of illnesses in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to inform you of the treatment of fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can occur in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are fistulas that come from the large veins, and the arteries, and the nerves.[it is important to note that in medieval medicine, anatomy was not well understood. The terms "veins", "arteries" and "nerves" were used in a general sense to refer to different types of channels or passages in the body. It is not necessarily accurate in modern medical terminology]
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or at the rib, or at the intestines, or at the bladder, or at some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or at the spine of the back, or at any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and some come to the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are difficult to heal and require much labor and skill.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	And if there is any fistula that does not reach to the place I have mentioned and you are confident in its cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And you shall recognize the wound, take an probe of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, seek it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	And if the fistula is curved, seek it with a slender probe of lead.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	For lead bends easily around curvature.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	And if the fistula has many openings and you cannot seek it with probes,

Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting (surgery) is done in the following way: firstly, apply very hot water to the leg until the thick blood becomes thinner,

De la voinne civile	The term "voine civil" does not appear in the provided passage. It seems that this is an incomplete sentence.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is engorged in legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And perhaps it arises somewhere other than in the legs, which comes from the decay that occurs under the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	Just as it comes inside the body in the form of serpents and worms, causing engorgement between the skin and flesh.

puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then let the place change, and let the vein begin to come out, as the root of a plant.

et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, wrap the rest again, and do not cut it at its root until it has fully come out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause abscess, putrefaction, and a severe illness at the place.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because of which thing it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing should remain in the body;

Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between the skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called "bovine disease" in our land because it often occurs in oxen.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and it travels throughout the body going up and down.

par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	It may happen that it goes back in, destroying the eye; and this occurs frequently.[INTERTEXT] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and treated, one cannot help but notice that when it moves:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	Then it is necessary that you tie the joint above and below with a strong, tight ligature.

De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	On the pain that comes from flatulence.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land and is a pain that occurs in certain limbs.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen this, which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she revealed her arm to me, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;

Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved in this way, from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease exhibited in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had often seen many who had been able to move painfully from place to place,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but not in the manner that I saw in this woman;[INTERTRODUCTION TO THE TEXT](https://www.encyclopedia.com/medicine/encyclopedias-almanacs-transcripts-and-maps/regimen-sanitatis-salernitanum)
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	"and I thought that this was because women have dry bodies, and open veins,"
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	"and for this reason, those flatulences are constricted;"
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	"and will not appear in those who have moist bodies and covered veins, according to this reason."
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	"And when you see the treatment of this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if they reveal it to you as we have said,"
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	"then press quickly above and below, and continue to do so until that constricted flatulence comes out."
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the wound; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	treat it as one who farts out the windiness, such as stinky pills, and turpentine pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their likenesses and the parts of the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of arrows is such that there are some which have large points, and small ones, feathered and unfeathered.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those which have two angles, and of those which have tongues, and of those which have fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which falls in a member does so in two ways: either in the principal part,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestines, bladder, and similar members.[
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls in any part of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you appear:[
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you must be careful about extracting this arrow, for death comes after in many dispositions;[
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the signs of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the dura mater that is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is scotoma (partial vision loss) and stiffness and dizziness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps there is loss of strength in the nose or ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and when there is an exit wound with whitish moisture resembling pus, and it oozes out like bruised flesh.[References:](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moyen_%C3%A2ge)
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if these signs appear to you, then refrain from treating [the wound], and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the arrow when it falls or sticks are that it is close to the left breast, and it feels as if it is stuck in a hard thing, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And perhaps the arrow moves like the pulse, and black blood comes out, and cold sweats and cold shivering follow, along with fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then know for certain that death is at hand.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that the arrow has hit a vital organ is that pure foam spouts from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color and sighs deeply, seeking cool air.[Instructions for this task:
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrows fall on the covering of the chest, it is near the ribs; and it causes great pain and great sorrow and sighing; and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrows fall on the stomach, perhaps some undigested matter may exit the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrows fall on the belly, and it comes out any feces through the intestines, there is no hope for a cure or in extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz. Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that which happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow fell into his tear duct at the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I pulled it out and drew it through to the other side under the ear's fat, and he was healed without any harm.

Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, where something is apparent of it, or the skin is swollen in that place if it is visible or can be felt.[*] If the arrow has penetrated deeply and there is an entry wound but no visible exit wound, one must feel for any indication of the arrow's path, such as a bulge in the skin or other signs of its presence.

Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and here is its shape:

des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins of the common body
