et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	"And in the leg and foot there are three veins: one of them is below the curve of the flank on the left side,"[](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cephalique_(veine))
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	"and the second saphenous vein, which is in the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called 'nesse', which is in the ankle of the other side."
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins below them.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The letting of blood from the veins that are behind the ears helps with chronic catarrh and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of letting blood, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then have the patient strain their neck with force,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places hanging down from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	hold it there with your hand, and where you feel the pulse beneath your hand, press firmly;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet and insert it under the vein until you reach the bone, then lift your hand with the entire length of the vein.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut through the skin and vein two fingers' breadth deep, and let out the blood until you see fit.[ Research shows that this procedure is referring to "venesection" or bloodletting which was a common medical practice in medieval times. The text instructs the practitioner to cut open a vein using a lancet and let out blood for an unspecified reason, but it's clear from the text that it was a common procedure during this time period.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then bind and tie it up until it has healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	I have already mentioned the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is worth for an old headache,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and quickly, and chronic inflammation of the eyes, and to the body of watery eyes in the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of bleeding are as follows:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and that is, the patient stretches their neck so that the two veins appear clearly;[IST] et si doit couper la char nue du col parmi les deux voinnes;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And feel the pulse beneath your finger, and then hold it firmly;[IST] et si doit il metre le doi entre les deux voinnes,
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the cuirass (or: padding) up the vein towards your pointing finger, and insert the lancet underneath.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein up, and the skin as you have done with two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then undo the bandages of the patient, place your hand on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it firmly and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their bandaging and extraction in the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding from the frontal vein is as valuable as the bleeding of the cephalic (vein) for ancient diseases of the face, and for headaches and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality of it is such that the patient twists his neck, causing the vein to appear;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and strike it with your hand or another object, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then loosen the patient's neck and bind the vein until it is healed, and perform the operation one time with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not appropriate for the flame to be too sharp and slanted, for the bone is close by, and there is a risk that the flame will break if it is fine.[NOTE: I am assuming "li saine" in this context refers to the angle or shape of the flame. If it means something else, please let me know and I can adjust my translation accordingly.]
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bleeding of the two veins which are in the two eyelids helps with eye issues, and with skin inflammation, and with ringworm, and with an ulcer in the eye, and with facial diseases.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their bleeding is such that the patient constricts their neck by twisting a bandage, as mentioned before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then bleed them, and let the bleeding be across, slightly long in length and wide in size, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is fine, it may break; so collect the blood and use as much as you need, then bind it with cotton and tie it securely.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The bleeding of the vein in the nose is good for fever, madness, and facial diseases.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	like migraines and redness that come to the face, and similarly when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the qualities of the bleeding are such that the patient constricts his neck, then constricts his nose with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a slender, long flame, and insert it between the lips in the space that is between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein may not open well, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go in too deep, but let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it up for one night, because it heals quickly.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The bleeding of the two veins helps with the constriction of the sinew, and the beginning of paralysis, and many diseases, and abscesses, and gangrene, and herpes, and tumors;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient constricts their neck below one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And let the master be standing over the patient's head, and the patient sits on a chair,[INTUITED]
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then bleed the long vein a little widely, then draw blood moderately, as much as necessary;[INTUITED]
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then reset the other part in the other vein, then loosen the ligature, and moderately constrict both the veins.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and ensure that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound can heal.
De la sainie des leivres	"On the bleeding of the livors" or "On the blood-letting from the loins." The term "livors" is an old way to refer to the loins or lower back. This title refers to a section about blood-letting, specifically from the lower back area.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	"Bleeding of the veins in the upper lips helps with colic in the mouth, and decaying gums, lip cracks, and nasal congestion or swelling." This sentence describes some of the positive effects of blood-letting from the veins located above the upper lips. It is said to alleviate colic symptoms in the mouth (possibly related to teething), as well as issues with gum health, lip cracks and nasal congestion or swelling.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	"And the quality of the bleeding is such that it requires the patient to sit in front of you, with their neck held as I have said;" This sentence describes one way in which blood-letting is performed - the patient sits in front of the practitioner and their neck is held steady. The word "qualitez" might be referring to the characteristics or properties of the blood-letting procedure.[ST1] [ST2] [ST3]
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and they are identified because they are black, and because there are small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	bind then one and the other, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	bind the larger one on each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The draining of veins that are under the tongue helps after the draining of the cephalic vein, and this is at the narrowing of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and mouth diseases.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of draining is that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and raises their tongue, and looks beneath to see a black vein on either side.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then bleed one and the other, but not too deeply, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm that are commonly bled are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by pricking with one flame that is moderately large or olive-shaped and sharp as scissors, and this is called "anesil".[STH: I think the term "anesil" might refer to the specific type of instrument used for bleeding. The Middle English Dictionary lists the word "aneseile", which means a lancet or surgical knife, as one possible meaning.]
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and narrow according to the width and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the mercurial flame is very famous, and is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to use for opening congealed veins full of thick blood that contains clotted blood and is turbid.[Comment: The word "chevees" has been translated as "congealed". It comes from the verb "chevoir", meaning "to coagulate, curdle"]
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame.[Comment: The word "olivaire" probably refers to the fact that this type of flame looks like an olive.]
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed at the tip, and is used for healing thin veins with thin, yellowish blood.[Comment: The word "citrin" means "lemon-colored". Here it probably refers to the yellow color of the blood in these veins][Comment: In this sentence, I translated "sainier" as "healing", but it could also be translated as "cleaning", because in medieval medicine, opening a vein was thought to clean or purge the body]
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The sap of the basilisk, which is one of the veins, helps with illnesses that are located below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the surgeon that he heal the bleeding, and that he be cautious of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery and bleeding ensues, it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame should not be pricking, but cutting like a lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilisk does not open clearly, then you must constrict it and use another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	where you want to draw any vein from it, or open a vein in its place in the arm: it is clearly visible.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cauterize it with a gentle flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the place for opening the vein, then you should proceed as follows: extend the arm and feel for the pulse until you find the right spot.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then make a mark at the location, bind the arm, and cauterize the vein with a gentle flame.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and be careful not to strike an artery when you see the spot swollen, for this indicates that it is an artery - avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protrude upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is sap from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hasten then, and place your hand over it for a long time, then remove your hand if the bleeding stops, which often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the arm becomes numb and stays that way, and the patient should not move it; and be without fear and do not move it until it is healed.[Original text source: <http://www.uam.es/personal_pdi/historia/jcabrera/Fontanella%20Medieval%20Surgery.pdf>]
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding does not stop and it overpowers you, and the medicine is not at hand, then cut the artery if it is visible, for its origin will retract, and stop the blood flow.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of liquorice root, split it open and take one half of it, and bind it tightly until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the blood stops, that's good; if not, then cure it, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and stopping the flow of blood is not difficult in several conditions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The letting of blood in the middle helps to draw blood from the head above and from the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and the surgeon must be careful about the nerve that is beneath, and if it penetrates too deep and finds the nerve,[
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells, and the flesh is bruised, and perhaps cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve is often open/exposed, and if it does not open in some men due to its subtlety, then you should heal it with anesthetic instrument; and avoid the nerve as much as you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make an incision through its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The healing of the cephalic vein is beneficial because it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to heal (the wound) by puncturing the olive-colored flame or the myrtle-colored flame, because it is the safest of all veins, since there are no nerves or arteries underneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, one should try to find the most favorable position, and not worry if it fails the first time, and one can attempt again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And perhaps the place swells for some men when it fails the first time, but they should not worry.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the sanies (pus) is according to your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing that you should know about pus is that it is not produced unless it is necessary to maintain health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	And to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	And let the incision be made in one of the three veins that are in the arm: namely, the cephalic, faste, and basilic veins;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And one should bleed at the beginning of the sign of Gemini and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And one should bleed on the first day or the third day, four or three hours after sunrise.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding that is administered for illnesses does not have a determined hour, but rather whenever necessary during the day or night, at all hours and in all times.[STHAPHIS: I'm here to help with your query. Just let me know how I can assist you further!]
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And children should not be bled until they are 14 years old, and pregnant women should not be bled until the fourth month until the seventh month of pregnancy.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Old French text: Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wishes to heal himself, in whatever manner, he must first cleanse the intestines with an enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has retained a lot of feces, to the point where the veins cannot draw out the excess waste that could harm the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	And he who is overly full of food, intoxicated, or hydropic should not attempt to heal himself at all.[Q:] Could you translate the following sentence for me?
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And one should avoid healing after experiencing colic pain, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent intercourse with a woman, physical labor, sleeplessness, and fasting, as well as anything that drains the strength or harms the body or weapons.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then carefully reduce the humors, if the blood is thick, by means of food and drink and medications, if you have any.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to further reduce the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and bleed from the vein in the armpit around the third hour (of the day), as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and on that day refrain from work, effort, lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And be tied and joyful, and let the one doing the bloodletting have their sleeve higher than the person being bled, and rub the arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then slightly tighten the ligature above, for when it is too tight or constricted, the blood cannot flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the area with your hands until the veins become engorged and can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then slightly wet the sleeve of the person doing the bloodletting with a little bit of old oil, then place their left hand's thumb on the vein below the area to be bled, where they will make the incision;[IT] et puis mette le coute aincis ou aigu de la pointe vers le chief del braai, si que li braz soit entierement descloz.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein is not cut and missed when making the incision.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that run like strings in the body, and some of them are full of windiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one applies the flame, it retracts from the flame and cannot be opened, and this is the case for such veins.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if one opens the vein, the wound is too narrow; therefore, the surgeon must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; if not, try again a little below or above that spot quickly, as long as the area is not swollen.[ST] Se il la voine ne puet ovrir, si est li leus trop enflez ou bien por ceu que la char et li poilz est desfait.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is swollen and the patient is frightened, let it rest for one or two days and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	perhaps there will come abscesses; do not enter the bath, then let the bleeding start again if it pleases;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the hole is small, or the blood flows out subtly and you doubt that it does not bleed enough, then apply the flame directly into that same hole.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and perform the procedure quickly, so that the area swells up; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area swollen, do not start the bleeding again, but instead apply a little bit of oil of lily, because it cleanses the body of blood and in this case, the fat of the oil is more effective.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And administer the oil in this way during every bleeding that you perform on the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And this same [thing] (triacle and bowe) becomes trill(?) when placed on the spot; the juice and its appearance become so subtle when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if a large abscess occurs, which happens frequently, even when it has not healed for any other time except for the moment when the vein is opened and the incision is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	then hurry and place a sponge soaked in warm water and a little salt on it, and bind it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And you should do this after the issuing of blood from the vein, and if there remains some blueness or greenness in its place for several days, it will not harm it;[IT] Et quant il sera saniez, si face le cautere de feu;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you wish, put something of aloe or myrrh ground up and mixed with chamomile juice, marshmallow or similar on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there comes an abscess and discharge at the basis of the shin: place then your hand upon it, and if you find a soft spot on compression of the hand, then this appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, be cautious not to apply any of the things we have mentioned, for perhaps it may pierce the artery; but instead make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each person according to the quantity of their strength and the color of their blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it thins out; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for the person who is plump and strong, and in need of bloodletting, make a larger incision, and let the wound be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the weak person, do the contrary, and they need to be bled frequently, and they should be bled by cutting across, not by puncturing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bleeding is free from bloodletting and nerve damage, and it is worth more than long or broad bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the person who is lacking in bleeding, give them a piece of bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if they are overheated, then bleed them three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if they are of a cold complexion, then give them bread soaked before bleeding in reduced syrup, either made from muscatel or aromatic honey with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cheese, and make the syrup fragrant.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if they are weak after bleeding, after the loss of much blood, then they should drink broth made from meat and subtle fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and make use of other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm, and purge himself another time, then it is necessary, when he has become weak due to heavy bleeding, that he bleeds drop by drop, according to the amount of his remaining strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong veins, should bleed 7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.[NOTE: I assumed that "houres" is a typo of "heures". If not, please let me know.]
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to purge himself in another way, should do so on the second day or the third.[NOTE: I assumed that "d'autre part" refers to a different type of medical treatment. If it means something else, please let me know.]
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is a lot of blood inside the body which has been heated up and causes fever, so one must extract a large quantity and widen the vein until it closes again;[NOTE: "le pertus" refers to the incision or opening made in the vein for bleeding. "Em pameson" is an archaic form of "en son pais", meaning "in its place".]
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	since you have fulfilled all the conditions of cleanliness, and placed your hand on its pulse when it coagulates, so that death does not come in its place.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens frequently, when the surgeon is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not appropriate, when you see the arm loosened and blood comes out a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press hard;[Translate]
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is crooked, should you quickly extend the arm, because that would be harmful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but you should leave it alone until it coagulates a second time; or you can apply the tip of the flame there until the blood that has congealed in the opening of the vein comes out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and place on it one handful of salve rehydrated in water, and lightly press on it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not squeeze it until the abscess has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled instead of the vein in the head because it is compound.[
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of bloodletting is as follows: the patient places their hand in warm water until the vein becomes red;[
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be bound moderately, so that the vein is visible, while keeping a steady hand, not roughly or for too long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and make the incision wide, and cauterize it close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot exit, place the hand in warm water, and allow the blood to flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if this is done in the summer, do not place the hand in warm water, for it is more appropriate to use it in the winter than in the summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the incision made from this vein is safer than any other veins, as there are no artery or nerve present in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The incision of the saphenous vein of the right hand is beneficial for all liver diseases, and here's how to do it:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	restrain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein swells, if one sees it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the flesh is cut crosswise, and if you sew it all the way through, it will not matter;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not go too deep, for the nerves are underneath, stripped of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand back in hot water if the blood is congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn enough blood as is necessary, then put oil and wax on the vein to quickly heal it, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The flow of sap in the left hand is worth as much for the disease of gout, and does the same thing as I told you for the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The flow of sap in the shin is worth as much for all the diseases that are below the body (i.e. the legs).
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	Such as diseases of the varicose veins, retention of fluids, illness of the legs, thighs and old age-related ailments, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of this sap is such that the patient places their foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it disappears,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and ties it above the ankle joint; and the vein is at the ankle, and many small veins run along the foot;[IST] et quant li voinne perent, si adesce li pie et si s’i frotent, et ce fet il souvent.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	clean then either the narrow wound or the wide gap, or at the ankle, which is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you clean it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath, and clean it across as well, just like in cutting meat; and let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if blood cannot come out, put the foot back in water and let the vein empty completely.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the incision is not enough the first time, try again a little higher up, for the place is salt.[This may refer to the belief that saltwater or sea water had healing properties and could help in the healing process. This would mean making another incision a little higher than the previous one to allow more of the "salty" seawater to flow into the wound.]
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And do not worry about nerves, as we have said before, and do the same with the shin of the other foot as well.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The ligament of the sciatic vein is at the back of the thigh, and its discharge is worth/amounts to the pain of a swelling, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its discharge is such that the patient urinates and squeezes above the ankle four times while twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	Because otherwise, the vein will not open, and if it does open, drain it in all ways that you can, including crossing (the flow).
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is better to cut the ligament because it is tough and difficult to grasp by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't find it (the ligament), drain some part of it that opens at the back of the leg and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And make sure to stanch the blood so that it stops, and then loosen the tie, and place cotton on it and bind it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Of blistering cups (or "of cupping by scarification")[ETB: I'm assuming this is a medical term related to the practice of bloodletting or cupping. Let me know if you have any context that suggests a different meaning.]
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cups are made of horns, or of tin, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this kind of cupping which is done without striking is also done in two ways: either with heat or without heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And cupping that is done by striking and drawing blood is done in 14 places on the body,[ETB: I'm assuming this refers to specific locations on the body where cups can be applied for medical purposes. Let me know if you have any context that suggests a different meaning.][ETB: I will now translate all of the provided text in one go.]
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is entirely under the head; and the other is in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others at the sides of the neck; and a vacuum cup under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and a vacuum cup on each shoulder; and a vacuum cup on the buttocks;[...continued in next message...]
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and vacuum cups between the two arms; and vacuum cups on both legs;[...continued in next message...][Text cut off due to character limit, continuing translation:]
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the vacuum cups at both ankles; and the application of vacuum cups does not involve blood flow, except for small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	"And therefore, do not weaken it at all, as is done with venesection."
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	"And it is not appropriate for it to be administered, neither with strong heat nor without heat, in any disease that arises from plethora, until the entire body is evacuated."
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	"And if it is necessary to bloodlet due to illness or as a habit, we administer it every hour at the beginning or end of the month and in between, at any time."
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	"For there are some who, when they need to be bloodletted, have a heavy head;"
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	"And there are some who find plethora and redness in their faces, and in their head, and The practice was often recommended during the menstrual period as it was thought to help regulate menstruation and prevent diseases. However, this is not supported by modern medicine.]
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The letting of blood from the nose helps with headache... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the entire body; [Notes: In this context, "letting of blood" refers to bloodletting or phlebotomy, a common medical practice in medieval times. It was believed that removing excess blood from the body could help balance the bodily fluids known as humors and treat various illnesses. However, modern medicine recognizes bloodletting as an outdated and potentially harmful practice. The phrase "evacuation of the entire body" likely refers to purging or laxative treatments that were also used in medieval medicine.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bloodletting#History)

si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	Like we place on the nipples when the milk is flowing; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we place cups on the stomach and thighs to reduce the size of the limb.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and alleviate pain when there is an abscess or stone; as it possibly draws out the abscess, or clears the stone from its place through its attractive virtue.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And it does the same when placed on the liver and spleen when there is trapped wind,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these cups are administered empty to simply suck, and sometimes they are administered with heat, and sometimes filled with warm water.

Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping vessel applied by fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should have two fingers' width in diameter and be half a palm deep, with a small hole on one side, as if to insert a needle.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it should be made of tin, smooth at the front so that it does not cut or harm the patient when placed on the body part.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And in the middle, have an iron or tin bar across it to hold a candle.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And let there be large and small ones, according to the diseases they are used to treat and the age of those who use them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because children's cups are different than adults',
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should apply this cup in this way to the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	soak the cloth or a linen strip in oil or wax and place it inside the cup through the rod that is inside the cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the flame is at the bottom of the cup and does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb with your hand over the opening we mentioned earlier. When you want to release the vacuum, simply remove the cup.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the linen as before, and reapply it frequently, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	And for the cup applied to the disease of pleurisy, which is wet and has no opening or abscess, and is only applied when it is full of water, placed on the body part only;
et c’est li forme:	And this is the method:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Cups are only applied to parts of the body where it is not possible to apply cups due to their small size, such as the lips and gums, and similar areas.[The text seems to be discussing bloodletting with cups. The use of cups on certain parts of the body like lips and gums is not possible because those parts are too small for cups. ]
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And in places devoid of flesh, such as fingers or nails and similar areas;[The text is explaining the method for bloodletting with cups. The text states that cups are not applied to small parts of the body, but they can be applied to large fleshy areas like the stomach and thighs. In case of places with little flesh, such as fingers, one must be careful while applying cups.]
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	"And the qualities of the water are such that when you find sues that are in clean, clear waters without pollution, then take them."
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	"And place them in clean water until they become familiar with it and have nothing in their bellies."
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	"Then it should be bled with a vein and cupping glass, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place the sues on top."
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	"And when they are full and heavy, if it is possible to put a cupping glass there, do so, because this is very helpful."
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the level of aspiration (or "asile"), and then of water, very well, and then apply a cupping glass (or "espreint").
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the wound takes too long to heal near the veins, wet a linen cloth in cold water and place it on top until the vein has constricted.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if there are multiple veins, apply crushed vitriol (or "vitriole broié"), or gal (a sticky substance from trees), and similar things on top until they have constricted.[Note: Vitriol is an archaic term for a sulfate mineral used in alchemy. Gal is the resinous sap from certain trees, similar to modern-day turpentine.]
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or place half of fried and peeled beans on the wound, and let them stay there until they become hot against it. This will stop the bleeding immediately.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more, take other veins (or tendons).[Note: The Old French word "sansues" can refer to both veins and tendons depending on the context.]
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the veins do not want to be bled, rub the place with fresh blood, or insert a needle until blood comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And then place them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will heat up;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are hot, sprinkle on a little powder of crushed aloe and salt, or ashes, and they will now shrink back to normal.[Original text in Old French: "et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant."]
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish doctors throw away this chapter, as they never saw any of the ancient books, nor did they read any letters.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, the medical profession is strange in our land, because I never found anyone skilled in it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing about it except for what I have learned from the ancient books, which I have studied extensively and put into practice in my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described for you in this chapter what it contains, summarized at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are prepared, just as I did in the previous two chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Then it is necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and the chapters where the wise man directs his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who have been tested may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or bruising occurs to someone, it is necessary to quickly heal the patient from one side and the other, if nothing prevents you, such as weakness of the body, children, or the elderly;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the time is not very hot or too cold; and eat little frozen food, that is to say cold meats, and bird and hare meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill oneself with too much food that fills the veins with blood, until you are certain there will be no hot abscess or swelling of matter in the limb; so that the patient can return to their usual regimen as soon as possible.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that provide robust nourishment and have stickiness, such as wheat cooked in water, rice, heads, feet, dairy, eggs, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at times, a delay in treatment results in greater deformation and faster fractures.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the old and infirm cannot heal or knit together well according to their nature due to the weakness of their limbs, nor can those who are too tender, such as the bones of young children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but do not worry, set a large splint on the broken bone which pulls and brings the limb together until it heals as it was before; and do not neglect your work, and therefore you must feed it with rich foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different from that of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that tends to go towards the groin, and another one pointing upwards, like the tip of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break is just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And for each type there should be its own tool and proper instrument for the restoration, according to what comes to mind in its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And a break in the bone is recognized by the fact that the place is twisted and clearly visible, and it sounds when pressed with the hand;[As the text seems to be describing how to recognize a broken bone, "li leus est tors" refers to the location of the break being twisted or deformed. "Et sone au presseir de la main" means that when pressure is applied with the hand, the break makes a sound, likely due to the fractured ends of the bone grinding against each other.]
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And if there is no twisted appearance or sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break;[In this sentence, "li malaides" refers to the sick or injured person being treated. The phrase "se n'i a point de brisure" can be translated as "then there is no break," which suggests that the absence of twisted appearance and sound upon touching are indicators that the bone is not broken.]
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have crookedness, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move him by hand at all, but instead apply the following mentioned medicines and then bind him gently.

And then align it with the movement that you can easily and safely do, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restoration where there are parts missing; then bind it as described below.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into two pieces, whether it is an arm or a leg, or with two ropes for a small member, or with one rope and your hand;

And feel it with your hand to see if it seems not quite right; then align it well and do not pull too hard, or press as those do who cause hot abscess and contraction in the member through their work, as we have often seen.
