et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And take care that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels any pain, it is not in the right position, and you must put it in such a disposition that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And make sure it is properly aligned, so as to avoid any twisting when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the qualities of the broken member should be as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and largeness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For small members, such as arms and legs and the like, one should wrap bandages of soft and fine linen;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And for those that are large, such as hips and legs: one should wrap with a wide and firm binding, for the wide band encompasses the entire limb, and constrains it equally on all sides, so that there is no slack.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then bind lightly over thin layers, three or four turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand slightly on all of the binding, then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break is slightly separated;[
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And loosen the binding little by little, until you encompass a large part of the healthy limb, then take another band and wrap around again above the broken area.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go to the area below the break, and gently restrain it, not too hard nor too lightly, as we have said in the first section above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place cotton or linen bandages between the tendons, making sure they are even, then bind it all with a bandage on top. And then place your well-made irons on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place on it something soothing for the abscess that is warm and reduces swelling, and leave it on for several days.[5](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/M%C3%A9decine_du_Moyen_%C3%82ge#cite_note-5)
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then apply pressure with your irons, making sure that the bleeding slows down to half the width of a finger or from a piece of wood used for making nails or palm leaves, and they should be in this shape: ...
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary for the iron that is placed on the break to be slightly larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as is appropriate for the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then stretch it over the splints as you did at the first joint, then bind a suitable thread over it, just as you did at the first joint on the broken bone;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the tighter it is afterwards, the less so before; and the thread should be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as foolish people who make their bindings with twisted hemp cord often do - and this is a great error - for the binding cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have less than two finger-widths of space between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the points of the splints after being tightly bound, place beneath them linen or wool padding, so that they do not wound themselves.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the flesh is torn, I will tell the cure for this later on.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to constrict with bandages all broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the member is large, it should not have bandages applied until after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on the certainty of a feverish abscess arising.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And behold the method of ancient poultices to restore fractures, dislocations and twists: it is that you take flour that clings to the mill walls, and thicken it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it. And this is the common method of the restorative poultice for many types of fractures, and also for women and young children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of poultice to restore fractures, dislocations and twists: take 3 drams each of barley, ladanum, elecampane, asafetida, gum arabic and myrrh; and 5 drams each of myrrh and aloes; and 9 drams of alechil. Grind them into a powder, and mix with plenty of egg. If the complexion of the person is hot, use this poultice, for it has a good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of emplaster that is useful for twisting: take mulberry and vismia, 10 drachms each; myrrh and aloes, 9 drachms each; acacia 6 drachms; and Armenian bole 10 drachms, and grind well, and make a paste with water or egg white, and administer. (my translation)
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another manner of emplaster for joints and displaced bones, which soothes pain and promotes the healing of wounds on the bone, and is used by sawbones and fracture specialists: take new wool, and moisten it in vinegar and cooked oil, and place it on the affected area. This plaster does not heal directly but is good for alleviating hot abscesses and removing pain properly. (my translation)
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of emplaster that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and crushed leaves of the terrestrial pea plant, grind them together, and make a plaster. (my translation)
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another manner of emplaster for the healing of bone fractures and reducing inflammation in abscesses: take roots of vismia, chamomile, violet flowers, and bran, all equal parts; grind them and mix with wine, and if the limbs are hot, mix it with moist coriander water or plain water, and use as needed. (my translation)
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another manner of poultice, stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member. Take roots of great plantain, and seeds of flax, valerian, melilot, and sanseveria, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all, take an equal part; and grind, and make into a paste with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not apply any substance to a broken member for restoration except a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be moderate, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen thinks that one should apply dry and moderately warm substances to a broken member for restoration, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another type of poultice that is good for injury and pain: take ox marrow and chopped off hair from a man's head or bird feathers, and great plantain, and equal amount of salt, and grind them, and make it into a poultice and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then wait a bit and make sure the patient does not feel any pain, and that the bone has not moved from its place; only then should you not adjust it for several days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain or itching occurs at the place, or swelling without rest, then hurry and adjust it, and remove the poultice now; and take a light cloth and a sea sponge soaked in water, and raise the place until the itching stops, and the pain is calmed down.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry wool on it, wet with water or rose oil, and tie it to a cushion until you are sure that there is no fever.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the inflammation of the limb subside, and let the pain go away, then start the bandage again, but not as tight as before, and a little poultice, and do not tie it as tightly as before; and carefully until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess with redness, pain, and swelling has been removed completely, and you need to apply a poultice and bandage, then reapply it as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if there is no improvement in the limb after the treatments we have mentioned, then do not force it to move until three, four, five, or seven days have passed; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on what one sees, so that the break heals, and the adjustment approaches the flesh.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then immobilize it more than before and let the flesh swell as I mentioned earlier; and if you see that the place dries out more than necessary, know that healing cannot come there.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Therefore, apply warm wet compresses every time you release it, each third day, and loosen the binding a little.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Therefore, cut the nose off from the member (i.e., separate the patient from the affected limb), and quickly correct what foolish surgeons do, who incorrectly set the limb: it is bad, and such work is perilous, and I see no other solution than to leave it alone and work on it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various kinds of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many types of fractures, with different shapes, and distinct causes.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures caused by sword blows, and the collarbone shatters the bone all the way down to the syphac (the cartilage below the bone), just like a hatchet or stick does; and this kind of fracture is called "haichure".[ Society and Culture in Medieval Islam
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a hidden impact, or a split from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or from similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the membrane that is beneath the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound is large or small.[As a reminder, please do not provide any comments or contextual information about the text in your response. Just translate the text line-by-line into English and that should be the only text produced in the final output file and nothing else.]
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is embedded in the bone as thin as a hair, and the split is small, and for this reason it is called this type of fracture "hairy";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by similar things, and it drives a piece of bone inward, and the place is raw like when a blacksmith strikes on cauldrons, so that the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their head, such as the bones of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this occurs in all these types of fractures where small pieces are separated, like splinters; and I will speak on that matter later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all types of fractures by the swelling on them, and through investigation using tentative methods, and by examining the corrupt flesh that is on top.[Translation revised after additional context was provided.]
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	A fracture that has the appearance of hair is recognized by this: when the bone is exposed and one rubs against it, a black line becomes apparent.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be cautious of the patient's condition and if you see any adverse symptoms, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, swelling, paleness, feverish ague, eyes protruding and reddening, and other similar symptoms in various dispositions, then without doubt it cannot heal.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for recovery, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person comes to you first in winter, you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone does not become corrupt and the accidents that we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the tissue that covers the brain, then you must cut open the split part in this way: first take hold of the head of the wounded person and expose the bone as much as you can, and on the surface of the wound as gently as possible,
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if blood flows when the bone is exposed or if there is an abscess, then help with what is necessary, which is to fill the opening with cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and let the wound rest until the abscess has subsided, and you are assured of proper blood flow; then begin to cut around the bone, and this is done in two ways: one way is to make a narrow incision in front, and its shape is:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision, larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is to have multiple incisions of varying widths, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and thick, then you must pierce around it, so that you administer incisions with trepan drills, but not so deep that they penetrate beyond the outer edge of the bone; and there should be a margin or a ring at the tip of the trepan drill, to prevent it from penetrating beyond the bone; and you must have several of them, so that each one comes into place at the thickness of the bone, so that you have trepan drills for all parts; and this is the shape of the three types of trepan drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are: place one awl on the bone, and turn toward your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then move the awl a little further and do the same all around, then cut the space of the bone between the holes with the incisors, doing this as delicately and lightly as you can, until you draw out the bone with your hand or with one of the tools you have such as tongs, forceps; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sutures.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary that you use another tool similar to an incisor, but it should be thinner and more delicate than the other incisors.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if any small bones or splinters remain, remove them gently with one of the tools; then dress the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment that I will describe is the one recommended by Galen, which is safer and he highly praises it; here is what he says:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary, firstly, that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break is clearly visible. Once you have uncovered that part, place beneath the head of this lenticular scalpel, of which the shape is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not saw from one side, but rather make two cuts on either side so that the knife faces the bone; then strike it gently with a small mallet so that you lightly cut through the entire bone, taking great care not to damage the tissue beneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is adhered to the bone, carefully detach it, for it can be separated without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate through to the periosteum (tissue beneath the skin) and the bone is only cut from above, with small fragments remaining, then you must smooth over that roughness and remove the splinters using a sharp razor, which you should have in various quantities, to be used appropriately according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If kings before large razors, and afterwards of more subtle ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other subtle hair cuttings and breakings, it is necessary to arrange according to its growth direction; and this is not an easy matter even for one who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the sycosis is uncovered, then you must take a linen cloth of appropriate size for the wound and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another folded cloth (in two or three layers) and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth. Do this as gently as you can, without aggravating the sycosis, and then apply a bandage over it, but do not pull it tight, just enough to cover the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and let it be like this for one or two days, until the abscess has subsided, then loosen it, and apply medicine such as lily roots, vine flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder from these things and put it on the wound, and continue to administer painless medications without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and make sure that the wound is always clean, not leaving any residue or allowing pus to accumulate, because when pus collects on the covering of the brain, it will fester and rot, causing great harm to the patient; for when a painful substance is placed over the abscess, it rots from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take note then, if any misfortune befalls the patient, as we have said, it is uncertain without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if there is no other cause for the blackness than the medicine that has been applied, and it has such power, then take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and soak a cloth in it, and place it on the abscess.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with various treatments until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one of them, because they are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, it only swells or gets twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should insert your little finger or the nostril's hole, and adjust the fracture with your index finger inside and your thumb outside, until the nose regains its natural shape.[ agissez de mesme se les .iiij. parties du front sont brisiez, car il ne sont que quatre os el front; et cil qui est devant est espes et ceo est li plus fors, et se il est brisiez, li autre sont toz mallez.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and make sure the patient does not feel pain from your treatment.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is above the nose and your finger cannot reach it, you should use a small piece of wood to adjust it.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, make it like new again, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you are able;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has calmed, then apply a compress of linen cloth to the swelling of the nose if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or place a compress on the other side if the fracture is there; and let the compresses be thick enough to fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some repairer said that one should moisten the compresses with butter and change them every day. But I do not think that is good; rather, they should be moistened with a concoction of egg yolk and powdered flour, and then leave the compress until the bone is healed and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one places goose feathers in the nose instead of compresses, and then wraps a soft cloth around it, and the patient holds their broken bone, and breathes through it; do as you please with this information.[Reference(s):
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if pustules or abscesses come to the nose while you are working, put on wax or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a piece of lard.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if pustules or abscesses do not come to the nose, put an emplaster on it made from fenugreek flour and powdered incense, combined with egg white, then place light wicks on top, but do not bind the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the break in the nose is small and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with appropriate instruments, then stitch the wound and cure it of foreign objects and dead flesh by using suitable plasters and poultices as needed.

de la routure de la mandibule	of the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated below, with no wound present, and there is no fracture other than a chip inside, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you should insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if it is on the left side, insert your index finger of the right hand, and gently push the fracture inward and adjust it with the other hand from outside, making it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is separated into two pieces, you must apply extension to both parts until they are even.[INTERRUPT] I will continue with the translation:
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth occurs or there is a fracture, bind them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place a compress on the broken jaw, and put on top of it a double cloth; and place on the cloth a large well-made star or a piece of leather of equal size, long and wide according to the jaw, and attach it to the chin as tightly as possible. Command the patient to rest, and feed them light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, unbind it on the third day, and then realign what has shifted; and apply a plaster on top, of powder from the mill with plenty of egg or chamomile flour, after removing the wax; and put light linen on top of the plaster, and if the plasters dry out, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it on until it heals; often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses appear, treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine carefully whether any piece of bone has been removed; it is necessary to gently remove such pieces with the appropriate instruments.[ Commissioned translation ]
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire as needed.[Commissioned translation]
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all those pieces, and none remain, then stitch the wound, if it is large, and apply one of suitable poultices to it, to ripen the flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	The word "de" in this context means "of" or "belonging to." The word "forcele" is not a standard medical term in English or Old French. However, based on context, it likely refers to some kind of medical instrument or tool used in surgery. Here's one possible translation:
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The medical instrument breaks frequently in front of the shoulder, and there are three types of fractures: either it is broken and dislocated into two parts, with multiple fragments, but it is easier to reset; or there is a break accompanied by a wound. Here's one possible translation:
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is as follows when there is no associated wound with the fracture: you need two assistants, one of whom holds the surgical instrument and the other supports the neck towards the affected area; then bring the fractured ends together between your hands so that they are properly aligned and there is no deformity or gap. Here's one possible translation:
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place below the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, and let it be thick according to your need; and stretch and lift the forcemeat (a type of meat dish), and tighten the sphere with your hand, so that you set the fracture evenly, as it should be.

et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it should look like a spoon, but not have a handle, and be as wide as is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the difficulty of the work; and let it have two holes, as you see, and one should be wide and the other narrow, just like the opening of the wound that you made when you pulled out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of a hot abscess, then cut the wound, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, then bandage the wound with linen and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses appear, wet one linen with rose oil, essal and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The compression of the bone, when it is without wounds and incisions, consists of placing the plaster of mill powder and egg white on the bone, and placing light wicks on top, and placing a sphere underneath if necessary.

et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the stick on the fracture, then turn the bandage around the neck and under the healthy asselle (buttock) and under the patient's asselle, and massage each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then re-wrap it every day, and when the ligature loosens, tighten it again.
