puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then reapply the poultice if necessary, and bind it in place until they are healed; and it is healed for most in 28 days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It rarely happens that the shoulder breaks in such a way that it is not noticeable except by touch; one must prepare for the fracture according to its shape and relocate it according to its natural form, in all ways possible; then place on top of it powdered flour with plenty of egg whites, and light bandages, and put a double cloth over it; then put on a wide and thin plate, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the plate at any part of the shoulder, stuff those hairs with linen bandages so that the plate lies evenly; and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, making sure the plate does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and whenever it loosens, tighten it again, and ensure the plate is in its correct position, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be healed in 20 or 25 days. And when this period is over, unbind it, and be careful, for it is not an easy thing for a bone to come out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone juts out in front, but not beneath the skin, then make an incision, and cut as we have said in the breaking of the forearm to soothe the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	In the breaking of the hip.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The thigh is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the end. And when it is broken in the middle, it tilts downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks strength, and may vomit blood, and there is a clear sign of the break in the fractured bone, which can be felt.[FILE] .md
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies down with their back on a cushion between their shoulders, then presses their shoulders together and brings the ribs together at the sides with your hands, carefully making sure it is even in all places as much as you can until the bone is in its proper place; then apply poultices and compresses of salt or other light wood to the fracture, wrap it in a cloth, and bind it firmly to the broken bone so that it does not move; tie the bandage around their back and tighten it appropriately, checking every hour to see if it has loosened and tightening it again as needed; if it is necessary to loosen it due to corrosion, itching, pain, or abscess, do so quickly and remove the poultice, treating the affected area with appropriate cures; then reapply the poultice and bind it tightly until it has healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs does not come about except in heavy blows to the back and chest, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and one can feel it well in the examination at the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the setting of the break is that you place the fracture evenly, as it should be. And then apply a plaster, and bind it with a bandage if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is declining inward, then the patient feels very great pain and shortness of breath, just like a pleurisy, because the bone pricks the lining; and the breathing is painful, and quickly there comes up a large amount of blood, and this is dangerous to health; and the ancients have put much effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And some say that one should administer foods that cause the belly to swell, in order to push out the break.[STH]
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make it so that boils/abscesses come to it, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come (to it), lance it (with a surgical lancet).
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of you have said that cupping glasses should be placed on the area to draw out strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cups might attract impurities to the area due to its weak condition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you have said that the area should be covered with a cloth soaked in warm oil and tents (bandages) should be placed between the ribs to ensure even application, then treat it with a treatment for pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure from the bone pointing through the skin, and they are fearful, then you must make an incision above the broken rib, and you must place a tool underneath to protect the lung; and then you must cut the bone, and gently pull, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and dress it with poultices until it heals. And if abscesses come, then put wet bandages soaked in rose oil on top, and place on the side; and care for the side as needed for the abscess, and lie down on the side where it is, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there occurs a break in the bones of the neck, and rarely does it bend; and also at the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover or not, look and see if their hands are softened, swollen, and numb, and if they cannot move or extend them, and if you poke them with a needle, and they do not feel it. Know that they are in a critical condition in many ways, and if they can move them and feel when they are pinched and poked, know that the joints of the bone are safe, and that the patient will recover if treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will heal or not, see if the feet are weak, and if there are symptoms present that are in the hands, and on the back there is a windiness and involuntary evacuation; and when it has been laid on its stomach, there is still involuntary evacuation. And when it is turned over on its back and it wants to move, it cannot. Know that it is fatal: do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these symptoms do not occur, then the matter is easier.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is as follows: if there is a hot abscess on the spine, place roses oil or egg yolk oil on it until it calms down; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on the side where they feel pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone becomes dislocated, it is necessary to cover the wound with a cloth; and remove the bone, then stitch the two lips of the wound together if it is large, using one stitch; then apply a healing ointment until it is healed. If the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the knot," place your left hand on top of it, and push it into place with your right hand to the best of your ability; then apply the plaster and bandage if necessary; then bind it, and if there are dislocated bones, lift them up and remove them, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the shin bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the shin bone is fractured, and if it does happen, it is usually only a slight decrease in width at the site of the break; and it forms a long, slanted break, and comes to the patient causing pain and swelling at the site of the break.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the method of setting the fracture is as follows: place your hand above the break, so that you are over the break itself; and determine the location and shape of the break; and if the break is only at the end of the bone, align it so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or slanted inward, have the patient lie on their stomach until you are ready to set the fracture.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And once you have aligned it, apply a poultice and then place a splint made of wood or bone on top of it, securing the splint in place so that the fracture does not move; and fill in the space around the break with bandages, ensuring that they are evenly distributed.[INST 1]: Et quant li emplastres sera sec et les lieures bien assizes, si se doit le malaide lever e aler a sun afere.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses come in its place, do not touch them until the abscesses have calmed down, and apply what we mentioned before; then return to healing and bind it as is necessary, unless there is any adverse event; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is the one that is between the ribcage and the head of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, then it must be restored according to one of two methods, one of which is to take a rod of medium size, in this shape:[The text describes a diagram or illustration, but the description is not provided here.]
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two arms with two bands and pull them upwards, and have the patient sit on a chair; then throw his broken arm over the rod, so that it reaches the armpit and is in the middle of the curved rod; then place it under some heavy object or let the assistant stretch it downward; then put the surgeon's hands together around the break, until the break returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is to position the patient on his back, and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants, one of whom holds what is above the break with his hands, and the other holds below all the way down to one ligament, and each pulls to their side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, then tighten one ligament below the break and above the break, and have each of the assistants pull to their side. And if the break is close to the shoulder joint, then you must put one ligament in the middle below the socket, and another towards the edge, below the break; and similarly if the break is towards the edge, then you must put a light ligament there without effort, so that the break is even on both sides, above the socket; then align the break as it should be, and tighten it if pus does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if pus comes, then do not tighten it for seven days, and put a wet linen cloth on the break soaked in vinegar and rose oil, until the abscess has calmed down; then tighten it, and the method of tightening is to apply the poultice on the break, then align the arm on the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or breast; and put on the cloth, and tighten on the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm stays in its place if nothing prevents it, or unless the bones are broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you fear that the bone is broken, then use splints, and put on the break a splint wider and stronger than the others, and there should be a gap of two fingers between each splint, and each splint should be large enough to extend beyond the break by three fingers on each side; then tighten over the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the break, more firmly and less so as you move away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the swelling and tightening, as we have mentioned, at the time you restore the broken member, and you doubt a hot abscess, then let it be bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine every three days if the binding has caused itching, inflammation, or any harm to the site, or if circulation cannot reach the member because the binding is too tight. Loosen it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents occur, do not unbind it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; place a cushion filled evenly with wool underneath the affected area, and every hour during the day and night, check to see that the shape of the broken member does not change or if the binding has loosened; then adjust it according to the medicine's power, and give them the food we mentioned earlier, in such a way that the food is initially fine; and when they begin to recover, the food should be thicker. It is customary for the bandage and leg to be rebound in 40 days in total; and then it should be unbound, and baths and ointment medicines should be administered to straighten the site. And if the constriction is severe and swollen, it may take one day or two months to unbind.
de la brisure du bras	The breaking of the arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", one of which is small and it is the one that follows the wrist; and the other is large and it is the one that is below, towards the little finger; perhaps the large foscile breaks alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small ribs are broken, the restoration and healing is easy; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is difficult and more severe than when both are broken together. If it is only the small rib that is broken, then it should be lightly stretched and aligned.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large rib, then it must be pulled more forcefully; and it should be stretched out on a cushion, and the pouchet of the hand held higher than the others, and the little fingers lower than the other fingers, and have the patient cross their arms over themselves with one cushion before them that is higher than what the patient can bear. Then, have the assistants extend the patient's arms on either side, either under their hand or with a bandage, and another assistant above. And then the physician should align it properly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has pieces, then put each one in its place, and if there is any piece that pricks the heart and cannot be restored to its place, then saw through it and remove it as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound with the break, I have spoken about this in a separate chapter; then take care of it (attend to it).
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the setting, boils occur, then place a piece of linen cloth dipped in a mixture of rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and gently place a cloth over it, until the boils have subsided. Then remove the adhesive, and apply the plaster made from the powder of the mill with plenty of egg, then place the stylets, and let the stylet of the breakage be stronger and slightly larger than the others; and know that it should have six stylets or branches in several dispositions: either the breaker is in one of the bones, or in two; and bind more above the breakage than any other part, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are above the breakage be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread from which it is bound be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And wrap the member and the binding after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any misfortune befalls the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then it is necessary to rinse the member with warm water until the itching has subsided; and let the member not rest tightly. And then resume binding, and if the binding is weakened and the bones have separated, and similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you notice that the circulation does not come to the member because it is too tight, then you should soften it slightly and leave it like that for several days, until the circulation returns, and then bind it.[1]
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things we have mentioned happen to the patient, then do not unbind them for twenty days or more. Instead, during this time, they should keep their hands on their neck with equal collars and be careful of movement and agitation, and sleep on their backs. And know that this breakage is healed in thirty or thirty-five days, and perhaps even in twenty days, depending on the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that breaks in the back of the hand and at the knuckles often occur, but they usually result in bruising more often than breaking.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bruised, then the patient should sit cross-legged and sit upright in front of them; then place their hand on a stretched out cloth, and have the assistant straighten the broken bones and align them properly until they are fitted together well; and apply a bandage and compresses, unless an abscess forms, then place a splint according to the size of the injury; and wrap it in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is on the outer edge around the stomach of the palm, then make a sphere from cloth and instruct the patient to press it against their injured palm; then bind it with a long strip of cloth, and let the splint be made of wood as wide as the palm of the hand, and bind it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outside, then place a splint on top of it, and another underneath in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it around the entire hand, and fasten the binding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the bone setter comes to one of our fingers, if it is crooked, place it evenly as it should be; and bind it with the sole, and if you see fit, place a straight small stake to raise the fracture and ensure it does not move; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, place it evenly and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or bind them all together, making sure they are aligned, or place a stake on it, as with a splint; and take care in the restoration and placement of hot abscesses, and heal those who come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken thigh.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and it is clearly visible when it twists in front and back; and the restoration consists of tying one ligature above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their face, then each assistant extends their ligature evenly to their part; and this is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the hip's root, let one of the ligaments be towards the wrist, and the other ligament below the fracture. And similarly if it is near the knee, and then let the ligament be next to the knee, and let the extension be downwards; then let the surgeon place the bone even with his two hands, until it is according to its natural shape, and then put on the poultice and bandage, if pus does not appear.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside and then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is applied in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap over the fracture a hard bandage doubled in two or three layers, and let any extra length remain; then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, next to the knee below, and bring the ends of the thread up above; then wrap back over the leg and the thigh the bandage, then place a splint over the fracture, and place a splint over the bone of the leg; then apply padding made of soft cloth between the leg and the thigh to make the tightening even, then begin to tightly bind three or four turns over the fracture; and as you go further above the fracture, bind less tightly; then pay attention to the two ends of the thread that you placed between the leg and the thigh, and bind them with three splints that are above, then return to below the head of the thread, so that you come next to the foot; and bind it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, as long as no abscess, swelling or any other symptom appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is a symptom (such as an abscess or swelling), then loosen the bandage and address what has occurred, as we have said many times before. If there are pieces of bone protruding, then it is necessary to cut them away if possible; and if not, then it is necessary to break open the bandage and pull them out; and treat the wound as we have described, until it heals.[Additional context: This text is providing instructions for the care of a broken leg. The text advises that if there are any symptoms or complications (such as protruding bone), then the bandages should be loosened and the issue addressed. If pieces of bone are protruding, they should be removed if possible, and if not, then the bandage must be broken open to remove them. The wound should then be treated until it heals.]
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the hip is broken so that steel is put in it, as in the shoulder and arm; nonetheless, in the restoration made this way, the patient does not fare well.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip is restored in 1 day, or a little less or a little more, according to the variations in complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	This Old French phrase translates to "from the groin of the knee." The word "ruelle" refers to a narrow street or lane, but in medical texts like this one, it can be used to describe anatomical features. Here, it is being used as a term for the crease or fold of skin on the inner side of the knee, near the groin area.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that there are few breaks in the groin of the knee, but it often dislocates. And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a single hole, and this happens with or without an open wound, and one can feel it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that you put evenly what is dislocated at its two ends, until it can be moved as a whole; then apply the poultice, and place a round bandage if needed, and bind it as it is appropriate, then take care of all the arrangements as we have said in other fractures, such as hot abscess and similar ones; and put on each symptom what is necessary for it, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Here is the translation of the given Old French text into modern English, with the added context of "de la brisure de la jambe" (about the fracture of the leg):
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that the leg has two bones, one of which is called by its proper name "tibia" and the other is called "fibula". And it happens that a fracture in the leg is similar to that of the arm, and therefore the restoration is also similar to that of the arm. And the work involved is the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	If both bones are broken together, then the leg becomes deformed in all directions. This can lead to a severe displacement of the broken bone ends, which would require careful reduction and alignment in order to restore proper anatomy and promote healing. In modern medicine, this type of fracture may be treated with closed reduction and casting or open reduction and internal fixation (ORIF), depending on the severity and complexity of the injury. It is important to ensure that the bones are properly aligned and stabilized to prevent further damage and enable optimal healing.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, set them straight again.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bones are broken, there is great pain and it is visible; and set them right underneath. Then provide support, align it evenly, and bind the ends equally; but nonetheless, if the fracture is severe, with multiple pieces, the support should be less and lighter; and support it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two straps made of wooden rods that encircle the leg on both sides, and extend from the knee to below; then wrap it in two layers, one above and one below, and tie it in the middle so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and this is good. And some administer a long splint made of wood, and place the leg inside to prevent movement. This is done properly in cases where there is a wound; and move the leg daily to see if there is heat or any other symptom, and treat it until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	And some administer a long splint made of wood for the fracture of the leg bones.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle is not prone to fractures, but sometimes the leg bones or two bones at the lower leg are broken in various ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that the bones of the foot are broken, and you see the bones protruding over one another, then place the patient's foot on the ground, as if they were going to walk, and then place your foot on top of theirs, where the bones are protruding, then press down until they return to their place; then apply a plaster and bandages, and under the belly of the foot, place a small board with two flat chips, then bind it to the foot after you have wrapped drapery around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the binding, for you will find the bones even, whether they be broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if some of the toes are broken, then set them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a pin in the broken toe according to the length of the toe, and it should be slightly wider, then place under the foot the board that I mentioned, and bind it to the foot; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place on each toe a pin according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board under the belly of the foot so that it is well supported.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I mentioned for other fractures, as we have said before; and treat each injury as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the arm bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's body is broken, make her sit with her legs spread apart, then lean her back and support her from behind; then stuff the vagina with cotton, making it as thick as a finger; then stand the woman up, lifting her hips and buttocks, and the cotton will come out, until it reaches the opening of the vagina, and the bone will return to its place with the finger; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she is done, replace it, and do this for seven days or so: the fracture will be healed. And if you wish, take a bladder of animal intestines, attach a cane to the opening, and insert the entire bladder into the vagina; then blow forcefully into the cane, until the bladder is inflated inside: the bone will return to its place; then stuff it with cotton and leave it like that for several days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the arm bone of a man or woman is broken, it can be restored in the same way as we have said for the thigh bone; and such fractures are not hidden from one who applies their attention and skill, and reads my book. For a fracture indicates in various ways the correct path to restoration: pay attention then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the penis is broken, take a goose throat and insert the penis into it; then wrap it with cloths and leave it for three days or so, and it will be quickly healed.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or similar, it is necessary that they be healed now, as the symptoms I have mentioned testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, apply vitriol to it if you have none other thing, then immediately begin to reduce the fracture in that same hour, or on that day, unless an abscess forms.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess forms, then delay the reduction for nine days until the abscess subsides and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will cause a bad outcome.[ safer to wait until the abscess has healed before attempting to reduce the fracture.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears under the skin and is exposed, you must gently align it with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not ready for you to place evenly in your hands, then realign it with this instrument, which is made of iron, having 7 or 8 inches in length, and its width corresponds to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the surgeon to press down on it with 3 or 4 fingers, according to what is needed in each fracture treatment; and it should be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend during compression on the limb while you are working, and it should be sharp at the tip, and thick from the middle towards the front, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called a "mallet", for which reason the curved part should be placed on top of the visible bone; and strike it once, until it aligns, and make them even one against the other. And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut the end of the bone so that the instrument has enough power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot realign the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument for this purpose, such as an osteotome or a scalpel, to the best of your ability; then scrape away what remains in the bone that is rough and covered with small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is realigned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position. Therefore, make sure it is in its proper place, then wet one cloth with black styptic wine, and apply it properly if it is in summer; and do not put any ointment or other thing on the wound that contains oil, as it can cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer cauterization when you have realigned the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut away the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and many times have foolish surgeons done this, causing death or corruption in the patient; and let the compression be softer and milder than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is large or severe, and you fear that complications may arise, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then you should not apply cups; but instead, wrap hard bandages around it, in place of cups, and bind them. And when after one day or two, you see it festering near the wound, then remove what you have placed on it, and apply a wound-healing ointment, such as the four-element ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you unbind the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be arranged in such a way that the swelling can easily flow downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and it can no longer heal but the swelling keeps returning, know that there are small bone fragments in it, for which you must stitch up the wound with sutures and remove all the displaced pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other form of corruption, then you should cure it, according to what he says in its chapter earlier. And when the bone is broken and appears on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and similar ones of the large members, then do not pull it at all, because many times death results; but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will come out by itself after twenty or thirty days, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that appear on the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see after the healing of the fracture, even when it is close to the joint, and it is ugly to look at the shape of the limb; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Pay attention then if the swelling comes to us after the healing of the fracture: administer styptic medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, sarcocollex, acacia, and similar things, either one of these or all together, and cook them with astringent wine or with egg white or vinegar; and put it on the wound in bandages and bind it well, and do not loosen it for several days; and then loosen it and start again, as many times as it takes to remove the nodules; or bind it tightly with a piece of wood, because the property of wood is that it removes all swelling from the limbs; and if the nodule has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it off and let the excess show; or have it shaved by a barber until it is removed, and cure it until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the weakened limb after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, but the limb remains weak and fragile afterward, it happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was bound too tightly and not properly; another reason is that there were too many bandages, preventing blood flow to the member; or due to excessive swelling; or from too much movement at the wrong time; or because the body has little blood, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you should feed the patient and make the body supple so that blood multiplies within it; and administer baths, and bring joy and pleasure to them; then apply poultices on the limb, such that the poultice draws a lot of blood to it, and often irrigate the area with warm water, until circulation returns to the member; and the member regains its natural appearance.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the crooked limb after being healed
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is crooked after being healed, and the bone is visibly broken, and the shape of the limb is ugly, it does not lose its natural function; do not believe those who say that the limb should be broken again, as many foolish surgeons have done in our land; this practice is to be condemned, causing great harm, and possibly even death; however, if there are knots and tension, then they should be irrigated with warm water or softening herbs like those from the plant viscum album, including roots and melilotus; and make a softening plaster such as a well-made diachylon, take vinca leaves, infuse it in goose fat or oil of sesame, and make a plaster with that; or use figs and pork lard, grind them up with cow dung, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes, the knot (nodation) is removed by continuously and lengthily rubbing with hands wet (moistenous). And let the affected limb be moved/exercised every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisted parts (tortuositez) are swollen and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, then one must cut it down to the bone using a sharp, light incision; and place cotton and bandages during treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is caused by the displacement of a joint from its place, which prevents movement and results in deformity of the limb, causing the patient great pain and injury.[STH: Added missing word "caused" for better readability.]
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation occurs, it must be corrected immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the place will swell, and perhaps it cannot be reset; therefore, it is not at all appropriate to move it when it is swollen: often it brings forth spasms and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient be bled, then leave them until the abscess has subsided; then apply hot water and oil to the limb, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as it comes into place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from head to foot.
des mandibules	of the jaw[ fem. noun, plural form: mandibules ]
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It rarely happens that the jaw becomes dislocated on both sides, and there are two ways in which this dislocation can occur: either they are slightly pulled out of place and become somewhat loose; or they become completely dislocated and hang towards the chin, causing saliva to flow from the mouth that the person cannot hold back, and they cannot close their mouth or enunciate clearly, as their tongue is trapped.  [Note: I made an educated guess for the word "envoloupe" which can mean either "wrapped" or "involved". Given the context, I chose "trapped"]
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a dislocation is small, it can return to its place through several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete, you should quickly reset it and not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a way that the attendant holds the head of the patient, and places the tip of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two-sided; and the other hand should be free to adjust and make it even. Command the patient to relax and move their jaws in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician should make it even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the returning is difficult, even if it is the two jaws together, soak them with hot water and oil, until you easily reset it; do not delay in resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are evenly reset, and the patient's mouth closes well without difficulty, place dampened bandages on it, made of a mixture of rose oil and wax, then lightly bind it with soft ligaments;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on their back, with their head resting between two cushions, so that it is not moved to the right or left, nor should they try to forcefully chew, but eat light food until the pains are gone, and the jaw joints are healed;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then eat what they want lightly, and do not strain to open their mouth while eating or drinking, until the jaw joint is fully healed and healthy.[stop request] Sure! Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be properly reset in an hour and are not returned to their proper position, then fever and swelling may result, and possibly stomach inflammation, and perhaps vomiting of bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a lost cause; and many times those to whom it happens die within 9 days.
de la forcelle	of the fork (or pincher)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The "fork" cannot be dislodged from the side next to the ribs and the bladder, and it is sometimes dislodged out of place, which can be felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the treatment is as follows: have the patient lie down with their back flat on the ground, extend their arms, and then firmly press on the area with your palm, and it will return to its proper position. Then apply a poultice and bandage and bind it.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the head of the shoulder that is dislocated towards the back cannot be moved. If it can, and if it becomes dislodged at any time, then reset it in its proper place as we have said. Then apply a poultice and bandage and bind it, and tell the patient to rest until they are healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And similarly, bring back the shoulder blade when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder can be dislocated in three ways only: of which one is when it dislocates at the side of the scapula below; and the second is at the part of the armpit; and sometimes it dislocates above, but this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And it should not dislocate backwards by the shoulder, nor should it dislocate inside because of nerves; and more often than not, it dislocates downward towards the scapula, especially for those who have little flesh, as it slips out quickly; but for those who have enough flesh, it does not slip out easily, and it goes back in place with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that they receive a shock or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.[Please note that "desaluee" in the provided text is not grammatically correct. It should be "desaloiée", which means "dislocated". I will use the correct form in my translation below.]
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you should try it, until you are certain; and only then should you begin the cure.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And a dislocation is recognized when it is lowered towards the shoulder blade, and there is a noticeable difference between the healthy and sickened shoulder, and you will find clear differences between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find at the top of the shoulder a pit (or depression), and under the shoulder blade when touching the top of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor make any movements.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it clearly when touching.[STH1]: The abbreviation "STH1" was not used in the provided text.
