et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this type of dislocation is not difficult to correct when it is new, or in the case of infants being sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the servant raises the patient's hand up high, then puts your feet under the pelvis, and pulls the joint with force up to the place; and the servant lifts the hand, and stretches it up, then puts it down; it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said many days after, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and give them soothing and relaxing remedies, such as a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let them take it.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then lay the patient down on their back, and place a soft woolen cushion under the pelvis, not too hard or too soft, then put the patient's heel on the cushion and lift the shoulder with strength, and pull the hand of the afflicted person;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and have another servant hold the head of the patient, so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder will come back into place immediately, and if you see that it is dislocated, reset it in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and make sure there is a person present who is bigger than the patient; and let them stand to the patient's side, and push their shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit up high, so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and let another assistant pull the patient's hand down towards their belly. And if the patient is too lightweight, have them hold onto something heavy, and with this, the dislocation should return to its proper position now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And another way to reset it is as follows: take a long stake and drive it into the ground, so that the head of the stake is about the same size as a fist, and neither too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then place it underneath the patient, but make sure they have soft blankets or cloths beneath them, and let the patient be lying lengthwise along the stake. Then stretch out their hand on the other side, and the joint will quickly return to its proper position.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And if it does not want to return due to all the things we have mentioned, perform this cure: take a splinter of 2 arms length and 4 fingers width, which has a pointed end to enter deep underneath the dislocation, in this manner:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then place a soft cloth over the wood so that the wood does not injure the patient, then place it under the dislocation of the patient; and stretch the arm out along the length of the wood, and tie the shoulder to the wood, and the arm at the wrist of the hand, then place the arm on a step of a ladder wide enough, and let the hand hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side; the joint will return in this way.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is back in place, no matter how, you should then place underneath the dislocation a sphere of wool equal [in size], then apply ointment made with powder from the mill, with incense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around, then bind it under the dislocation appropriately, and turn the binding over the ointment, and bring the hand to touch the neck, and let the hand remain in this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eats only liquids until the limb feels better, as it will heal faster; and then eat solid food after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, then it has healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, then you should apply cauteries at three openings, as it is stated in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this, and it becomes dislocated again after seven days, and the joint cannot hold and the arm cannot be raised, then you should know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder have been cut or stretched or weakened; and you should know that the joint will never return to its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	A dislocation that is to the side of the hip, or the breasts, or the back, is caused by impact and extension of the hands, and another joint is used as a replacement; and it should be treated until it has healed.[ original text was "i aministre on autre lieure" which I translated as "and another joint is used as a replacement". Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing there comes cracking in the limb and difficulty moving, then the patient should take many baths until the cracking has subsided and the limb returns to its normal state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the rib(s)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the rib is dislocated at points, and returns to those points; it is dislocated all around, both in front and back, and the dislocation has not been corrected, for it is clearly visible and can be felt; and it is dislocated according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you align the affected rib with the healthy one, it can be clearly seen. For the joint is misaligned and the patient cannot bend their arm or touch their shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it must be set in such a way that abscesses do not develop there, for if abscesses were to form there, setting it would be difficult and perhaps impossible to fully reset, especially when it is dislocated in the back; this type of dislocation is worse than others, and more painful, and may even lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration, when it is of such a nature that it can be reset, is as follows: you stretch out your two hands and hold his arms spread wide, with the doctor's hands placed around the rib both above and below, pressing the joint back into place at its roots or the base of the palm until it returns to its original position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it comes back when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes the root of the palm with the displaced joint.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and this is done by two people extending the arm, and holding it with two people, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side after you have wrapped a long and wide cloth around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when the surgeon has joined the joint to his hand, he anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then strongly pushes the joint until it comes back.[^1](#footnote_inline_1_0)
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in its place, apply dry emplaster with egg white, and bind it firmly, and raise the arm to the patient's neck, and leave it for several days, then loosen it.[^1](#footnote_inline_1_0)
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, loosen the binding and let it be; but if you see that the joint is not tightly bound, reapply the dressing and binding, and leave it for several days until it is firmly set; then loosen it.[^1](#footnote_inline_1_0)
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub him well, and press until he is eased; or put sheep fat on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and make him enter the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then replace the fat, and then enter the bath; and do this twice or thrice, until he is healed; and if you wish, put moist cow dung warmed with butter, and bind it on. Thus will it return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand has become dislocated, and the recovery is quicker than for other joints. Nevertheless, it should be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour that it becomes dislocated, so that the place is swollen, or there comes a hot abscess.

de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers.

dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	The dislocation of the spine of the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the swelling of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death quickly approaches the patient.

des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the hip joints and shoulder joints do not come out of place except for dislocations, and not in the same way as other joints; and the hip joint can become dislocated in four ways: inwardly, outwardly, forward, and backward; and more so inwardly than otherwise, and slightly out of place in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the recognition of an inward dislocation is that when the affected leg is joined with the healthy one, it appears longer, and the affected knee appears more prominent than the healthy one, and the affected patient cannot bend their knee over the fire.[translator's note: it is mentioned that the patient is unable to bend their knee while sitting near a fire as a sign of an inward dislocation]
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and the area next to it is swollen due to abscess, because the head of the thigh bone moves there.[translator's note: The text suggests that the swelling occurs because the head of the femur (thigh bone) has moved towards the area due to dislocation.][IST] Et quant la jambe est desaloiee devant, li cuissiaus vient au leu ou l’os de la hanche reposa por coi il ne se puet muevre, et plus se montre cels que li sains;
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that which is about to happen to him, is that these symptoms are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of that which is about to happen, is that he stretches his leg well according to its full length; nonetheless, he does not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot advance, and he holds his urine, and his ankle swells, and when he walks, he lifts himself up on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of that which has already happened, is that he cannot stretch or bend his knee, and one leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankle is swollen, and the head of the femur is located below the ribcage.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The reduction of this type of dislocation is as follows: observe whether the dislocation is old and persists in its position, then there is no need for treatment and one should not be overconfident.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case of a fresh dislocation, which can be of four types, one should act quickly to return the joint to its place and stretch it both inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return to its place and there is no need for further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not come back in this way, you should prepare for one strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or with a strap tied above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and have another minister extend their hand in such a way that they place their hands beneath the patient's armpits, then bind them with a gentle strap above the thigh; and another holds the head of the strap.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And they extend upwards and downwards all at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground in one motion, and remains hanging.[Additional context: This passage describes a procedure for reducing a dislocated shoulder, involving several assistants to hold the patient in place while resetting the joint.]
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in four cases, and if the dislocation has been reduced as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If not, you should attend to its likeness. When the dislocation is on the side, you should often turn the patient onto their healthy side, then place the strap on the root of the thigh and the joint that is beneath the groin, and then pull the strap upwards toward the groin and toward the armpit;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then take another assistant and hold the patient's arms, hug the patient's hip girdle, and stretch it out very much: it will return to its place now; and this type of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot hold it in place in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary to tie the patient's two feet together with a strong but soft ligament at the heels and knees, and keep the affected leg extended two fingers more than the other.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then have them hang by the head from a beam and be two arms' length off the ground; then command one assistant to hug the head of the thigh and have another assistant hanging with the patient, who will strongly hug the thigh, for the joint will return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is outside, let the patient lie down as we have said in the one with gout, and tie a ligament on the affected leg properly, and also on the foot.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then place two hot irons, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert one hot iron between the thighs of the patient in a horizontal manner;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have cloths soaked in water placed around [the patient], so as not to burn them, then each assistant should extend towards the patient, and the doctor should place his hand evenly on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it [the dislocation] returns to its place, that is good. If not, place a board under it and press as we have said in the section on paralysis, and let the patient lie on their healthy side.[OT: It is unclear what "it" refers to in the first sentence (the dislocation or the limb). I assumed it was the dislocation. If it refers to the limb then the translation would be: "If it [the limb] returns to its place, that is good. If not..." ]
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front [of the body], one must quickly stretch out the affected leg as I have said; and the doctor should take care to be over the bad groin, then press with his other hand and pull downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is on the side, one must not stretch out the patient downwards nor lift them up from the ground, instead they should be in the same position as if their haunch was dislocated to the side, just as we have said about lying on both haunches.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	And let it be above its position, and the bandages extended as we have said before, and one should press on the joint against the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	It will be done when the patient stretches out their legs and they are even; then adjust the thighs, and apply the poultice, and bind it with a bandage so that the swelling does not move;
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And let him rest for three or four days, then loosen it and apply the poultice again; and if you see that they are even, bind it as before, and leave it for three more days; then loosen it and make him walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee becomes dislocated in three ways: namely, inside and outside, and backward; but never in front.[Note: Dislocation of the knee in the front is anatomically impossible]
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you tell the patient to bend his leg at his hip, and if it does not bend at his hip, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	And the restoration of all [dislocations] is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his face, and place his foot on top of your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	Then take his knee with your palms, and pull it towards you between your arms, then bend the two sides of the knee strongly; and have another assistant stretch out his foot until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he can easily bend his leg at his hip.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And apply the poultice and heat the leg against the hip, and bind the limbs together firmly for three or four days, then loosen it; and the patient must not move or walk until the limb is healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limb is not healing, apply strong extension as we have said in the treatment of inflammation, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes dislocated and sometimes completely misaligned, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the sign of this is that the ankle is swollen and tends to bulge towards the side where it is dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The reduction (of the dislocation) is easy and one should gently stretch it with their hands when it is only dislocated.[https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/R%C3%A9duction\_orthop%C3%A9dique](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/R%C3%A9duction_orthop%C3%A9dique)
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated completely, you should make the patient sit upright and have one assistant hold them by the leg, above the ankle.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot toward you with your right hand, and then two times with your left hand, then stretch it upwards, and properly push the foot upward;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this two times, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns to its place, that is good; if not, then begin the task again, for it will return.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return to its place in this way, then have the patient lie down on their back on the ground, and firmly plant a stake in the ground between their thighs, and tie cloth around it so that it does not injure the patient;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then one minister should hold the thigh, and another minister should extend the foot with their hands or using a strap, tying it to the neck of the foot;[ST1] Then one minister should grasp the thigh, and another minister should stretch out the leg with his hands or with a band, which he should tie around the neck of the foot.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then have each minister stretch out evenly, and the stake should still be between the patient's thighs to hold the patient in place when being stretched.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then place the doctor evenly the dislocation in his hands, and another minister holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will come back quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is ready, apply the poultice and bandages firmly, and bind the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the binding is not too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandages loosen, tighten them; then undo the binding on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient to walk for four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes before this time limit, it is not safe that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come, you must calm them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the shoulders
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, they should be stretched out nicely without force, and this is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back or leg, you should make the patient sit on a flat bed or on a table, straight up, and place your foot on the visible joints. Then press firmly with your foot until it returns to its proper position.[STT\_1]
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when it is aligned and there's nothing visible, place a two-legged table under the sole of your foot, then apply strong pressure and leave it for three days before loosening it. Allow the patient to rest until they are healed.[STT\_1]
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	regarding wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with a dislocation, and one wants to reset it, it often happens that the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	And do not be overconfident in treating it if you are not skilled in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful, and slow, not quick.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And at the beginning, use soothing treatments for a hot abscess and leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope for their recovery.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, then reset the limb in its place now, so that the hot abscess comes there.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is in place, then administer soothing treatments for the hot abscess and treat the wound as it should be, with drying ointments.[STHAP: I translated "d'oignemens desiccatis" as "with drying ointments", because "desiccatis" comes from the Latin verb "desiccare" which means to dry out. ]
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if with the dislocation there is a break and small bones disjoined, set the bones, and do what we have said in simple illnesses;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	and take care not to enter the path of fear, as I have said, for it will be harmful to you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your weapons and body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	Here is a possible translation: "Here ends the romance (or tale) of physics."
